Materialism refuted by a scientist's own admission
Buti refutes materialism via a biologist's admission on life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the admission of a materialist scientist undermines the philosophical basis of dialectical materialism.

Core Idea
A materialist scientist's own words prove materialism false.

In this passage, Shaykh Ramadan al-Buti presents a powerful argument against dialectical materialism by quoting a leading Russian biochemist. After decades of research, Alexander Oparin admitted that life cannot arise from chemical reactions alone. Buti uses this to show that materialism's claims about life's origin are scientifically unfounded, even by its own proponents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the tone and the key claims made by Buti.
Pay attention to the quote from Oparin and its significance.
2
Identify Oparin's admission
Find the exact words of Alexander Oparin regarding the origin of life. Note his conclusion after 37 years of research.
Oparin stated that life cannot start from nothing or from chemical reactions.
3
Understand Buti's argument
Buti argues that this admission from a leading materialist exposes the illusion of dialectical materialism. He emphasizes that it is not Muslims but the materialists themselves who provide the refutation.
The phrase 'شهد شاهد من أهلها' (a witness from its own people) is key.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider what this means for the materialist worldview. If science cannot explain life's origin, then materialism's claims are based on blind faith, not evidence.
Buti mentions that materialist tenets rely on the 'tendentious factor' (العامل الذرائعي) rather than scientific proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمر الحياة لا يزال مجهولاً ، ولا مطمع في أن يصل إليه العلم يوماً ما . وكان أول من صدق على هذا ذلك العالم الروسي نفسه . ومجمل القول - كما يقول الدكتور أنور عبد العليم - أن العلم لم يتوصل بعد إلى كشف هذا السر الأعظم المعروف بالحياة ، كما يتضح أن هذه المشكلة مدى من أن تكون مجرد بناء مواد عضوية معينة وظواهر طبيعية وكيميائية خاصة (۱) وتقتضي الحكمة الإلهية العظيمة أن تزداد هذه الحقيقة تـأكـداً ووضوحاً على لسان العالم الروسي بالذات ؛ ففي العام المذكور : ۱۹۵۹ تناقلت وكالات الأنباء وفي مقدمتها وكالة الأنباء السوفييتية ( تاس ) ما يلي أعلن ألكسندر أوبارين ، رئيس معهد الكيمياء الحيوية في روسيا بعد أن ظل يبحث ٣٧ عاماً في أصل الحياة وفي البحث عما إذا كان من الممكن إيجاد الخلية الأولى عن طريق تفاعل كيميائي ، أن الحياة لا يمكن أن تبدأ من العدم أو أن تتوالد من التفاعل الكيميائي والتوالد الذاتي ، وأن العلم لا يمكن أن يخوض فيما وراء حدود المادة فأي معنى يبقى بعد هذا الكلام والذي قبله ، للفلسفة المادية التي تخيلها ماركس ذات يوم من الأيام بدافع انفعالي معين ؟ .. وها أنت ترى أننا لسنا نحن الذين نزيح عنها لثامها الفلسفي الوهمي الذي يختبئ خلفه قدر كبير من الجهل والوهم ، ولكن الذي يفعل ذلك إنما هو أهل الدار نفسها ، فقد شهد شاهد من أهلها . وكفى الله المؤمنين القتال . أما تفصيلات هذه الفلسفة ، والنظر في مقولاتها وقوانينها ، فلسنا الآن في معرض مناقشتها أو نقضها . وهي على كل حال مقولات لا تستند إلى شيء من البراهين العلمية ، وإنما تستمد سندها الوحيد من العامل الذرائعي .. وبوسعك أن تقرأ تفاصيل ذلك كله في كتابنا « نقض أوهام المادية الجدلية »
The matter of life still remains unknown, and there is no hope that science will ever reach it. The first to affirm this was that same Russian scientist. And the summary of the statement—as Dr. Anwar Abd al-Aleem says—is that science has not yet succeeded in uncovering this greatest secret known as life, and it is evident that this problem is far from being merely a construction of certain organic substances and specific natural and chemical phenomena (1). And the great divine wisdom requires that this fact become more confirmed and clear on the tongue of that Russian scientist in particular; for in the aforementioned year: 1959, news agencies, led by the Soviet news agency (TASS), reported the following: Alexander Oparin, head of the Institute of Biochemistry in Russia, announced after having researched for 37 years on the origin of life and on whether it was possible to create the first cell through a chemical reaction, that life cannot begin from nothing nor be generated from chemical reaction and spontaneous generation, and that science cannot delve beyond the limits of matter. So what meaning remains after this speech and that which preceded it for the materialist philosophy that Marx imagined one day out of a certain emotional motive? And you see that we are not the ones who remove its illusory philosophical veil behind which lies a great deal of ignorance and illusion, but rather the one who does that is the very people of the house itself, for a witness from its own people has testified. And Allah sufficed the believers from fighting. As for the details of this philosophy and the examination of its tenets and laws, we are not now in a position to discuss or refute them. They are, in any case, tenets that are not based on any scientific proofs, but rather derive their sole support from the tendentious factor. And you can read the details of all that in our book: 'Refuting the Illusions of Dialectical Materialism.'
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of materialist philosophy, specifically dialectical materialism, regarding the origin of life. The author begins by stating that the mystery of life remains unknown and science has no hope of uncovering it. He then cites a Russian scientist (Alexander Oparin) who, after 37 years of research, admitted that life cannot arise from non-life or chemical reactions, and that science cannot go beyond matter. The author argues that this admission from a leading materialist scientist himself destroys the credibility of Marx's materialist philosophy. He emphasizes that it is not Muslims who expose the illusion of materialism, but the materialists themselves have provided the testimony. The author concludes by stating that the details of this refutation can be found in another book of his, and that materialist claims are not based on scientific proof but on tendentious motives.

Key Terms
الفلسفة المادية
الحياة
العلم
الحكمة الإلهية
البراهين العلمية
العامل الذرائعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume that scientific progress will eventually explain the origin of life through natural processes.
Correction: This passage shows that a leading materialist scientist, after decades of research, admitted that life cannot arise from non-life or chemical reactions, suggesting that the origin of life is a mystery beyond material explanation.

Checkpoint
What did Alexander Oparin conclude after 37 years of research on the origin of life?
A) Life can be created through chemical reactions.
B) Life cannot begin from nothing nor be generated from chemical reactions.
C) Science will eventually discover the origin of life.
D) The first cell can be synthesized in the laboratory.

Key Takeaway
The origin of life remains a mystery beyond scientific explanation, even by materialist scientists, refuting dialectical materialism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of your closely held beliefs might be based more on emotional motives (like Marx, as Buti suggests) than on solid evidence? Are you willing to re-examine them today?
?
Oparin spent 37 years trying to prove a falsehood. What part of your life have you spent pursuing something that deep down you know is untrue? Will you have the courage to stop?
?
Buti says the testimony against materialism came from its own people. Is there an area where you have ignored a witness from your own 'camp' because it challenged your worldview? Will you listen today and let the truth change you?

Definition and Claims of Historical Materialism
Buti defines historical materialism and its dialectical development before critiquing it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core claims of historical materialism as presented by Buti, including its rejection of absolute truth and its dialectical view of societal development.

Core Idea
Historical materialism reduces all human reality to economic production and denies absolute truth.

In this passage, Buti turns to the second branch of Marxist philosophy: historical materialism. He explains its fundamental claim that the entire structure of society – values, ideas, language, knowledge – originates from the economic situation, which itself is determined by the means of production. Understanding this worldview is essential before examining Buti's critique.

Guided Path
1
Read and translate the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then read the full English translation. Note how Buti defines historical materialism and outlines its key components.
Pay attention to terms like 'وسيلة الإنتاج' (means of production) and 'النسبية المتطورة' (developed relativity).
2
Identify the three main claims
The passage presents three interconnected claims: (1) all societal elements arise from the means of production, (2) there is no absolute truth, only relative truth based on economic conditions, and (3) society develops dialectically through internal contradictions.
These claims are the foundation of historical materialism.
3
Understand the dialectical process
Buti explains that development happens through internal contradictions (e.g., capital accumulation leads to revolution). Trace how the flourishing of means of production leads to class struggle and eventually communism.
This process is central to Marxist theory.
4
Preview the critique
Notice that Buti ends by stating he will weigh these ideas using the 'balance of talazum' (correlation). This sets up his refutation in the next part.
Talazum is a method Buti explained earlier in his methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نناقش الفرع الثاني من فروع هذه الفلسفة وهي ( المادية التاريخية ) فنقول : إن المقصود بهذا العنوان دعوى أن تركيب المجتمع الإنساني بما فيه القيم المختلفة والأفكار واللغة والمعارف ، كل ذلك ناشئ عن الوضع الاقتصادي الذي نشأ هو بدوره عن سبب الأسباب كلها ، ألا وهو « وسيلة الإنتاج » وعلى هذا فإن الحقيقة المطلقة » لا مكان لها في الوجود كله ، وإنما يمتد في مكانها وعلى اتساع الوجود كله قانون « النسبية المتطورة » في كل شيء ، إذ المعرفة ذاتها وليد ظروفها الاقتصادية ، فمن أين تأتي الحقيقة المطلقة ؟ ثم يزعمون أن تركيب المجتمع الإنساني يتطور تحت سلطان الوضع الاقتصادي ووسيلة الإنتاج ، تطوراً ديالكتيكياً ، أي بعـوامـل من داخـلـه تحمـل بـذور نقیضه ، وليس بواسطة عوامل من خارجه كما هو شأن العلة مع المعلول . فازدهار وسيلة الإنتاج يسبب تضخم رأس المال وهذا الوضع نفسه يحمل في طوايـاه بـذور الثورة عليه إذ يتسبب عنه انتقال وسائل الإنتاج إلى طبقة البروليتاريا ، ويستمر هذا التناقض بين وسائل الإنتاج وعلاقات الملكية عاملاً وحيداً للصراع داخل المجتمع . ويظل هذا الصراع مستمراً حتى تنمحي الطبقية من المجتمع إلى الأبد ويدخل العالم في مرحلة الشيوعية العظمى ، وعندئذ يهدأ الصراع وتسكن العاصفة وينتهي كل شيء . ونحن نقوم هذه الأفكار بميزان « التلازم » الذي أوضحناه في منهج البحث فنقول : --
Then we discuss the second branch of the branches of this philosophy, which is (historical materialism), and we say: What is meant by this title is the claim that the structure of human society, including its various values, ideas, language, and knowledge, all of that arises from the economic situation, which itself arises from the cause of all causes, namely the 'means of production.' And on this basis, 'absolute truth' has no place in all existence, but rather extending in its place and across the whole expanse of existence is the law of 'developed relativity' in everything, for knowledge itself is the offspring of its economic circumstances, so from where would absolute truth come? Then they claim that the structure of human society evolves under the authority of the economic situation and the means of production, a dialectical evolution, i.e., by factors from within it that carry the seeds of its opposite, not by factors from outside it as is the case of cause with effect. So the flourishing of the means of production causes the expansion of capital, and this very situation carries within it the seeds of revolution against it, as it causes the transfer of the means of production to the proletariat class. And this contradiction between the means of production and relations of ownership continues as the sole factor of conflict within society. And this conflict continues until class distinction is erased from society forever, and the world enters the stage of great communism, and then the conflict calms, the storm subsides, and everything ends. And we weigh these ideas with the balance of 'talazum' (correlation) which we explained in our research methodology, so we say: --
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the claims of historical materialism, the second branch of Marxist philosophy. The author begins by stating what is meant by the term: that all human societal components (values, ideas, language, knowledge) arise from the economic situation, which itself is determined by the means of production. Therefore, there is no absolute truth; only relative truth exists, since knowledge is a product of economic conditions. The author then explains how dialectical development occurs: internal contradictions within the means of production drive societal change, not external causes. For example, the flourishing of the means of production leads to capital accumulation, which inevitably produces the seeds of revolution, transferring means of production to the proletariat. This class struggle continues until class vanishes and communism is achieved. The author concludes by stating that he will evaluate these ideas using the method of "talazum" (correlation) previously explained in his methodology, introducing his upcoming refutation.

Key Terms
المادية التاريخية
وسيلة الإنتاج
النسبية المتطورة
تطوراً ديالكتيكياً
البروليتاريا
الشيوعية العظمى
التلازم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Historical materialism is a scientific, objective theory of history that does not rely on metaphysical assumptions.
Correction: Buti shows that historical materialism itself makes metaphysical claims (e.g., the means of production as the 'cause of all causes') and denies absolute truth, which is a philosophical stance, not a scientific one.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does historical materialism claim about absolute truth?
A) Absolute truth exists but is unknowable.
B) Absolute truth has no place in existence; only relative truth exists.
C) Absolute truth is revealed through dialectical progress.
D) Absolute truth is found in the means of production.

Key Takeaway
Historical materialism reduces all of human reality to economic factors and denies absolute truth, claiming society evolves dialectically toward communism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If historical materialism claims that your belief in absolute truth is merely a product of economic conditions, does that shake your certainty? On what basis do you personally stand firm against such a claim?
?
This passage states that knowledge itself is a child of economic circumstances. If that were true, would you trust your own reasoning? What does this reveal about the necessity of a foundation beyond material conditions?
?
Historical materialism promises a final classless society where conflict ends. But who decides what is just? Without absolute truth, can justice exist? Examine your own heart: do you seek truth that is beyond temporary circumstances, or do you settle for relative comforts?

The Contradiction in Dialectical Law and Absolute Communism
Buti exposes the contradiction in claiming that dialectical law stops with absolute communism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Buti exposes an internal contradiction in the Marxist claim that dialectical law governs history but ceases with the establishment of absolute communism.

Core Idea
If dialectics is universal, communism cannot be its endpoint.

In this passage, Buti presents a logical dilemma that challenges the consistency of Marxist theory. He shows that the claim of dialectical law's universal application is incompatible with the assertion that absolute communism marks the end of all development. By drawing out the necessary implications, he forces the reader to choose between two contradictory positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the clear logical structure: implication, claim, contradiction, dilemma.
2
Identify the dilemma
Buti presents two mutually exclusive possibilities. Identify the two horns of the dilemma and understand how each one undermines the Marxist claim.
The dilemma is a classic tool of refutation in Islamic theology.
3
Reflect on the contradiction
Consider why the Marxist position cannot be consistently maintained. Ask yourself: which horn of the dilemma would a Marxist have to accept?
This exercises your ability to spot logical inconsistencies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن مقتضى سيطرة قانون الدياليكتيك، أن يظل تركيب المجتمع الإنساني في تطور وتناقض، وهذا يعني أن قيام الشيوعية المطلقة شأنه من الآخر أن يحمل في داخله بذور نقيضه، باعتباره طوراً من الأطوار الإنسانية التي تدور حول الفلك الاقتصادي. ولكنهم يزعمون بأن حركة التطور تقف وقوفاً تاماً عند انبثاق الشيوعية المطلقة. وهذا يناقض دعواهم الأولى مناقضة واضحة صارخة. أحد شيئين: إما أن نظام الدياليكتيك هو المسيطر حقاً على سير العالم، وإذا فليس صحيحاً أن شعلة التطور ستنطفئ عند قيام الشيوعية المطلقة. وإما أن الصحيح هو الثاني، وأن زوال الطبقية ينهي كل تطور ويقضي على كل صراع، وإذاً فليس صحيحاً ما يقولونه من سيطرة الدياليكتيك على حركة العالم.
The requirement of the dominance of the law of dialectics is that the structure of human society remain in development and contradiction, and this means that the establishment of absolute communism by its very nature carries within it the seeds of its opposite, as it is a stage of the human stages that revolve around the economic orbit. But they claim that the movement of development stops completely at the emergence of absolute communism. This contradicts their first claim in a clear and blatant contradiction. One of two things: either the dialectical system truly dominates the course of the world, and if so, it is not correct that the torch of development will be extinguished with the establishment of absolute communism; or the second is correct, and the abolition of class ends all development and eliminates all conflict, and if so, what they say about the dominance of dialectics over the movement of the world is not correct.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a logical refutation of the Marxist claim that dialectical law governs history but ends with absolute communism. The author states the necessary implication of dialectical law: society remains in a state of development and contradiction, so every stage contains the seeds of its opposite. Therefore, absolute communism, as a stage, should also contain its own negation and eventually be superseded. However, Marxists claim that development stops at absolute communism. The author presents a dilemma: either dialectical law is supreme, then development cannot stop at communism; or development stops at communism, then dialectical law is not truly dominant. The contradiction is clear, and the Marxist position is shown to be inconsistent.

Key Terms
الدياليكتيك
الشيوعية المطلقة
التطور
التناقض
الطبقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author accepts dialectical law as true and only points out an internal inconsistency.
Correction: Buti is not endorsing dialectics; he is using its own logic to show the Marxist claim is self-contradictory. The refutation works regardless of whether dialectics is true.

Checkpoint
What dilemma does Buti present to the Marxist claim about dialectics and communism?
A) Either dialectics is false or communism is eternal
B) Either dialectics dominates or it does not, but both lead to contradiction
C) Either communism will not last or dialectics is not universal
D) Either development continues or dialectics is not the moving force

Key Takeaway
Buti exposes a self-contradiction in Marxist theory: if dialectical law is universal, absolute communism cannot be the final stage; if communism is final, dialectical law is not universal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you identify a belief or worldview you once held that, like Marxism, contained an internal contradiction you ignored for convenience? How did you eventually resolve it?
?
If you were to apply Buti's logical scrutiny to your own life, what area of inconsistency would be exposed first? Are you willing to examine it now?
?
When you claim a universal principle (like justice, honesty, or faith), do you ever make convenient exceptions for yourself? What would it cost you to be consistent?

Self-Refutation of Materialist Relativism
Buti argues that denying absolute truths contradicts the claim that dialectical materialism is itself an absolute truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the self-referential contradiction in the materialist claim that all truths are relative.

Core Idea
Denying absolute truths is self-defeating if you claim your own theory is absolutely true.

Buti exposes a powerful logical flaw in historical materialism. If everything is relative, then the claim that everything is relative cannot itself be absolute. This lesson walks through that argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let Buti's argument unfold naturally.
Notice the two-part structure: presentation of the materialist view, then its refutation.
2
Identify the materialist claims
The passage states that dialectics holds reason to be a product of economic struggle, and that absolute truths are relative. Note these claims.
Materialism reduces truth to economic conditions.
3
Spot the self-contradiction
Buti points out that if the materialist claim is true, then dialectics itself is not a fixed law but just another relative notion. This is a contradiction.
The theory presents itself as an absolute truth while denying absolute truths.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes that thought (not material factors) drives social development. Consider how this follows from the refutation.
Buti uses reason to defend reason as a source of absolute truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن فرضية الدياليكتيك تستلزم القول بأن العقل وما يتبعه من النشاطات الفكرية ليس إلا ثمرة لصراع الإنسان من أجل رفع مستواه الاقتصادي، وتطوير وسائل الإنتاج، ومن ثم فإن الحقائق المطلقة أمور نسبية لا وجود لها في ظل المادية التاريخية، وهي ليست أكثر من ظلال لمقتضيات زمنية متطورة. فإذا فرضنا أن هذا الكلام صحيح، فإنه لدليل بدهي على أن الدياليكتيك ليس قانوناً حقيقياً يستوعب التاريخ كله ويغطي أطوار الإنسانية كلها، بل هو ليس إلا كبقية «الحقائق» المزعومة الأخرى، أمر نسبي لا حقيقة ثابتة له. إن من التناقض الذي لا يخفى على عاقل، أن نقول بأن أحكام العقل ليست حقائق مطلقة ثابتة، ثم نعتمد على أحكام العقل ذاته في استنباط ما ندعي أنه أعظم حقيقة ثابتة تستوعب التاريخ الإنساني كله. والخلاصة، أننا نطرح هذا السؤال: ما هو علة التطور الاجتماعي؟ والجواب الواضح على لسان كل باحث: إنه الفكر.
The hypothesis of dialectics entails the statement that reason and its consequent intellectual activities are nothing but the fruit of man's struggle to raise his economic level and develop the means of production, and therefore absolute truths are relative matters that have no existence in the shadow of historical materialism, and they are nothing but shadows of evolving temporal necessities. If we suppose that this statement is true, then it is a clear proof that dialectics is not a real law that encompasses all of history and covers all stages of humanity, but rather it is like the other alleged 'truths,' a relative matter with no fixed reality. It is a contradiction not hidden from a rational person that we say that the judgments of reason are not absolute fixed truths, and then we rely on the judgments of reason itself to deduce what we claim is the greatest fixed truth that encompasses all of human history. In conclusion, we pose this question: What is the cause of social development? And the clear answer from every researcher: it is thought.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the materialist doctrine of historical materialism by exposing a self-referential contradiction. The author explains that dialectical materialism claims that reason is merely a product of economic struggle and that absolute truths do not exist; all truths are relative. But then he points out that this very claim is presented as an absolute, all-encompassing truth about history. If the claim is true, then dialectical materialism itself is not a real, fixed law but just another relative notion. It is self-contradictory to deny absolute truths while relying on reason to assert a grand absolute truth. The author concludes by stating that the true cause of social development is not material factors but thought (الفكر).

Key Terms
الدياليكتيك
المادية التاريخية
الحقائق المطلقة
العقل
النسبية
الفكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that historical materialism's denial of absolute truths is logically consistent.
Correction: Buti shows that the denial is self-refuting because the theory itself claims to be an absolute truth about history.

Checkpoint
What is the self-contradiction Buti points out in historical materialism?
A) It claims truth is relative but asserts itself as absolute
B) It relies on economic factors while ignoring psychology
C) It uses dialectical method to prove its own inconsistency
D) It denies reason but uses reason to argue

Key Takeaway
The materialist denial of absolute truth is self-refuting because it asserts its own absolute truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim that all truths are relative, but what about that very claim? Is it absolutely true? If you say it is, you contradict yourself. If you say it is not, then why should anyone accept it? How does this affect your own certainty?
?
When you dismiss moral absolutes as cultural constructs, do you realize you are making an absolute claim about morality? What does that tell you about your own need for absolute truth?
?
You rely on reason to argue against absolute truths. But if reason is just a product of your economic circumstances, why should anyone trust your argument? How does this expose the inconsistency in your position?

Refuting the Materialist Explanation of Thought
Buti refutes materialism's economic determinism and concludes thought is an independent gift from God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the materialist explanation of thought fails to account for the human-animal divide, and how Buti concludes that thought is an independent reality bestowed by the Creator.

Core Idea
Material conditions alone cannot explain thought; the human-animal gap proves its divine origin.

Buti challenges the materialist claim that thought arises from economic needs and means of production. Using a simple but powerful analogy, he asks: if material conditions were the cause, why did animals not develop thought, language, or economy? His conclusion points to a higher, independent source: the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Understand materialism's claim
Read Buti's presentation of the materialist view: thought originates from economic factors like the need for food and drink.
Materialism reduces thought to a byproduct of material survival.
2
Follow Buti's objection
Notice the critical question: animals shared the same conditions, so why did they not develop thought? This exposes a flaw in materialism.
The objection is based on a comparison between humans and animals under the same material circumstances.
3
Grasp the conclusion
Buti concludes that thought is an independent reality that came from the Creator, not from matter.
This conclusion directly refutes materialism by invoking a transcendent cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بد أن نسأل عامل انبعاث الفكر ؟ .. وتجيب المادية ذلك فها بعد هو التاريخية على هذا السؤال الثاني بكل بساطة : إنه العامل الاقتصادي المتمثل في وسائل الإنتاج ، فالشعور بالحاجة إلى الطعام والشراب هو الذي حرك البذور الأولى للفكر والعقل ، وهو الذي فجّر أيضاً طاقة اللسان وقدرة التعبير . ولا بد أن يسأل كل عاقل في الدنيا : فلماذا تخلفت البهائم والسباع المختلفة ، عن زميلها « الإنسان » في هذه المرحلة التي تكافأت فيها الفرص، وأظلها نظام قانون واحد ؟ ولماذا استطاعت سياط الدياليكتيك أن تدفع بالإنسان إلى حيث وصل الآن ، دون أن تستطيع هذه السياط نفسها تحريك سائر الحيوانات الأخرى شبراً واحداً إلى الأمام ؟ فلا هي تمتعت بفكر ولا اغتنت بلغة ولا ازدهر فيها اقتصاد ! إن الجواب الذي لا مفر منه بحال من الأحوال ، هو أن الفكر حقيقة مستقلة تنزلت إلى الإنسان من لدن خالق الإنسان (۱) (۱) إذا أردت أن تقف على خرافة الفكر المادي بتفصيل ، فارجع إلى كتاب نقض أوهام المادية الجدلية لمؤلف هذا الكتاب
We must ask: what is the factor that triggers thought? Materialism answers this second question simply: it is the economic factor represented in the means of production. The feeling of need for food and drink is what moved the first seeds of thought and intellect, and it also unleashed the energy of the tongue and the ability to express. And every rational person in the world must ask: why did the various beasts and predators fall behind their counterpart 'man' in this stage when opportunities were equal and a single system of law overshadowed them? And why were the whips of dialectics able to drive man to where he has now reached, while these same whips could not move the rest of the animals even an inch forward? They neither enjoyed thought, nor enriched themselves with language, nor did an economy flourish among them! The answer from which there is no escape whatsoever is that thought is an independent reality that descended to man from the Creator of man. (1) (1) If you wish to know the myth of materialist thought in detail, refer to the book 'Refuting the Illusions of Dialectical Materialism' by the author of this book.

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the materialist claim that thought originates from economic factors, specifically the means of production and the need for food and drink. The author presents a logical objection: if the same material conditions existed for both humans and animals, why did animals not develop thought, language, or economy? The conclusion is that thought is an independent reality bestowed by the Creator, not a product of material forces. A footnote directs to a more detailed refutation.

The Prophet's Non-Involvement in the Quran and Adherence to Truth
Buti asserts the Prophet's non-involvement in the Quran and calls for rational truth-seeking.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet Muhammad had no role in composing the Quran and that the proper attitude is to adhere to truth purely for its own sake, guided by reason.

Core Idea
The Quran is entirely from Allah; the Prophet had no part in a single letter.

This passage concludes a discussion on the divine origin of the Quran. The author firmly states that the Prophet Muhammad played no role in its composition—every letter is from Allah. He then reflects on the futility of hatred and bigotry, and urges reliance on reason alone to recognize and cling to truth for its own sake.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm and emphasis come through.
Notice how the passage shifts from a factual assertion to a reflective prayer.
2
Identify the core assertion
The passage begins with 'Because of this, Muhammad has no part in a single letter of it.' Identify why this is significant for the Quran's divine origin.
This directly refutes any claim that the Prophet authored the Quran.
3
Understand the author's attitude toward opposition
Buti acknowledges that despite clarity, some people hate and oppose due to bigotry. He admits he cannot cure them with arguments but turns to prayer.
This shows humility and reliance on Allah.
4
Reflect on the call to reason and truth
The author prays for freedom from all authority except reason, and to know and adhere to truth simply because it is truth. Ask yourself: What does this imply about how we should approach faith?
This is a call for intellectual sincerity and objectivity.

بسبب هذه لا دخل لمحمد صلى الله عليه وسلم في حرف واحد منه، من الآية التي نزلت. وبوسع أي عاقل أن يبصر هذا الذي أراه ولكن لاحيلة لنا، كما قلت الحادثة لك، في أن نعالج بشيء من هذه الحقائق حقد الحاقدين، أو عصبية المتعصبين، أو غيظ المغتاظين. ونشهد أن لا قبل لنا بشيء من ذلك إلا أننا نسأل الله تعالى لأنفسنا ولجميع الناس التوفيق إلى التحرر من كل سلطان إلا سلطان العقل وحده، وإلى معرفة أن قطار العمر الذي يغذ السير بنا مسرعاً إلى الموت لا يغنيه شيئاً عن الموت أو عما وراء الموت أن نحقد ونتعصب ونسوق الفكر تحت سياطهما إلى ما يشاءه سلطانها، ولكن الذي يغنيه في ذلك أن نعرف الحق الذي هو الحق، ثم نتمسك به لا لشيء إلا لأنه الحق.
Because of this, Muhammad (peace be upon him) has no part in a single letter of it, from the verse that was revealed. And any intelligent person can see what I am seeing, but we have no way, as I said to you about the incident, to treat with any of these truths the hatred of the haters, or the bigotry of the bigots, or the rage of the enraged. And we testify that we have no power over any of that except that we ask Allah Almighty for ourselves and for all people for success to be free from every authority except the authority of reason alone, and to know that the train of life that speeds us rapidly towards death is not benefited by hating and being fanatical and driving thought under their whips to whatever their authority wishes, but what benefits us in that is to know the truth that is the truth, then adhere to it for no reason except that it is the truth.

Commentary
This passage is a concluding reflection from the author. He asserts that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) had no part in composing the Quran; every letter is from Allah. He then notes that despite the clarity of this truth, there are those who hate and oppose due to bigotry. The author admits the difficulty of curing such hatred with rational arguments. He concludes by praying for all people to free themselves from all authority except the authority of reason, and to recognize the fleeting nature of life, and to adhere to the truth simply because it is truth. The passage emphasizes the divine origin of the Quran and the proper attitude of a believer: relying on reason and seeking truth without prejudice.

British Strategy: Targeting Al-Azhar
Buti lays out British colonial strategy to reform Al-Azhar, citing Lord Lloyd's memoirs as evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how British colonialism strategically targeted Al-Azhar University to weaken Islamic adherence, and the historical evidence Buti provides from Lord Lloyd's memoirs.

Core Idea
Colonial powers deliberately reformed Al-Azhar to sever Muslim religious fervor.

In this passage, Buti unveils the colonial blueprint behind the 'reform' of Al-Azhar. He explains that Britain, realizing Al-Azhar's immense influence over Egypt and the Islamic world, made it the primary target for intellectual subversion. Buti also cites an explicit admission from Lord Lloyd, the British High Commissioner, to prove that this was a calculated strategy to weaken Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing to analyse every word. Then read the English translation to grasp the flow of Buti's argument.
Pay attention to the shift from general strategy to specific quote.
2
Identify Britain's motive
Buti says Britain wanted to change Muslim thinking to distance them from intense religious adherence. Mark the phrases that describe this goal.
3
Understand why Al-Azhar was targeted
Notice Buti's explanation of Al-Azhar's leadership role. Understand why reform had to start there.
4
Analyze the Lord Lloyd quote
Read the quoted passage carefully. What does Lord Lloyd say about Al-Azhar? What solution does he propose if reform is not possible?
This is direct evidence of colonial intent.
5
Reflect on Buti's methodology
Buti contrasts his method with Western historiographical methods. What does he claim to follow instead? Think about why he inserts this remark.

فرأت - كما هو شأنها دائماً ـ أن لا بد من الاستعانة بمنهج فكري يغير من تفكير المسلمين تغييراً يقصيهم عن هذه الشدة في التمسك بالدين والتضحية من أجله والاعتماد عليه وحده . ويجعلهم يلتقون مع الفكر الأوربي في أوسع قدر ممكن من سبل الحياة . وقامت بريطانيا بهذا الدافع ، بتطبيق ما أطلقت عليه اسم الإصلاح الاجتماعي والديني : وكان الميدان الأول لهذا ( الإصلاح ) هو الجامع الأزهر المتمثل في مناهجه الدرسية وطريقته الفكرية . ذلك أن قيادة القطر المصري كله كانت إذ ذاك بید الأزهر ، وكان إشعاعه يتجاوزه إلى كثير من البقاع الإسلامية الأخرى ، فلم تكن هناك من قضية وطنية أو دينية أو مشكلة فكرية أو اجتماعية إلا والأزهر هو الرأس المدبر والمفكر فيها وهو المحرك لها ، لذلك فلم يكن لينجح أي ) إصلاح ( ديني أو فكري من وجهة نظر بريطانيا إلا إذا بدأ بالأزهر . وينبغي أن نذكرك هنا بأننا لا نتبع فيا نرويه من أحداث ووقائع تاريخية ، منهج الاسترداد أو التوسم الذي يتعلق به دون غيره منهجيـو الغرب خصوصاً بالنسبة لتاريخنا وإسلامنا ، ولكننا نتبع المنهج العلمي السليم الذي أوضحناه والتزمناه . ولعلك تتساءل ، فمن أين علمنا أن بريطانيا وضعت لنفسها هذا المخطط ، وضاقت ذرعاً بالإسلام وبأزهره ؟! فاسمع ما يقوله في ذلك اللورد لويد ، المندوب السامي لمصر إذ ذاك ، في مذكراته التي سماها ( Egypt Since Cromer : مصر منذ أيام كرومر ) . يقول : ( إن التعليم الوطني عندما قدم الإنكليز ، كان في قبضة الجامعة الأزهرية الشديدة التمسك بالدين والتي كانت أساليبها الجافة تقف حاجزاً في طريق أي إصلاح تعليمي ، وكان الطلبة الذين يتخرجون من هذه الجامعة قدراً عظيماً من غرور التعصب الديني ، ( تنبـه جـيـداً إلى معنى يحملون معهم الكلام ) فلو أمكن تطوير الأزهر لكانت خطوة جلية الخطر . فليس من اليسير أن نتصور لنا أي تقدم طالما ظل الأزهر متمسكاً بأساليبه هذه ولكن إذا بدا أن مثل هذه الخطوة غير متيسر تحقيقها فحينئذ يصبح الأمل محصوراً في إيجاد التعليم الذي ينافس الأزهر حتى يتاح له الانتشار والنجاح ) . أما مجال هذا التطوير و ( الإصلاح ( فلقد اعتمد على نقطة الضعف التي كانت الأمة العربية والإسلامية تستشعرها إذ ذاك حيال النهضة العلمية في أوربا والاكتشافات والاختراعات المختلفة التي قامت في أنحائها بفضل الانطلاقة العلمية التي لم تكن من قبل . لقد كان المخطط ( الإصلاحي ( إذاً ، هو تنبيه قادة الفكر العربي والإسلامي إلى أن وجود مثل هذه النهضة في العالم الإسلامي متوقف على تطوير الطريقة التي يتم بها فهم الدين والعقيدة الإسلامية ، بشكل يتفق مع الفكر العلمي المقبول ، وهذا يعني ضرورة تخليص الفكر الديني من كل حقيقة غيبية غير مفهومة أو داخلة في قوالب العلم الحديث وسرعان ما استجاب إلى هذه الدعوة ، أولئك المفتونون والمأخوذون بالنهضة العلمية الأوربية الحديثة والحضارة الغربية عامة ، ممن لم يرسخ الإيمان في أفئدتهم ولم تتمكن حقائقه في عقولهم ، وأخذوا يستيقنون - بدافع ذلك الافتتـان الجـديـد والضعف الإيماني السابق عليه - أن الوسيلة الوحيدة إلى نهضة شبيهة بالنهضة الأوربية ، إنما هي في التحرر من كثير من المبادئ الدينية المتعلقة بالعقيدة . ولم يكن على بريطانيا - وقد امتص إيحاؤها عدداً لا بأس به من المفكر بن العرب المسلمين ، أن تتعب نفسها كثيراً بمتابعة المخطط ، فقد اطمأنت إلى أن هؤلاء أنفسهم سيقومون بالعمل المطلوب. وما عليها إلا أن تقربهم وتسلمهم قيادة العمل الفكري في الأزهر ليوطدوا مناهجه ، وليبثوا منه إلى الفكر الإسلامي كلـه هـذا الوباء ( الإصلاحي الجديد ) .
It saw—as is its usual way—that there was no alternative but to employ an intellectual method that would change the thinking of Muslims in a way that distanced them from this intensity in clinging to religion, sacrificing for it, and relying on it alone, and would make them meet European thought in the widest possible scope of life. Britain, driven by this motive, applied what it called social and religious reform: and the first field for this 'reform' was Al-Azhar University, represented in its curricula and intellectual method. That is because the leadership of all Egypt was then in the hand of Al-Azhar, and its influence extended beyond it to many other Islamic lands. There was no national or religious issue, nor any intellectual or social problem, except that Al-Azhar was the directing and thinking head and the mover of it. Therefore, from Britain's point of view, no religious or intellectual 'reform' would succeed unless it began with Al-Azhar. And we should remind you here that in what we narrate of historical events and facts, we do not follow the method of retrieval or conjecture that Western methodologists, especially regarding our history and Islam, adhere to exclusively, but we follow the sound scientific method which we have clarified and adhered to. Perhaps you ask: how did we know that Britain set this plan for itself and became intolerant of Islam and its Al-Azhar? So hear what Lord Lloyd, the High Commissioner for Egypt at that time, says in his memoirs which he called 'Egypt Since Cromer'. He says: 'When the English came, national education was in the grasp of Al-Azhar University, which was strongly attached to religion and whose dry methods stood as an obstacle to any educational reform; and the students who graduated from this university carried a great amount of the arrogance of religious fanaticism (pay close attention to the meaning of what they carry with them). If it were possible to develop Al-Azhar, it would be a step of clear danger. It is not easy for us to imagine any progress as long as Al-Azhar remains clinging to these methods. But if it appears that such a step is not feasible, then hope becomes confined to creating education that competes with Al-Azhar so that it may spread and succeed.' As for the field of this development and 'reform', it relied on the point of weakness that the Arab and Islamic nation felt at that time towards the scientific renaissance in Europe and the various discoveries and inventions that occurred in its regions thanks to the scientific launch that had not existed before. The 'reformist' plan, then, was to alert the leaders of Arab and Islamic thought that the existence of such a renaissance in the Islamic world depended on developing the way religion and Islamic creed are understood, in a way consistent with accepted scientific thought. This meant the necessity of purifying religious thought from every unseen truth that is not understood or that falls outside the molds of modern science. Soon, those who were enamored and captivated by the modern European scientific renaissance and Western civilization in general—those whose faith had not been firmly rooted in their hearts nor whose truths were established in their minds—responded to this call. They began to be convinced—driven by that new infatuation and the preceding weakness of faith—that the only way to a renaissance similar to the European renaissance was to liberate themselves from many religious principles related to creed. And it was not incumbent upon Britain—after its inspiration had absorbed a considerable number of Arab Muslim intellectuals—to trouble itself much in following up the plan, for it was reassured that these same people would carry out the required work. It only had to bring them close and hand over to them the leadership of intellectual work in Al-Azhar to consolidate its curricula and to spread from it to all Islamic thought this new 'reformist' epidemic.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a historical analysis in which the author, Ramadan al-Buti, sets out the background of modernist movements in the Islamic world. He argues that British colonialism deliberately devised an intellectual strategy to weaken Muslims' adherence to Islam. The key step was to reform Al-Azhar, then the intellectual leader of the Muslim world. The author cites Lord Lloyd's memoirs to prove British hostility and intentionality. He then explains that the 'reform' exploited Muslims' sense of inferiority towards Western science, leading some intellectuals to call for a reinterpretation of religion to fit modern science. Buti describes these intellectuals as lacking firm faith, and their response as an 'epidemic'. The passage serves to critique the origins of modernist reformist thought and to warn against it.

Key Terms
الإصلاح الاجتماعي والديني
الجامع الأزهر
المنهج العلمي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that the 19th-century reform of Al-Azhar was an internal, natural development for progress.
Correction: Buti demonstrates, using colonial sources, that the reform was a deliberate external plan to weaken Islamic adherence, not an indigenous movement.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Britain deliberately targeted Al-Azhar as the first step in a colonial plan to weaken Islamic adherence, as evidenced by Lord Lloyd's own words.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
This lesson reveals that colonial powers deliberately targeted religious institutions. How does this change your view of calls for 'reform' in Islamic education today? Are you willing to scrutinize the origins of modern Islamic educational reforms and their alignment with Islamic values?

The Muslim Intellectual Response: The 'Reformist Epidemic'
Buti describes how colonial reform exploited Muslims' inferiority complex and led to a 'reformist epidemic'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how some Muslim intellectuals, driven by weak faith and fascination with Western progress, adopted the colonial reform agenda, leading to what Buti calls the 'reformist epidemic'.

Core Idea
The internal reform movement was a colonial epidemic, not genuine Islamic renewal.

In the second part of the passage, Buti explains how the colonial plan succeeded. He points to the 'point of weakness'—Muslims' sense of inferiority towards Western scientific progress. This led some intellectuals, whose faith was not firmly rooted, to call for a reinterpretation of Islam to align with modern science. Buti describes this as a 'new reformist epidemic' that Britain exploited by handing over leadership of Al-Azhar to these individuals.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. This section continues directly from the previous lesson.
2
Identify the 'point of weakness'
Buti says the reform plan exploited Muslims' feelings about the European scientific renaissance. What specific feeling is that?
It is a sense of backwardness and awe.
3
Describe the targeted intellectuals
Buti describes those who responded as 'enamored and captivated' by Western civilization and lacking firm faith. Highlight the phrases he uses.
4
What was the core demand of the reform?
The proposed reform required purifying religious thought from unseen truths that conflict with modern science. Understand the implication.
5
Britain's role in the outcome
Britain did not have to act further; it handed over leadership to these reformers. What does Buti call the result?
He calls it a 'reformist epidemic'—a loaded term.

فرأت - كما هو شأنها دائماً ـ أن لا بد من الاستعانة بمنهج فكري يغير من تفكير المسلمين تغييراً يقصيهم عن هذه الشدة في التمسك بالدين والتضحية من أجله والاعتماد عليه وحده . ويجعلهم يلتقون مع الفكر الأوربي في أوسع قدر ممكن من سبل الحياة . وقامت بريطانيا بهذا الدافع ، بتطبيق ما أطلقت عليه اسم الإصلاح الاجتماعي والديني : وكان الميدان الأول لهذا ( الإصلاح ) هو الجامع الأزهر المتمثل في مناهجه الدرسية وطريقته الفكرية . ذلك أن قيادة القطر المصري كله كانت إذ ذاك بید الأزهر ، وكان إشعاعه يتجاوزه إلى كثير من البقاع الإسلامية الأخرى ، فلم تكن هناك من قضية وطنية أو دينية أو مشكلة فكرية أو اجتماعية إلا والأزهر هو الرأس المدبر والمفكر فيها وهو المحرك لها ، لذلك فلم يكن لينجح أي ) إصلاح ( ديني أو فكري من وجهة نظر بريطانيا إلا إذا بدأ بالأزهر . وينبغي أن نذكرك هنا بأننا لا نتبع فيا نرويه من أحداث ووقائع تاريخية ، منهج الاسترداد أو التوسم الذي يتعلق به دون غيره منهجيـو الغرب خصوصاً بالنسبة لتاريخنا وإسلامنا ، ولكننا نتبع المنهج العلمي السليم الذي أوضحناه والتزمناه . ولعلك تتساءل ، فمن أين علمنا أن بريطانيا وضعت لنفسها هذا المخطط ، وضاقت ذرعاً بالإسلام وبأزهره ؟! فاسمع ما يقوله في ذلك اللورد لويد ، المندوب السامي لمصر إذ ذاك ، في مذكراته التي سماها ( Egypt Since Cromer : مصر منذ أيام كرومر ) . يقول : ( إن التعليم الوطني عندما قدم الإنكليز ، كان في قبضة الجامعة الأزهرية الشديدة التمسك بالدين والتي كانت أساليبها الجافة تقف حاجزاً في طريق أي إصلاح تعليمي ، وكان الطلبة الذين يتخرجون من هذه الجامعة قدراً عظيماً من غرور التعصب الديني ، ( تنبـه جـيـداً إلى معنى يحملون معهم الكلام ) فلو أمكن تطوير الأزهر لكانت خطوة جلية الخطر . فليس من اليسير أن نتصور لنا أي تقدم طالما ظل الأزهر متمسكاً بأساليبه هذه ولكن إذا بدا أن مثل هذه الخطوة غير متيسر تحقيقها فحينئذ يصبح الأمل محصوراً في إيجاد التعليم الذي ينافس الأزهر حتى يتاح له الانتشار والنجاح ) . أما مجال هذا التطوير و ( الإصلاح ( فلقد اعتمد على نقطة الضعف التي كانت الأمة العربية والإسلامية تستشعرها إذ ذاك حيال النهضة العلمية في أوربا والاكتشافات والاختراعات المختلفة التي قامت في أنحائها بفضل الانطلاقة العلمية التي لم تكن من قبل . لقد كان المخطط ( الإصلاحي ( إذاً ، هو تنبيه قادة الفكر العربي والإسلامي إلى أن وجود مثل هذه النهضة في العالم الإسلامي متوقف على تطوير الطريقة التي يتم بها فهم الدين والعقيدة الإسلامية ، بشكل يتفق مع الفكر العلمي المقبول ، وهذا يعني ضرورة تخليص الفكر الديني من كل حقيقة غيبية غير مفهومة أو داخلة في قوالب العلم الحديث وسرعان ما استجاب إلى هذه الدعوة ، أولئك المفتونون والمأخوذون بالنهضة العلمية الأوربية الحديثة والحضارة الغربية عامة ، ممن لم يرسخ الإيمان في أفئدتهم ولم تتمكن حقائقه في عقولهم ، وأخذوا يستيقنون - بدافع ذلك الافتتـان الجـديـد والضعف الإيماني السابق عليه - أن الوسيلة الوحيدة إلى نهضة شبيهة بالنهضة الأوربية ، إنما هي في التحرر من كثير من المبادئ الدينية المتعلقة بالعقيدة . ولم يكن على بريطانيا - وقد امتص إيحاؤها عدداً لا بأس به من المفكر بن العرب المسلمين ، أن تتعب نفسها كثيراً بمتابعة المخطط ، فقد اطمأنت إلى أن هؤلاء أنفسهم سيقومون بالعمل المطلوب. وما عليها إلا أن تقربهم وتسلمهم قيادة العمل الفكري في الأزهر ليوطدوا مناهجه ، وليبثوا منه إلى الفكر الإسلامي كلـه هـذا الوباء ( الإصلاحي الجديد ) .
It saw—as is its usual way—that there was no alternative but to employ an intellectual method that would change the thinking of Muslims in a way that distanced them from this intensity in clinging to religion, sacrificing for it, and relying on it alone, and would make them meet European thought in the widest possible scope of life. Britain, driven by this motive, applied what it called social and religious reform: and the first field for this 'reform' was Al-Azhar University, represented in its curricula and intellectual method. That is because the leadership of all Egypt was then in the hand of Al-Azhar, and its influence extended beyond it to many other Islamic lands. There was no national or religious issue, nor any intellectual or social problem, except that Al-Azhar was the directing and thinking head and the mover of it. Therefore, from Britain's point of view, no religious or intellectual 'reform' would succeed unless it began with Al-Azhar. And we should remind you here that in what we narrate of historical events and facts, we do not follow the method of retrieval or conjecture that Western methodologists, especially regarding our history and Islam, adhere to exclusively, but we follow the sound scientific method which we have clarified and adhered to. Perhaps you ask: how did we know that Britain set this plan for itself and became intolerant of Islam and its Al-Azhar? So hear what Lord Lloyd, the High Commissioner for Egypt at that time, says in his memoirs which he called 'Egypt Since Cromer'. He says: 'When the English came, national education was in the grasp of Al-Azhar University, which was strongly attached to religion and whose dry methods stood as an obstacle to any educational reform; and the students who graduated from this university carried a great amount of the arrogance of religious fanaticism (pay close attention to the meaning of what they carry with them). If it were possible to develop Al-Azhar, it would be a step of clear danger. It is not easy for us to imagine any progress as long as Al-Azhar remains clinging to these methods. But if it appears that such a step is not feasible, then hope becomes confined to creating education that competes with Al-Azhar so that it may spread and succeed.' As for the field of this development and 'reform', it relied on the point of weakness that the Arab and Islamic nation felt at that time towards the scientific renaissance in Europe and the various discoveries and inventions that occurred in its regions thanks to the scientific launch that had not existed before. The 'reformist' plan, then, was to alert the leaders of Arab and Islamic thought that the existence of such a renaissance in the Islamic world depended on developing the way religion and Islamic creed are understood, in a way consistent with accepted scientific thought. This meant the necessity of purifying religious thought from every unseen truth that is not understood or that falls outside the molds of modern science. Soon, those who were enamored and captivated by the modern European scientific renaissance and Western civilization in general—those whose faith had not been firmly rooted in their hearts nor whose truths were established in their minds—responded to this call. They began to be convinced—driven by that new infatuation and the preceding weakness of faith—that the only way to a renaissance similar to the European renaissance was to liberate themselves from many religious principles related to creed. And it was not incumbent upon Britain—after its inspiration had absorbed a considerable number of Arab Muslim intellectuals—to trouble itself much in following up the plan, for it was reassured that these same people would carry out the required work. It only had to bring them close and hand over to them the leadership of intellectual work in Al-Azhar to consolidate its curricula and to spread from it to all Islamic thought this new 'reformist' epidemic.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage is a historical analysis in which the author, Ramadan al-Buti, sets out the background of modernist movements in the Islamic world. He argues that British colonialism deliberately devised an intellectual strategy to weaken Muslims' adherence to Islam. The key step was to reform Al-Azhar, then the intellectual leader of the Muslim world. The author cites Lord Lloyd's memoirs to prove British hostility and intentionality. He then explains that the 'reform' exploited Muslims' sense of inferiority towards Western science, leading some intellectuals to call for a reinterpretation of religion to fit modern science. Buti describes these intellectuals as lacking firm faith, and their response as an 'epidemic'. The passage serves to critique the origins of modernist reformist thought and to warn against it.

Key Terms
الحقيقة الغيبية
النهضة العلمية الأوربية
الضعف الإيماني
الوباء الإصلاحي الجديد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that the call to reinterpret Islam to match modern science was a sincere attempt to revive Islamic civilization from within.
Correction: Buti argues that this call originated from a colonial plan and was adopted by those with weak faith, leading to a harmful 'epidemic' rather than authentic reform.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what was the 'reformist plan's' core demand regarding religious thought?
A) To adopt all Western scientific theories literally
B) To purify religious thought from every unseen truth that conflicts with modern science
C) To replace Islamic creed with secular humanism
D) To close Al-Azhar and open new universities

Key Takeaway
The colonial 'reform' succeeded because it exploited Muslims' inferiority complex and found willing intellectuals with weak faith to spread a new 'reformist epidemic'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Buti says the reformers were 'enamored and captivated' by Western civilization. Think of an area in your life—your career, education, lifestyle—where you might be unconsciously admiring Western norms more than Islamic values. What specific step will you take this week to realign that area with your faith?
?
The passage describes a deep inferiority complex towards Western scientific achievements. Have you ever felt that Islam is 'backward' or lacking in some way compared to modern advancements? If so, how has that affected your practice of the faith? What one truth from this lesson can you cling to when such feelings arise?
?
Buti warns that the colonial reform succeeded by handing leadership to those with weak faith. In your own community, do you see any leaders or influencers whose admiration for Western culture may be compromising Islamic teachings? How can you protect yourself and your family from being influenced by such 'reformist epidemics' today?

Buti's Critique of the Religious Reform Movement
Buti condemns the religious reform movement for double failure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's argument that the religious reform movement led to the loss of both religious truth and scientific progress.

Core Idea
The religious reform movement destroyed both faith and science.

In this passage, Buti delivers a sharp condemnation of the so-called 'religious reform' movement, accusing its proponents of being deceived by Western models, particularly Britain's manipulative approach. He concludes that this reform resulted in a double failure: neither preserving authentic religious identity nor achieving genuine scientific advancement. Let's examine the text and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Pay attention to the tone and the key accusations Buti makes.
Notice the rhetorical question and the reference to Britain's 'deceit'.
2
Identify Buti's main accusation
Buti claims the reform movement lost both religious truth and scientific renaissance. Find the phrase that states this dual loss.
Look for 'فقدان الحقيقتين معاً'.
3
Reflect on the critique
Consider why Buti is so critical. What does it mean for a reform movement to fail in both areas? How does this relate to broader concerns about Western influence?
This critique reflects a common theme in Islamic thought: that blind imitation leads to loss of authenticity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو همتهم أربابها ودعاتها أي نهضة علمية كالتي نهضتها أوربا ؛ كما كانوا يتوهمون ، وكما بريطانيا التي اختصت بفن المكر والخديعة واللعب بالعقول ، وليتها كانت عقولاً غير عقول المسلمين. كل ما جنته أيدي ذلك ( الإصلاح الديني ) فقدان الحقيقتين معاً ، فلا هم على حقيقتهم الدينية أبقوا ولا على النهضة العلمية عثروا .
Or did their leaders and advocates imagine any scientific renaissance like that of Europe, as they used to suppose, and like Britain which specialized in the art of deceit, trickery, and manipulation of minds—if only they were minds other than those of Muslims. All that the hands of that 'religious reform' reaped was the loss of both realities together: they neither preserved their religious reality nor succeeded in the scientific renaissance.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a critique of the so-called 'religious reform' movement. Buti begins by accusing its proponents of imagining a scientific revival similar to Europe's, but in reality, the example of Britain shows deception and manipulation. He then concludes that this reform led to losing both religious authenticity and scientific progress. It is a concise condemnation.

Key Terms
الإصلاح الديني
النهضة العلمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The religious reform movement successfully preserved Islamic faith while adopting Western science.
Correction: Buti asserts that it lost both: 'they neither preserved their religious reality nor succeeded in the scientific renaissance.'

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what was the result of the religious reform movement?
A) It preserved religion and advanced science.
B) It lost both religious truth and scientific advancement.
C) It preserved religion but failed in science.
D) It succeeded in science but lost religion.

Key Takeaway
Buti concludes that the religious reform movement led to the loss of both religious authenticity and scientific progress, achieving neither goal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life have you been willing to compromise a clear Islamic principle in order to gain something you thought was necessary for worldly success? What did you lose in the process, and what did you actually gain?
?
The reformers imagined they could have a European-style renaissance while keeping their religion. Buti says they lost both. Where in your own life are you trying to hold two incompatible things—like career ambition and religious devotion—hoping to balance them, while really losing both?
?
Britain is described as specializing in deceit and manipulation of minds. How has the constant exposure to Western media, education, or lifestyle subtly deceived you into valuing their standards over your deen? What concrete step will you take this week to reclaim your authentic religious reality?

Three Fundamental Truths About Humans
Enumeration of three human facts a Muslim must know and believe.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three essential truths about humanity that a Muslim must know and believe as a foundation for faith.

Core Idea
Three truths anchor human dignity, origin, and creation.

Before we can understand the meaning of faith in Allah, we must first understand who we are. The author presents three fundamental truths about the human being that every Muslim must internalize with certainty. These truths cover our status, our origin, and our creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the three points labeled A, B, C.
The author emphasizes certainty and internalization.
2
Examine each truth individually
Look at each truth: human nobility, creation from dust and from Adam, and special creation without evolution.
3
Reflect on the basis of faith
Consider how these truths support one's faith in Allah. The passage says they are the foundation for the meaning of faith.
Internalize them as certainties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على المسلم أن يلم بالحقائق التالية عن الإنسان وواقعه ، ثم يستيقنها في نفسه ، ويقيم عليها معنى إيمانه بالله عز وجل :
أ - الإنسان أفضل المخلوقات وأشرفها
ب - الإنسان مخلوق - من حيث الجنس - من عنصر التراب ، ومتكاثر - من حيث المصدر - من الإنسان الأول آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام .
ج ـ الإنسان مخلوق ، منذ النشأة الأولى ، في أتم مظهر وأحسن تقويم ، لم يتطور خلال شيء من تاريخه تطوراً نوعياً يتدرج به من فصيلة إلى أخرى .
It is incumbent upon the Muslim to be acquainted with the following facts about the human and his reality, then to be certain of them in himself, and to base upon them the meaning of his faith in Allah Almighty:
A- The human is the best and most noble of creation.
B- The human is created - as to genus - from the element of dust, and multiplied - as to source - from the first human Adam, peace be upon him.
C- The human was created, from the first origin, in the most perfect appearance and the best stature; he did not undergo during any part of his history a gradual typal development by which he would progress from one species to another.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of three fundamental truths about humans that a Muslim must know and internalize with certainty, and then use these truths as the basis for their faith in God. The author presents them as a list. First truth (A): Humans are the best and most noble of all created beings. Second truth (B): Humans as a species were created from dust (referring to the original creation of Adam), and they reproduce from Adam, the first human. Third truth (C): Humans were created in a perfect form from the beginning, and they did not undergo gradual evolutionary change from one species to another throughout history. These points establish human dignity, origin from a single source, and special creation without evolutionary transformation.

Key Terms
إنسان
مخلوق
تراب
آدم
تطور نوعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These facts are purely scientific claims, not religious certainties.
Correction: The author presents them as theological certainties that underpin faith, not as scientific hypotheses.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the source of human multiplication (reproduction) as to origin?
A) From the earth directly for each individual
B) From the first human Adam
C) From a common animal ancestor
D) From spontaneous generation

Key Takeaway
The three truths about human nobility, dust-born origin, and special creation are foundational Islamic beliefs that shape faith in Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if you are the best and noblest of creation? In what specific ways does your daily conduct either honor or cheapen that dignity?
?
When you feel pride or arrogance, do you recall that you were created from dust? How can remembering your humble origin actually transform your character this week?
?
Have you ever subtly accepted the idea that humans evolved from lower forms? How does this passage challenge you to fully submit to Allah's account of your creation, even if it contradicts modern narratives?

The First Truth: Humans as the Best of Creation – Scriptural Foundation and the Angelic Debate
Introduces the first truth about humans with Quranic proofs and debates on angelic superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic evidence for human superiority and the interpretive debate regarding humans versus angels.

Core Idea
The Quran affirms human honor, but the phrase 'over many' sparks scholarly debate about whether humans surpass angels.

This lesson unpacks the first fundamental truth about humanity: that we are the best of creation. The author presents clear Quranic proofs, yet a subtle ambiguity in the wording leads to an important theological discussion about our status relative to angels. We will explore both the evidence and the scholarly perspectives.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two proofs
The passage states that human superiority is established by two proofs: a truthful report (al-khabar al-yaqini al-sadiq) and a rational proof (burhan al-‘aql). However, only the first proof is elaborated in this excerpt.
The rational proof is not provided in these pages; it is mentioned but not detailed.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
Focus on the two verses: Surah al-Isra' 17:70 (honoring humans and favoring them over many) and Surah al-Baqarah 2:34 (command to angels to prostrate to Adam). Consider how each supports human superiority.
The prostration verse is a strong indicator of Adam's rank over angels.
3
Understand the debate over 'many'
The word 'many' (كثير) in verse 17:70 creates ambiguity. Some scholars argue that it implies there are creatures (likely angels) not included in the favor, while others hold that 'many' does not necessitate exclusion. Notice how this leads to different views on whether humans are superior to angels.
This is the central interpretive dispute discussed.
4
Review the positions and the majority view
Identify the two camps: those who say angels are absolutely superior (Ibn Abbas, al-Zajjaj) and the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah who distinguish between elites and commoners. Note that the passage ends before completing the majority's evidence.
The passage is incomplete; the rational proof and further arguments are missing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولا: الإنسان
على المسلم أن يلم بالحقائق التالية عن الإنسان وواقعه، ثم يستيقنها في نفسه، ويقيم عليها معنى إيمانه بالله عز وجل:
أ - الإنسان أفضل المخلوقات وأشرفها
ب - الإنسان مخلوق - من حيث الجنس - من عنصر التراب، ومتكاثر - من حيث المصدر - من الإنسان الأول آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام.
ج - الإنسان مخلوق، منذ النشأة الأولى، في أتم مظهر وأحسن تقويم، لم يتطور خلال شيء من تاريخه تطوراً نوعياً يتدرج به من فصيلة إلى أخرى.
ولنعد بالإيضاح إلى كل حقيقة من هذه الحقائق الثلاث على حدة.
أ - الإنسان أفضل المخلوقات وأشرفها:
ثبتت هذه الحقيقة بدليلين: أحدهما دليل الخبر اليقيني الصادق، ثانيها برهان العقل.
أما الخبر الصادق، فقوله عز وجل: وَلَقَدْ كَرَّمْنَا بَنِي آدَمَ وَحَمَلْنَاهُمْ فِي الْبَرِّ وَالْبَحْرِ وَرَزَقْنَاهُمْ مِنَ الطَّيِّبَاتِ وَفَضَّلْنَاهُمْ عَلَى كَثِيرٍ مِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَا تَفْضِيلًا. [الإسراء: 70] وقوله عز وجل: وَإِذْ قُلْنَا لِلْمَلَائِكَةِ اسْجُدُوا لِآدَمَ فَسَجَدُوا إِلَّا إِبْلِيسَ أَبَى وَاسْتَكْبَرَ وَكَانَ مِنَ الْكَافِرِينَ. [البقرة: 34].
والدليل في كل من الآيتين واضح الدلالة على المطلوب. ولا إشكال في معرفة أن الإنسان أفضل مما عدا الملائكة من المخلوقات، فهاتان الآيتان وكثير من الآيات الأخرى تصرح بذلك. ولكن وقع النظر والبحث في تعميم هذا حتى بالنسبة للملائكة أيضاً.
وسبب الاحتمال والغموض في ذلك، قول الله تعالى في آخر الآية الأولى التي ذكرناها: ﴿ وَفَضَّلْنَاهُمْ عَلَى كَثِيرٍ مِمَّنْ خَلَقْنَا تَفْضِيلًا ﴾ إذ هي تدل عند من أخذ بدليل الخطاب على أن هنالك بعضاً من المخلوقات لم يفضّل عليها الإنسان؛ ولا ريب أن هذا البعض ينبغي أن يكون الملائكة، لما ثبت في القرآن والسنة الصحيحة من بيان فضلهم وعظيم درجاتهم.
أما من لم يتمسك بدليل الخطاب، واكتفى بالأخذ بما ينطق به النص، فقد قال إن استعمال كلمة «كثير» بدلاً من «الكل» لا يدل على أن الحال في القليل بالضد. وأمضى الآية على عمومها في أفضلية الإنسان على سائر المخلوقات.
فيمن قال بأفضلية الملائكة على الإنسان مطلقاً، عبد الله بن عباس رضي الله عنهما، وهو اختيار الزجاج على ما رواه الواحدي) واحتجوا بما ذكرنا من آخر الآية، وبقوله جل جلاله عن الملائكة ﴿ بَلْ عِبَادٌ مُكْرَمُونَ لَا يَسْبِقُونَهُ بِالْقَوْلِ وَهُمْ بِأَمْرِهِ يَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الأنبياء: 26-27] وبقوله تعالى ﴿ لَا يَعْصُونَ اللَّهَ مَا أَمَرَهُمْ وَيَفْعَلُونَ مَا يُؤْمَرُونَ ﴾ [التحريم: 6] وبحديث البخاري رضي الله عنه «من ذكرني في ملأ ذكرته في ملأ خير من ملئه» قال القرطبي وهو نص في أفضلية الملائكة (٢).
ومذهب جمهور أهل السنة والجماعة أنَّ خواص البشر من الأنبياء والصديقين أفضل من خواص الملائكة، وهم الذين خصهم الله بالذكر في كتابه الكريم. وعوام البشر وهم الصالحون من المسلمين أفضل من عوام الملائكة. ومن أدلتهم على
First: The Human
It is incumbent upon the Muslim to comprehend the following facts about the human and his reality, then to be certain of them in himself, and to establish upon them the meaning of his faith in Allah Almighty:
A – The human is the best and most honorable of created beings.
B – The human is created – in terms of kind – from the element of dust, and multiplied – in terms of origin – from the first human, Adam, peace and blessings be upon him.
C – The human was created, from the first origin, in the most perfect form and the best stature, and did not undergo during any part of his history a qualitative evolution transitioning him from one species to another.
Let us return with clarification to each of these three facts separately.
A – The human is the best and most honorable of created beings:
This fact is established by two proofs: one is the proof of the truthful certain report, and the second is the proof of reason.
As for the truthful report, it is His saying, Almighty: 'And indeed We have honored the children of Adam, and carried them on land and sea, and provided them with good things, and favored them over many of those We have created with a marked favoring.' [Al-Isra: 70] And His saying, Almighty: 'And when We said to the angels, "Prostrate to Adam," and they prostrated, except Iblis; he refused and was arrogant and became one of the disbelievers.' [Al-Baqarah: 34].
And the evidence in each of the two verses is clear in indicating what is sought. And there is no difficulty in knowing that the human is better than the creatures other than the angels, for these two verses and many other verses explicitly state that. But consideration and investigation occurred regarding generalizing this even with respect to the angels as well.
The reason for the possibility and ambiguity in that is the saying of Allah Almighty at the end of the first verse we mentioned: 'And favored them over many of those We have created with a marked favoring' – for it indicates, according to those who adhere to the implication of the address, that there are some creatures over whom the human has not been favored; and there is no doubt that this 'some' must be the angels, due to what is established in the Quran and authentic Sunnah of the statement of their merit and the greatness of their ranks.
As for those who do not adhere to the implication of the address, and are content with taking what the text pronounces, they say that the use of the word 'many' instead of 'all' does not indicate that the situation regarding the few is the opposite. And they applied the verse to its generality concerning the superiority of the human over all other creatures.
Among those who said that angels are absolutely superior to humans is Abdullah ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, and it is the choice of al-Zajjaj according to what al-Wahidi narrated. And they adduced as evidence what we mentioned from the end of the verse, and His saying, Majestic is His Majesty, about the angels: 'But they are honored servants; they do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command.' [Al-Anbiya: 26-27] And His saying, Exalted: 'They do not disobey Allah in what He commands them, and they do what they are commanded.' [Al-Tahrim: 6] And the hadith of al-Bukhari, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Whoever mentions Me in a group, I mention him in a group better than his group.' Al-Qurtubi said: And it is a clear text on the superiority of the angels. (2)
And the doctrine of the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah is that the elite of humans – the prophets and the truthful – are better than the elite of the angels, and they are those whom Allah specifically mentioned in His Noble Book. And the common people of humans – the righteous among Muslims – are better than the common angels. And among their proofs is that
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage presents the first of three fundamental facts that a Muslim must internalize about human beings: that humans are the best and most honorable of created beings. The author, Ramadan Buti, opens by listing all three facts together as a set, then returns to explain the first in detail. He states that this fact is proven by two kinds of evidence: a certain truthful report (al-khabar al-yaqini al-sadiq) and a rational proof (burhan al-‘aql). However, in this section he only elaborates the revealed proof, providing two Quranic verses: Surah al-Isra’ 17:70, which explicitly states that Allah has favored humans over 'many' of His creation, and Surah al-Baqarah 2:34, which recounts the command to the angels to prostrate to Adam. The author notes that the superiority of humans over non-angelic creatures is uncontroversial from these texts. The difficulty arises when we consider whether humans are also superior to angels. The ambiguity stems from the phrase 'over many' in verse 17:70, which suggests that there are some creatures—likely angels—over whom humans are not favored. The author then presents two interpretive camps: those who follow 'dalil al-khitab' (the implication of the address) hold that the exception must be the angels, since their high rank is attested elsewhere. In contrast, those who do not employ this principle take the verse at face value, arguing that 'many' does not imply that the remainder are superior, and thus they maintain the generalization of human superiority over all creatures. The passage then notes that Abdullah ibn Abbas and al-Zajjaj held that angels are absolutely superior, citing additional Quranic verses (21:26-27, 66:6) and a hadith from al-Bukhari. Al-Qurtubi considered this hadith a clear text for angelic superiority. Finally, the author presents the majority view of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, which distinguishes between the elite of humans (prophets and the truthful) and the elite of angels, and between common righteous humans and common angels, affirming that each elite class is superior to the corresponding class of the other. The passage ends with 'and among their proofs is...' indicating that further evidence follows on subsequent pages.

برهان العقل
أفضلية الإنسان

دليل الخطاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'over many' in Surah al-Isra definitively proves that angels are superior to humans.
Correction: The verse uses 'many', which allows for two interpretations: either angels are excluded (showing their superiority) or 'many' does not imply exclusion, maintaining human superiority. The passage presents both views, so the matter is not definitively settled by this verse alone.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason for the ambiguity regarding whether humans are superior to angels?
A) The rational proof is insufficient.
B) The word 'many' in Surah al-Isra' 17:70 suggests some creatures are superior.
C) The angels refused to prostrate to Adam.
D) The majority of Ahl al-Sunnah reject human superiority.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic evidence for human honor is clear, but the superiority relative to angels is debated, with the majority view distinguishing between elites and commoners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah honored Adam by commanding the angels to prostrate, do you truly live with the awareness of that honor? Have you ever felt unworthy or low, forgetting that you are from the children of Adam? Ask yourself: What would change in your daily behavior if you fully internalized that you are the best of creation—not because of your own deeds, but because of Allah's choice? Commit to one action today that reflects that honor.
?
The debate on humans vs. angels is not just academic. If someone tells you that angels are better because they never sin, do you feel inferior? The lesson shows that the elite of humanity (prophets) are better than the elite of angels. Does this not call you to strive to be among those elite? What are you doing today to rise from being a common believer to a special one?
?
The verse says 'over many'—there are different interpretations. But the key is that Allah has favored you. Are you grateful for that favor? How often do you thank Allah for creating you as a human being capable of faith and obedience? Write down one specific way you can show gratitude for your humanity today.
