Two Interpretations of Human Superiority over Angels
Two opinions on human-angel superiority with evidence for angelic preference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main interpretations of Quran 17:70 regarding human superiority over angels, and the evidence used by those who argue for angel superiority.

Core Idea
The phrase 'over many' in the Quran sparks a debate: does it imply some creatures are excluded?

This lesson introduces the central theological debate on whether humans are superior to angels. The Quran states that humans are preferred over 'many' of creation, but later scholars disagreed on whether 'many' includes all. We will explore the two positions and the scriptural evidence for angelic superiority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of ambiguity
Read the opening lines and note how the word 'many' (كثير) in verse 17:70 creates uncertainty. Some scholars apply the principle of implication of address (dalil al-khitab) to argue that 'many' implies some creatures are excluded, while others take the literal meaning as general preference.
2
Find the two opposing opinions
The passage presents two groups: those who hold angels superior to humans (based on the implication that 'many' excludes angels) and those who hold humans superior over all creatures (taking the verse at face value). Identify each group and their key proponents.
Ibn Abbas and al-Zajjaj are mentioned for the angel-superior view.
3
Examine the evidence for angel superiority
The passage cites Quranic verses (21:26-27, 66:6) and a hadith from al-Bukhari, which al-Qurtubi considers a clear text (nass) for angel superiority. Read these sources carefully.
The hadith: 'Whoever mentions Me in a gathering, I mention him in a gathering better than his.'
4
Reflect on al-Qurtubi's statement
Al-Qurtubi explicitly says the hadith is a clear text on angel superiority. Consider what this means for the debate: does the hadith settle the question? Note that other scholars disagree.

Other verses declare that. But consideration and research occurred regarding generalizing this even to the angels. The reason for possibility and ambiguity in that is the saying of God Most High at the end of the first verse we mentioned: 'And We preferred them over many of those We created, a great preference.' [17:70] For it indicates, for those who take the implication of address, that there are some creatures over which humans were not preferred; and there is no doubt that this group should be the angels, due to what is established in the Quran and authentic Sunnah of the clarification of their virtue and the greatness of their ranks. As for one who does not adhere to the implication of address and suffices with taking what the text literally says, he said that the use of the word 'many' instead of 'all' does not indicate that the situation with the few is the opposite. And he applies the verse generally to the superiority of humans over all creatures. Al-Qurtubi said: this is a clear text (nass) on the superiority of the angels. (2) The madhhab of the majority of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a is that the elite of humans from among the prophets and the truthful are superior to the elite of the angels, and they are those whom God specifically mentioned in His noble Book. And the common humans, who are the righteous Muslims, are superior to the common angels. Among their evidences for that is the saying of God Most High: 'Indeed, those who have believed and done righteous deeds, those are the best of creatures.' [98:7] And 'creatures' includes the angels. And by the hadith that Abu Dawud and others narrated from the Messenger of God, may peace be upon him, that he said: 'Indeed, the angels lower their wings in pleasure for the seeker of knowledge.' Also they adduced that by what God equipped humans with of the components of moral responsibility (taklif) by which they deserve reward and recompense for carrying out the duties God charged them with. For God composed in them various desires and passions, by combating and overcoming which they deserve a reward that the angels do not deserve, due to the absence of any of these desires and passions in their existential composition. (1) Al-Qurtubi said: There is no way to be certain that the prophets are superior to the angels, nor certain that the angels are better than them, because the way to that is the reports of God Most High and the reports of His Messenger (i.e., the mutawatir among that) or the consensus of the community, and there is nothing of that here. As for the rational proof, it is represented in the following matters: The first matter: that the human soul is distinguished from all other souls and other existents by those amazing marvelous powers, namely the rational power that perceives the realities of things, and it is thereby the first key for subjugating many manifestations of the universe for humans and making them under his authority. And among the characteristics of this rational power is that it is the power in which the light of knowledge of God Most High is manifested and from which the light of His majesty shines, thus preparing its possessor thereby for practicing servitude to its great Creator, Exalted is His Majesty. So the human becomes, as a result, the first manifestation of the divinity of God Almighty and Majestic. And if the matter is so, then among its clear requirements is that the human soul be...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage presents the theological debate about the relative superiority of humans and angels. It begins by noting that some verses explicitly state human superiority over many creatures, but this raised the question of whether it applies even to angels. The author identifies the source of ambiguity: the phrase 'over many' in the Quranic verse (17:70). Those who adopt the principle of 'dalil al-khitab' (implication of address) argue that 'many' implies some are excluded, and that excluded group must be angels, given their high rank in revelation. Others, who reject this principle, take the verse at face value as a general preference of humans over all creatures. The text then reports the opinion of Ibn Abbas, al-Zajjaj, and others who hold angels absolutely superior, citing Quranic verses (21:26-27, 66:6) and a hadith that al-Qurtubi considers explicit text on angel superiority. Next, it presents the majority Sunni position: the elite humans (prophets and truthful) are superior to elite angels, and common righteous Muslims are superior to common angels. Evidence includes Quran 98:7, the hadith of angels lowering wings for knowledge seekers, and a rational argument: humans are composed with desires and passions, and overcoming them for obedience earns a reward angels cannot attain since they lack these desires. Al-Qurtubi then interjects that there is no definitive proof (qat') from mutawatir texts or consensus for either position. Finally, the author introduces a rational proof ('burhan al-aql') consisting of multiple points, but only the first is given here: the human soul possesses a rational power that perceives realities, enabling subjugation of the universe, and this power manifests knowledge of God and prepares for servitude, making humans the first manifestation of God's divinity. The rational proof is incomplete in this passage.

Key Terms
أفضلية
الملائكة
دليل الخطاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic phrase 'over many' necessarily implies that some creatures are excluded from human superiority.
Correction: The implication of 'many' is not logically necessary; it depends on the principle of dalil al-khitab, which is not accepted by all scholars. Literalists argue the verse does not indicate exclusion.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason for the ambiguity about human superiority over angels?
A) The word 'many' in Quran 17:70
B) The lack of any Quranic verses about angels
C) The hadith about gathering
D) The disagreement between Ibn Abbas and al-Zajjaj

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of the Quranic word 'many' is the pivot of the debate on human-angel superiority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quranic phrase 'over many' in verse 17:70, do you naturally assume it means 'over all' or 'over some'? What does your assumption reveal about your trust in your own reasoning versus relying on scholarly principles?
?
If the angels are indeed superior to you, are you comfortable with that? Does your ego resist the idea that a created being might be closer to God than you are?
?
The debate over this single word has divided scholars for centuries. Where does your heart stand: are you more concerned with being the best among creation, or with being beloved to God regardless of rank? How will you act on that priority today?

The Majority Sunni View and the Rational Proof for Human Superiority
Majority Sunni position on human-angel superiority with evidence and beginning of rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the majority Sunni position on human-angel superiority, the evidence they present, and the beginning of a rational proof based on the human rational soul.

Core Idea
Humans' ability to overcome desires makes them worthy of a reward angels cannot attain.

After reviewing the two interpretations, this lesson presents the majority Sunni view: elite humans (prophets and truthful) are superior to elite angels, and righteous common humans are superior to common angels. We will examine their evidence from Quran, hadith, and a rational argument from moral struggle, followed by the start of a rational proof emphasizing the unique rational power of the human soul.

Guided Path
1
Learn the majority classification
Read the passage to understand the distinction between 'elite' (khawas) and 'common' ('awam) humans and angels. Note the categories: elite humans vs elite angels, common humans vs common angels.
2
Identify the three types of evidence
The majority adduces a Quranic verse (98:7), a hadith about angels lowering wings for knowledge seekers, and a rational argument from taklif (moral responsibility). Find each one and note how it supports human superiority.
3
Understand the rational argument from taklif
The argument states that humans have desires and passions, and overcoming them for obedience earns a reward that angels cannot attain because they lack such inner struggles. Grasp why this is seen as evidence for human superiority.
4
Note al-Qurtubi's caution
Al-Qurtubi interjects that there is no definitive proof (qat') from mutawatir texts or consensus for either position. Consider the significance of this statement for the overall debate.
This shows that even the majority view is not considered absolutely certain.
5
Examine the first point of the rational proof
The rational proof (burhan al-aql) begins by highlighting the human soul's rational power, which perceives realities, enables subjugation of the universe, and manifests knowledge of God. This makes humans a manifestation of God's divinity. Reflect on how this supports human superiority.
The rational proof is incomplete in this passage; only the first point is given.

من الآيات الأخرى تصرح بذلك . ولكن وقع النظر والبحث في تعميم هذا حتى بالنسبة للملائكة أيضاً الحكم وسبب الاحتمال والغموض في ذلك ، قول الله تعالى في آخر الآية الأولى التي ذكرناها : ﴿ وَفَضَّلْنَاهُمْ على كَثِيرٍ مِّمَّنْ خَلَقنا تفضيلاً * إذ ( هي تدل عند من أخذ بدليل الخطاب ـ على أن هنالك بعضاً من المخلوقات لم يفضّل عليها الإنسان ؛ ولا ريب أن هذا البعض ينبغي أن يكون الملائكة ، لما ثبت في القرآن والسنة الصحيحة من بيان فضلهم وعظیم درجاتهم أما من لم يتمسك بدليل الخطاب ، واكتفى بالأخذ بما ينطق به النص ، فقد قال إن استعمال كلمة « كثير » بدلاً من « الكل » لا يدل على أن الحال في القليل بالضد . وأمضى الآية على عمومها في أفضلية الإنسان على سائر المخلوقات (١) الله فيمن قال بأفضلية الملائكة على الإنسان مطلقاً ، عبد الله بن عباس رضي ، وهو اختيار الزجاج على مارواه الواحدي ) واحتجوا بما ذكرنا من آخر الآية ، وبقوله جل جلاله عن الملائكة بل عباد مُكْرَمون ، لا يسبقونه بالقول عنهما - وهُم بأمره يَعمَلونَ ﴾ [ الأنبياء : ٢٦ ٢٧] وبقوله تعالى لا يَعْصونَ اللهَ ما أَمَرَهُمْ ،  َويَفَعَلونَ ما يُؤمَرونَ ﴾ [التحريم : ٦ ] وبحديث البخاري رضي الله عنه « من ذكرني في ملأ ذكرته في ملأ خير من ملئه » قال القرطبي وهو نص في أفضلية الملائكة (٢) ومذهب جمهور أهل السنة والجماعة أنَّ خواص البشر من الأنبياء والصديقين أفضل من خواص الملائكة ، وهم الذين خصهم الله بالذكر في كتابه الكريم. وعوام البشر وهم الصالحون من المسلمين أفضل من عوام الملائكة . ومن أدلتهم على ذلك قول الله تعالى ﴿ إن الذينَ آمَنوا وعملوا الصَّالِحاتِ أُولئِكَ هُمْ خَيْرُ البَرِيَّة ) [ البينة : ٧] والبريّة تشمل الملائكة ، وبالحديث الذي أخرجه أبو داود وغيره عن رسول الله مع العلم أنه قال : « إن الملائكة لتضع أجنحتها رضاً لطالب العلم » كما استدلوا على ذلك بما جهز الله به الإنسان من مقومات التكليف التي بها يستأهل الأجر والمثوبة على القيام بما كلفه الله به من واجبات ، فقد ركب الله فيه مختلف الشهوات والأهواء التي يستأهل بمقارعتها والتغلب عليها أجراً لا يستأهله الملائكة ، لعدم وجود شيء من هذه الشهوات والأهواء في تركيبهم الوجودي (١) • قال القرطبي : ولا طريق إلى القطع بأن الأنبياء أفضل من الملائكة ، ولا القطع بأن الملائكة خير منهم ، لأن طريق ذلك خبر الله تعالى وخبر رسوله ( أي المتواتر من ذلك ( أو إجماع الأمة ، وليس هاهنا شيء منه وأما برهان العقل : فيتمثل في الأمور التالية : . الأمر الأول : أن النفس الإنسانية تمتاز عن سائر النفوس والموجودات الأخرى بتلك القوى المدهشة العجيبة ، ألا وهي القوة العاقلة المدركة لحقائق الأشياء وهي بذلك أول مفتاح لتسخير كثير من مظاهر الكون للإنسان ولجعلها تحت سلطانه ومن خصائص هذه القوة العاقلة ، أنها القوة التي يتجلّى فيها نور معرفة الله تعالى ويشرق منها ضوء كبريائه ، فتهيئ صاحبها بذلك لممارسة العبودية لخالقها العظيم جل جلاله . فيصبح الإنسان نتيجة لذلك أول مظهر لألوهية الله عز وجل . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، فإن من لوازمه الواضحة أن تكون النفس الإنسانية
Other verses declare that. But consideration and research occurred regarding generalizing this even to the angels. The reason for possibility and ambiguity in that is the saying of God Most High at the end of the first verse we mentioned: 'And We preferred them over many of those We created, a great preference.' [17:70] For it indicates, for those who take the implication of address, that there are some creatures over which humans were not preferred; and there is no doubt that this group should be the angels, due to what is established in the Quran and authentic Sunnah of the clarification of their virtue and the greatness of their ranks. As for one who does not adhere to the implication of address and suffices with taking what the text literally says, he said that the use of the word 'many' instead of 'all' does not indicate that the situation with the few is the opposite. And he applies the verse generally to the superiority of humans over all creatures. (1) Among those who said angels are absolutely superior to humans is Abd Allah ibn Abbas (may God be pleased with them both), and it is the choice of al-Zajjaj according to what al-Wahidi narrated. They adduced what we mentioned from the end of the verse, and His saying, Exalted is His Majesty, about the angels: 'But they are honored servants. They do not precede Him in speech, and they act by His command.' [21:26-27] and His saying Most High: 'They do not disobey God in what He commands them, and they do what they are commanded.' [66:6] and the hadith of al-Bukhari (may God be pleased with him): 'Whoever mentions Me in a gathering, I mention him in a gathering better than his.' Al-Qurtubi said: this is a clear text (nass) on the superiority of the angels. (2) The madhhab of the majority of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a is that the elite of humans from among the prophets and the truthful are superior to the elite of the angels, and they are those whom God specifically mentioned in His noble Book. And the common humans, who are the righteous Muslims, are superior to the common angels. Among their evidences for that is the saying of God Most High: 'Indeed, those who have believed and done righteous deeds, those are the best of creatures.' [98:7] And 'creatures' includes the angels. And by the hadith that Abu Dawud and others narrated from the Messenger of God, may peace be upon him, that he said: 'Indeed, the angels lower their wings in pleasure for the seeker of knowledge.' Also they adduced that by what God equipped humans with of the components of moral responsibility (taklif) by which they deserve reward and recompense for carrying out the duties God charged them with. For God composed in them various desires and passions, by combating and overcoming which they deserve a reward that the angels do not deserve, due to the absence of any of these desires and passions in their existential composition. (1) Al-Qurtubi said: There is no way to be certain that the prophets are superior to the angels, nor certain that the angels are better than them, because the way to that is the reports of God Most High and the reports of His Messenger (i.e., the mutawatir among that) or the consensus of the community, and there is nothing of that here. As for the rational proof, it is represented in the following matters: The first matter: that the human soul is distinguished from all other souls and other existents by those amazing marvelous powers, namely the rational power that perceives the realities of things, and it is thereby the first key for subjugating many manifestations of the universe for humans and making them under his authority. And among the characteristics of this rational power is that it is the power in which the light of knowledge of God Most High is manifested and from which the light of His majesty shines, thus preparing its possessor thereby for practicing servitude to its great Creator, Exalted is His Majesty. So the human becomes, as a result, the first manifestation of the divinity of God Almighty and Majestic. And if the matter is so, then among its clear requirements is that the human soul be...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage presents the theological debate about the relative superiority of humans and angels. It begins by noting that some verses explicitly state human superiority over many creatures, but this raised the question of whether it applies even to angels. The author identifies the source of ambiguity: the phrase 'over many' in the Quranic verse (17:70). Those who adopt the principle of 'dalil al-khitab' (implication of address) argue that 'many' implies some are excluded, and that excluded group must be angels, given their high rank in revelation. Others, who reject this principle, take the verse at face value as a general preference of humans over all creatures. The text then reports the opinion of Ibn Abbas, al-Zajjaj, and others who hold angels absolutely superior, citing Quranic verses (21:26-27, 66:6) and a hadith that al-Qurtubi considers explicit text on angel superiority. Next, it presents the majority Sunni position: the elite humans (prophets and truthful) are superior to elite angels, and common righteous Muslims are superior to common angels. Evidence includes Quran 98:7, the hadith of angels lowering wings for knowledge seekers, and a rational argument: humans are composed with desires and passions, and overcoming them for obedience earns a reward angels cannot attain since they lack these desires. Al-Qurtubi then interjects that there is no definitive proof (qat') from mutawatir texts or consensus for either position. Finally, the author introduces a rational proof ('burhan al-aql') consisting of multiple points, but only the first is given here: the human soul possesses a rational power that perceives realities, enabling subjugation of the universe, and this power manifests knowledge of God and prepares for servitude, making humans the first manifestation of God's divinity. The rational proof is incomplete in this passage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The majority Sunni position is definitively proven and universally accepted without doubt.
Correction: Al-Qurtubi explicitly states that there is no decisive textual or consensus-based proof for either position, leaving room for scholarly disagreement.

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, who is superior to common angels?
A) Only prophets
B) The elite angels
C) Righteous Muslims (common humans)
D) No human is superior to any angel

Key Takeaway
The Sunni majority holds that righteous humans are superior to angels, supported by scriptural and rational arguments, but definitive proof remains absent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you view your struggles with your desires as a burden or as an opportunity to earn a reward that even angels cannot attain? How does this perspective change your daily battles?
?
The passage says the rational soul manifests knowledge of God. In what ways does your pursuit of knowledge about God actually shape your heart and actions, or are you content with intellectual understanding?
?
Al-Qurtubi notes that there is no definitive proof on this matter. How does living with theological uncertainty affect your humility before God and your reliance on His mercy?

Human Superiority: Certain over Creatures, Probable over Angels
Buti asserts certainty for human superiority over creatures except angels, and probability over angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that human superiority over all creatures except angels is a matter of certainty, while the question of superiority over angels is probable and should be reserved to God's knowledge.

Core Idea
Certainty about human superiority stops at angels.

In this concluding passage, Buti clarifies the doctrinal status of human superiority. He affirms with certainty that humans are above all other creatures—except angels—based on clear evidence from revelation and reason. He then addresses the more ambiguous question of human superiority over angels, where the evidence is only speculative, advising the believer to leave the matter to God's knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice that Buti presents two distinct claims: one certain, one probable.
The passage begins with 'خلاصة القول' signaling a conclusion.
2
Identify the two claims
Buti makes two main claims: (1) human superiority over other creatures (except angels) is certain, and (2) human superiority over angels is not certain—it is probable and disagreement is allowed.
Pay attention to the words 'بالقطع' (with certainty) and 'ظنية' (speculative).
3
Understand the evidence for certainty
Buti states that the first claim is supported by mutawatir report (al-khabar al-sadiq al-mutawatir) and rational proof (al-burhan al-‘aqli). Reflect on why these two sources together establish certainty.
Mutawatir report gives certainty in transmitted knowledge; rational proof gives certainty in intellectual knowledge.
4
Reflect on the speculative nature of the angel comparison
The second claim is based on speculative evidence, leading to disagreement. Buti advises the safest course is to refer the matter to God's knowledge.
This shows humility and acknowledges limits of human reason in some theological questions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فخلاصة القول : أن أفضلية الإنسان على سائر المخلوقات ( باستثناء الملائكة ( حقيقة ثابتة بالقطع . دلّ عليها الخبر الصادق المتواتر والبرهان العقلي الصحيح . فوجب على المسلم أن يعتقد ذلك وأما أفضليته على الملائكة ، فالأمر في ذلك محتمل ، والأدلة ظنية ولذلك وقع الخلاف ، ولعل الأسلم فيه أن نحيل حقيقة الأمر في ذلك إلى علم الله عـز وجل .
The conclusion of the statement: that the superiority of man over the rest of creatures (with the exception of angels) is a truth established with certainty. The truthful, mutawatir report and the correct rational proof indicate it. So it is obligatory for the Muslim to believe that. As for his superiority over the angels, the matter regarding that is probable, and the evidences are speculative, therefore disagreement occurred. And perhaps the safest in that is to refer the reality of the matter in that to the knowledge of God Almighty.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage concludes a previous discussion about the status of humans. It states two points: first, it is certain that humans are superior to all other creatures except angels, based on both transmitted (mutawatir report) and rational evidence; second, the question of human superiority over angels is not certain—it is only probable, so the safest position is to leave the true knowledge of it to God.

البرهان العقلي
القطع
الظن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think human superiority over angels is certain, just as it is over other creatures.
Correction: Buti clarifies that superiority over angels is only probable; the evidence is speculative, not certain.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the basis for the certainty of human superiority over other creatures (except angels)?
A) Speculation and personal opinion
B) Mutawatir reports and rational proof
C) Consensus of scholars
D) Benefit and practicality

Key Takeaway
Human superiority over other creatures (excluding angels) is certain and must be believed, but superiority over angels is probable and best left to God's knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are certain about a religious matter, do you check whether that certainty comes from solid evidence or from personal comfort? How would you respond if a dear belief of yours turned out to be only probable?
?
Buti says the safest is to refer the true reality of the angels question to Allah's knowledge. In what area of your life—perhaps a disagreement with a fellow Muslim—do you need to practice that same intellectual humility and entrustment to Allah?
?
If someone asked you, 'Do you believe humans are superior to angels?', would you feel compelled to answer with yes or no? How does this passage free you from insisting on certainty where Allah has not given it?

The Proof of Human Origin: Why Revelation Alone Suffices
Buti explains the epistemological basis for proving human origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the origin of humanity can only be proven through authentic transmitted reports (mutawatir), not through sensory experience.

Core Idea
Human origin is ancient history — only revelation can tell us.

Buti begins by establishing the epistemological category of the question of human origin. Since it is a matter of ancient history, it cannot be subjected to empirical testing. The only valid proof is a truthful, widely transmitted report (al-khabar al-sadiq al-mutawatir). This lesson explains that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to absorb Buti's argument about the mode of proof.
Notice how he distinguishes historical matters from sensory ones.
2
Identify the epistemological claim
Buti says the proof is 'confined to reliance on the truthful, mutawatir report'. Why? Because it is not a sensory matter.
This is the key insight: historical facts cannot be tested in a lab.
3
Reflect on the implications
Ask yourself: if someone demanded empirical proof for human creation, how would you respond based on this passage?
The answer is that such proof is impossible by nature; revelation is the only path.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ب - الإنسان مخلوق ) من حيث الجنس ( من تراب ومتكاثر ) من حيث المصدر ( من الإنسان الأول آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام . واعلم أن البرهان على هذه الحقيقة ، محصور في اعتماد الخبر الصادق المتواتر . إذ هي ليست من المسائل المتعلقة بالحسيات حتى تخضع لدليل التجربة والمشاهدة . وإنما هي منبثقة عن خبر يتعلق بتاريخ قديم . فلا مطمع . للتحقق منها . بأكثر من التحقيق في الخبر نفسه فأما أن الإنسان مخلوق ) من حيث جنسه ( من عنصر التراب ، فقد دلت على ذلك آيات صريحة وكثيرة في كتاب الله عز وجل . فمنها قوله عز وجل ﴿ مِنها خَلَقناكُمْ ، وفيها نُعِيدُكُمْ ، وَمِنها نُخْرِجُكُم تارَةٌ أخرى ) [ طه : ٥٥] وقوله عز وجل ﴿ وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا الإِنسانَ مِن صَلْصَالٍ مِّن حَمَإٍ مسنون ﴾ [ الحجر : ٢٦] وقوله تعالى خلق الإنسان من كالفخار ﴾ [ الرحمن : ١٤ ] . صلصال والصلصال طين يبس فهو يتصلصل أي يصوّت كأنه الفخار أي الطين المشوي . والحماً طين أسود متغير ، والمسنون أي المصوّر صورة إنسان . فالصلصال تفسير الجنس التراب ؛ والحمأ المسنون تفسير الجنس الصلصال . كما تقول : أخذت هذا من رجل من العرب من الشام) . وأما أنه متكاثر من آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وأنه الإنسان الأول ، فقد دلت على ذلك أيضاً آيات صريحة وكثيرة في كتاب الله تعالى . تقرأ هذه الآيات في قصة خلق آدم التي تكررت كثيراً في الكتاب المبين
B - Man is created (in terms of genus) from dust and multiplied (in terms of origin) from the first man Adam, peace be upon him. Know that the proof for this truth is confined to reliance on the truthful, mutawatir report. For it is not among the matters related to sensory things so that it would be subject to the evidence of experiment and observation. Rather, it emerges from a report related to ancient history. So there is no hope of verifying it beyond investigation of the report itself. As for that man is created (in terms of his genus) from the element of dust, then numerous explicit verses in the Book of God Almighty indicate that. Among them is His saying, 'From it We created you, and into it We will return you, and from it We will bring you out another time' [Ta-Ha 55]; and His saying, 'Indeed, We created man from sounding clay of altered black mud' [Al-Hijr 26]; and His saying, 'He created man from clay like pottery' [Ar-Rahman 14]. صلصال (sounding clay): dried clay that makes a sound like pottery, meaning baked clay; حمأ (altered mud): black, changed mud; مسنون (molded): meaning formed into the image of a man. So الصلصال is an interpretation of the genus of dust; and الحمأ المسنون is an interpretation of the genus of الصلصال. Just as you say: I took this from a man from the Arabs from Syria. And as for that he is multiplied from Adam, peace be upon him, and that he is the first man, then that is also indicated by numerous explicit verses in the Book of God Almighty. You read these verses in the story of the creation of Adam which is repeated often in the Clear Book.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage classifies human origin under two aspects: genus (creation from dust) and source (multiplication from Adam). The proof for both relies solely on authentic transmitted reports (al-khabar al-sadiq al-mutawatir) because these are historical matters inaccessible to sensory experience. The author then cites Quranic verses for creation from dust and explains the terms (salsal, hama' masnun, etc.) as interpretations of the dust element. For descent from Adam, the Quranic story repeated in many places is sufficient evidence.

Key Terms
الخبر الصادق المتواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human origin can be proven through scientific experimentation or philosophical reasoning alone.
Correction: Buti argues that human origin is a historical matter inaccessible to sensory evidence; only authentic transmitted reports (mutawatir) can establish it.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what type of evidence establishes the fact of human origin?
A) Rational demonstration
B) Empirical experiment
C) Authentic transmitted reports (mutawatir)
D) Consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
Human origin is a historical fact known only through authentic revelation, not empirical science.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own existence, do you genuinely rest on the Quranic account of your origin from dust and Adam, or do you find yourself looking to scientific theories for validation? What does that reveal about the depth of your trust in Allah's word?
?
Buti argues that only a mutawatir report can settle ancient history. If you truly believe the Quran is that report, how should it affect the way you view your life's purpose and ultimate accountability? Are you living as if that report is the most certain thing in your life?
?
You have never seen Adam or the creation from dust, yet you claim to believe it. Is that belief merely intellectual assent, or does it shape your humility, your gratitude, and your sense of being a creature? When was the last time you thanked Allah for creating you from humble dust?

The Quranic Evidence: Humanity Created from Dust and Descended from Adam
Buti cites Quranic verses for creation from dust and descent from Adam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the Quranic verses that prove humanity's creation from dust and descent from the first man, Adam, and understand the interpretation of key terms like salsal and hama' masnun.

Core Idea
The Quran clearly confirms both human creation from dust and descent from Adam.

After establishing the proof method, Buti now presents the specific Quranic verses that testify to two truths: that humanity as a race was created from dust, and that all humans come from the first man, Adam. This lesson examines those verses and the explanation of key terms.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses cited
Buti cites three verses about creation from dust. Read them in Arabic and translation.
Notice the different descriptions: dust, sounding clay, altered black mud.
2
Understand the terminology
Buti explains that salsal (sounding clay) interprets the genus of dust, and hama' masnun interprets salsal. They are layered descriptions.
The terms are not contradictory but complementary.
3
See the evidence for descent from Adam
Buti states that numerous verses indicate multiplication from Adam, specifically the repeated story of Adam's creation.
He does not quote them all but refers to the Quranic narrative.
4
Reflect on the proof structure
Ask: how does the Quran prove both claims? Through explicit verses for creation from dust, and the repeated account of Adam for descent.
Both rely on the mutawatir nature of the Quran.

ب - الإنسان مخلوق ) من حيث الجنس ( من تراب ومتكاثر ) من حيث المصدر ( من الإنسان الأول آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام . واعلم أن البرهان على هذه الحقيقة ، محصور في اعتماد الخبر الصادق المتواتر . إذ هي ليست من المسائل المتعلقة بالحسيات حتى تخضع لدليل التجربة والمشاهدة . وإنما هي منبثقة عن خبر يتعلق بتاريخ قديم . فلا مطمع . للتحقق منها . بأكثر من التحقيق في الخبر نفسه فأما أن الإنسان مخلوق ) من حيث جنسه ( من عنصر التراب ، فقد دلت على ذلك آيات صريحة وكثيرة في كتاب الله عز وجل . فمنها قوله عز وجل ﴿ مِنها خَلَقناكُمْ ، وفيها نُعِيدُكُمْ ، وَمِنها نُخْرِجُكُم تارَةٌ أخرى ) [ طه : ٥٥] وقوله عز وجل ﴿ وَلَقَدْ خَلَقْنَا الإِنسانَ مِن صَلْصَالٍ مِّن حَمَإٍ مسنون ﴾ [ الحجر : ٢٦] وقوله تعالى خلق الإنسان من كالفخار ﴾ [ الرحمن : ١٤ ] . صلصال والصلصال طين يبس فهو يتصلصل أي يصوّت كأنه الفخار أي الطين المشوي . والحماً طين أسود متغير ، والمسنون أي المصوّر صورة إنسان . فالصلصال تفسير الجنس التراب ؛ والحمأ المسنون تفسير الجنس الصلصال . كما تقول : أخذت هذا من رجل من العرب من الشام) . وأما أنه متكاثر من آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وأنه الإنسان الأول ، فقد دلت على ذلك أيضاً آيات صريحة وكثيرة في كتاب الله تعالى . تقرأ هذه الآيات في قصة خلق آدم التي تكررت كثيراً في الكتاب المبين
B - Man is created (in terms of genus) from dust and multiplied (in terms of origin) from the first man Adam, peace be upon him. Know that the proof for this truth is confined to reliance on the truthful, mutawatir report. For it is not among the matters related to sensory things so that it would be subject to the evidence of experiment and observation. Rather, it emerges from a report related to ancient history. So there is no hope of verifying it beyond investigation of the report itself. As for that man is created (in terms of his genus) from the element of dust, then numerous explicit verses in the Book of God Almighty indicate that. Among them is His saying, 'From it We created you, and into it We will return you, and from it We will bring you out another time' [Ta-Ha 55]; and His saying, 'Indeed, We created man from sounding clay of altered black mud' [Al-Hijr 26]; and His saying, 'He created man from clay like pottery' [Ar-Rahman 14]. صلصال (sounding clay): dried clay that makes a sound like pottery, meaning baked clay; حمأ (altered mud): black, changed mud; مسنون (molded): meaning formed into the image of a man. So الصلصال is an interpretation of the genus of dust; and الحمأ المسنون is an interpretation of the genus of الصلصال. Just as you say: I took this from a man from the Arabs from Syria. And as for that he is multiplied from Adam, peace be upon him, and that he is the first man, then that is also indicated by numerous explicit verses in the Book of God Almighty. You read these verses in the story of the creation of Adam which is repeated often in the Clear Book.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage classifies human origin under two aspects: genus (creation from dust) and source (multiplication from Adam). The proof for both relies solely on authentic transmitted reports (al-khabar al-sadiq al-mutawatir) because these are historical matters inaccessible to sensory experience. The author then cites Quranic verses for creation from dust and explains the terms (salsal, hama' masnun, etc.) as interpretations of the dust element. For descent from Adam, the Quranic story repeated in many places is sufficient evidence.

Key Terms

حمأ مسنون

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The multiple Quranic descriptions of human creation (dust, clay, sounding clay) contradict each other.
Correction: Buti shows they are complementary: each term interprets the previous one, like specifying 'a man from the Arabs from Syria'.

Checkpoint

A) Dried clay that makes a sound
B) Black, changed mud molded into human form
C) Pottery-like clay
D) Simple dust

Key Takeaway
The Quran provides explicit, layered evidence that humanity was created from dust and descends from Adam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your body was shaped from dust and will return to it. Does your daily life reflect that you are a fragile creation owned by God, or do you act as if you are permanent and self-sufficient? What will you change today to remember your origin?
?

If He cared so precisely about your physical form, how much more does He care about your spiritual purpose? The Nested Explanation of Creation Materials
Explanation of the nested relationship between Quranic terms for human creation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic terms for human creation (صلصال, حمأ مسنون, تراب) relate to each other as sequential explanations of the same original substance.

Core Idea
The Quranic terms for human creation are nested explanations, not contradictions.

This passage clarifies a common confusion: why does the Quran use different terms for the material of human creation? Rather than contradictions, these terms are sequential specifications. Let's explore how the author explains this relationship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage once
Read the Arabic and translation to get a sense of the author's argument.
2
Identify the three terms
Find the terms تراب, صلصال, and حمأ مسنون in the passage. Notice how the author explains their relationship.
The author uses the word 'تفسير' (explanation) for each.
3
Understand the linguistic analogy
The author gives an example: 'I took this from a man from the Arabs of Syria.' This shows how each term specifies the previous. Relate this to the creation terms.
4
Reflect on the doctrinal implication
This explanation shows that the Quran is consistent. There is no contradiction between dust and clay.
This guards against misunderstandings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالصلصال تفسير الجنس التراب ؛ والحمأ المسنون تفسير الجنس الصلصال . كما تقول : أخذت هذا من رجل من العرب من الشام)
.
وأما أنه متكاثر من آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام ، وأنه الإنسان الأول ، فقد دلت على ذلك أيضاً آيات صريحة وكثيرة في كتاب الله تعالى . تقرأ هذه الآيات في قصة خلق آدم التي تكررت كثيراً في الكتاب المبين
Thus, صلصال is an explanation of the genus dust; and حمأ مسنون is an explanation of the genus صلصال. Just as you say: 'I took this from a man from the Arabs of Syria.'
And as for the fact that he (mankind) is multiplied from Adam, peace be upon him, and that he is the first human, then that is also indicated by clear and numerous verses in the Book of God Almighty. You read these verses in the story of the creation of Adam, which is repeated many times in the Clear Book.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage provides two interconnected doctrinal affirmations about human creation. First, it explains the relationship between the different terms used in the Quran for the material of human creation: تراب (dust), صلصال (clay), and حمأ مسنون (mud). The author asserts that these are not separate creations but sequential explanations: صلصال explains the genus dust, and حمأ مسنون explains the genus صلصال. He gives a linguistic analogy: just as one might say 'I took this from a man from the Arabs of Syria'—where 'Syria' specifies the type of 'Arab', and 'man' the type of 'human'—so the three terms are nested specifications of the same original substance (dust). Secondly, the passage affirms that all human beings are descendants of Adam, and that Adam is indeed the first human being. This is supported by multiple clear verses of the Quran that recount the creation of Adam. The author does not present a proof from reason here but relies on the explicit testimony of revelation.

Correction: The passage shows these are not different creations but nested explanations: clay (صلصال) is a specific form of dust, and mud (حمأ مسنون) is a specific form of clay.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic terms for human creation are nested specifications, not different creations.

Human Creation: Best Form Since the Beginning
Affirms human creation in best form from origin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrinal position that human beings have been created in the best form from the very beginning, based on definitive textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
Humans have always been in their best form — no evolution from lesser forms.

This passage establishes a key Islamic creedal point: the human being was created in the most perfect appearance from the very start. While the topic of humanity's first origin cannot be settled by empirical science, the mutawatir (mass-transmitted) revelation provides certainty. We'll examine the Quranic verses and the hadith that affirm this truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the English translation. Notice the author's emphasis on certainty through revelation.
2
Understand the epistemological claim
The author argues that the origin of humanity cannot be known through sensory experience or rational deduction; only a mutawatir report provides certainty. Reflect on why this matters for creed.
Empirical proofs are limited for historical matters.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Examine verse 95:4 and 82:6-7. Note that the definite article 'al-' in 'al-insan' indicates generality (all humans). Also note the description of being 'balanced' (fa'adala-k) meaning upright and erect.
These verses directly affirm the best form.
4
Interpret the hadith on Adam's image
The hadith 'God created Adam in his image' is explained by the author as meaning Adam had the same form from creation onward, not that he was created in God's image. Pay attention to the pronoun reference.
The pronoun 'his' refers to Adam, not God.
5
Reflect on the refutation of evolution
The passage implicitly refutes any theory that humans evolved from other forms. Consider how this doctrinal point relates to the scientific theory of evolution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإنسان مخلوق منذ النشأة الأولى في أتم مظهر وأحسن تقويم :
والحديث عن النشأة الأولى للإنسان ، لا يخضع هو الآخر لبراهين التجربة والمشاهدة المحسوسة ، إذ هو في جملته حديث تاريخي لن تستطيع أن تعمل فيه الفكر والنظر بأكثر من دليلي التوسم والاسترداد ، وهما دليلان وهميان كما سبق أن أوضحنا ذلك ، يستحيل إقامة عقيدة قطعية على شيء من نتائجها .
•
ولو أن الله عز وجل لم يحدثنا بشيء قطعي في هذا الصدد ، لما التزمنا في شأنه بأي حكم نعتقده ونقطع به
ولكن الخبر الصادق المتواتر ، وضعنا في ذلك أمام مالا مجال للشك أو الظن فيه . وهو قوله تعالى : ( لقد خلقنا الإنسان في أحسَن تقويم ﴾ [ التين : ٤ ] و « أل » الداخلة على الإنسان للاستغراق كما هو معلوم ، فهي عامة للأفراد كلهم .. ومثل ذلك قوله تعالى و يا أيها الإنسانُ ماغَرَّكَ بِرَبِّكَ الكَرِيمِ الَّذِي خَلَقَكَ فَسَوَّاكَ فَعَدَلَكَ ﴾ [ الانفطار : ٦ - ٧] أي جعلك سوياً مستقيماً معتدل القامة منتصبها في أحسن الهيئات والأشكال.
ومن مؤكدات هذه الحقيقة التي قررها القرآن ، ماروي في الصحيحين عن أبي هريرة رضي الله عنه أن رسول الله قال : « خلق الله آدم على صورته .. » أي أنه منذ خُلق إنما كانت صورته هي الصورة ذاتها التي استمر عليها وعرف بها ، أي لم يُنَشَّأ متنقلاً من شكل إلى آخر . فالضمير في صورته راجع إلى آدم
Man is created from the very first origin in the most complete appearance and best form.
And the discourse about the first origin of man is likewise not subject to proofs of experiment and sensory observation, for it is in its entirety an historical discourse, concerning which the intellect and consideration cannot make use of more than the two proofs of conjecture and inference, which are illusory proofs as we have explained, and it is impossible to establish a definitive creed based on any of their results.
And if God Almighty had not told us something definitive in this regard, we would not have committed ourselves to any ruling that we believe and are certain of.
But the truthful, mutawatir report placed us before that which has no room for doubt or suspicion. That is His saying: 'Indeed, We have created man in the best form' (Quran 95:4), and the definite article (al-) entering upon man is for generality, as is known, meaning it is general for all individuals. And similar to that is His saying: 'O man! What has deceived you about your Noble Lord, who created you, then proportioned you, then balanced you?' (Quran 82:6-7), meaning He made you upright, straight, moderate in stature, erect in the best of forms and shapes.
And among the confirmations of this reality which the Quran has established is what is narrated in the two Sahihs from Abu Huraira that the Messenger of God said: 'God created Adam in his image' – meaning that from the time he was created, his image was the very image which he continued upon and by which he was known, i.e., he was not brought up transitioning from one form to another. The pronoun in 'his image' refers to Adam.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage affirms the Islamic doctrine that the human being has been created in the most perfect form and best appearance from the very beginning of creation. The author first notes that the topic of the first origin of man is not subject to empirical proof; it is a historical narrative where only conjectural methods (توسم and استرداد) could be used, which are illusory. Thus, without definitive revelation, no certain creed could be established. However, God has provided a mutawatir (mass-transmitted) report that leaves no room for doubt. The key verse is 'Indeed, We have created man in the best form' (Surah at-Tin, ayah 4). The definite article 'al-' in 'al-insan' indicates generality, meaning all human beings are included. Another verse from Surah al-Infitar (82:6-7) emphasizes that God created man and proportioned him upright. Furthermore, the authentic hadith from the two Sahihs reports that 'God created Adam in his image' with the pronoun referring to Adam himself, meaning that from the moment of creation Adam had the same form he continued to have; he did not evolve from other forms. Thus the passage decisively refutes any theory of human evolution from lower beings.

Key Terms
أحسن تقويم
خلق الله آدم على صورته
متواتر
الخبر الصادق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that the hadith 'خلق الله آدم على صورته' means Adam was created in God's image.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the pronoun 'his' refers to Adam himself, meaning Adam was created in his own image that he continued to have.

Checkpoint

A) Adam was created in the image of God
B) Adam was created in his own image, meaning he had the same form from the start
C) Adam was created gradually from other forms
D) Adam's image changed over time

Key Takeaway
The Quran and authentic hadith affirm that humans were created in the best form from the very beginning, without any evolutionary change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that you were created in the best form? How does that affect the way you view your own body and the bodies of others, especially those with disabilities?
?
The passage says without revelation we would have no certainty about our origin. Are there areas in your life where you rely on your own reasoning over God's revealed truth? What is one specific change you will make today to prioritize revelation?
?
If Adam was created in the best form from the beginning, what does that say about modern claims that humans can 'improve' themselves through technology? Are you seeking to 'improve' what God has already made best, or are you trusting His design? What action can you take to show gratitude for your form?

The Definitive Truth of Human Creation
Buti presents the hadith interpretation and the three definitive matters that prove man did not evolve.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the hadith about Adam's creation confirms that humanity did not undergo any evolutionary change, based on three definitive matters about man.

Core Idea
Man was created in the best form from the beginning, not evolved.

Buti begins by examining two interpretations of a key pronoun in a hadith about Adam's creation, showing that both lead to the same conclusion: Adam was created with full honor. From this, he derives three definitive facts about man: his nobility, his origin from dust and from Adam, and his creation in the best form. These three facts produce the certain ruling that man never evolved.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith interpretation
Understand the two views on the pronoun reference (Adam or Allah) and how both confirm honor.
The majority view takes the pronoun back to Adam.
2
Identify the three definitive matters
List the three facts about man that are irrevocably established: nobility, creation from dust, and best form.
These are taken from Quran and hadith.
3
Connect to evolutionary change
See how these three facts collectively rule out any evolutionary progression from one species to another.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهناك رأي آخر، يرى أن الضمير راجع إلى ذات الله تعالى، والمقصود بالصورة الصفة، أي خلقه عالماً مريداً حكيماً سميعاً بصيراً.. وتلك صفات هي الله تعالى (انظر ص ۱۳۸ من هذا الكتاب). وسواء أعدت الضمير على آدم، كما هو رأي الجمهور ويدل عليه ظاهر الحديث، أو أعدته إلى ذات الله تعالى، فالحديث تأكيد للدلالة القطعية في القرآن، إذ البحث في معرض بيان تكريم الله لآدم منذ أول خلقه. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك، وجب أن نعلم بأن الإنسان لم يتنقل خلال تاريخه كله، في أي تطور نوعي. كأن يقال إنه ترقى من فصيلة إلى أخرى، أو تدرج من مظهر نوعي في الهيئة والشكل إلى مظهر آخر. وهذا الحكم نتيجة قطعية للأمور الثلاثة التي ذكرناها عن الإنسان، وهي: أنه أفضل المخلوقات وأشرفها، وأنه مخلوق من التراب، ومتكاثر من آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام، وأنه خلق (في نشأته الأولى) في أحسن تقويم.

مصير نظرية النشوء والارتقاء أمام هذه الحقيقة
وكما ترى، فإن هذه الحقيقة القطعية التي يجب على المسلم الاعتقاد بها تتناقض مناقضة كلية مع ما يسمى بنظرية النشوء والارتقاء، التي تتبنى فرضية تاريخية أخرى عن الإنسان، وهي أنه تسلسل ضمن حلقات مختلفة من التطور النوعي، تدرج فيها من البسيط إلى المعقد، ومن البدائية إلى الرقي، في كل من الشكل والفكر معاً. فما موقف المسلم من هذا التناقض والخلاف؟ والجواب: أن موقفه ينبغي أن يكون الموقف ذاته الذي يتخذه أي عاقل لدى تناقض حقيقة علمية مع مسألة نظرية. إذ لا ريب أن الحقيقة العلمية هي التي ينبغي أن يكتب لها البقاء، ولا مناص من نسخ النظرية مادامت مناقضة لتلك الحقيقة لا يمكن جمعها معها.
وعلينا الآن أن نوضح (مجدداً) كيف أن الحكم الذي ذكرناه عن واقع الإنسان، حقيقة علمية ثابتة، بينما الحكم بتطور الإنسان تطوراً نوعياً مجرد نظرية بل فرضية ليس من حولها أي برهان علمي.
وينبغي أن تعلم أولاً، أن هذه المسألة ليست مما يتعلق بالمحسوسات والمشاهدات، فلا مطمع في أن تبحث لها عن دليل من التجربة المحسوسة المشاهدة. ذلك لأن البحث ليس متعلقاً بالإنسان الحالي، حتى يكون الموضوع خاضعاً لمجهر التجربة والمشاهدة، وإنما هو متعلق باكتشاف ناحية تاريخية فيه، مرت وانطوت. وكل ما يمكن الاستعانة به في البحث، من المستحاثات ووجوه الشبه بين الإنسان وحيوانات أخرى وغير ذلك، إنما هو من وسائل البحث.
There is another opinion, which holds that the pronoun refers to the Essence of Allah the Exalted, and by 'image' is meant the attribute, i.e., He created him knowing, willing, wise, hearing, seeing... and those attributes are Allah the Exalted (see p. 138 of this book). Whether the pronoun is referred back to Adam, as is the view of the majority and indicated by the apparent meaning of the hadith, or referred back to the Essence of Allah the Exalted, the hadith is a confirmation of the definitive indication in the Quran, since the discussion is in the context of explaining Allah's honoring of Adam from the beginning of his creation. If this is the case, then we must know that man did not, throughout his entire history, undergo any evolutionary change, such that it is said that he advanced from one species to another, or progressed from one form in appearance and shape to another. And this ruling is a definitive result of the three matters we have mentioned about man, namely: that he is the best and most noble of creatures, that he is created from dust and multiplied from Adam (peace be upon him), and that he was created (in his first origin) in the best form. The fate of the theory of evolution in the face of this truth. As you see, this definitive truth that the Muslim must believe totally contradicts what is called the theory of evolution, which adopts another historical hypothesis about man, namely that he is a sequence within different rings of evolutionary change, progressing from simple to complex, and from primitiveness to advancement, in both form and thought together. So what is the Muslim's position regarding this contradiction and conflict? The answer: that his position should be the very position that any rational person takes when a scientific truth contradicts a theoretical issue. For there is no doubt that the scientific truth is what should endure, and there is no escape from abrogating the theory as long as it contradicts that truth and cannot be reconciled with it. And we must now (again) clarify how the ruling we mentioned about the reality of man is a fixed scientific truth, while the ruling about man's evolutionary development is merely a theory, indeed a hypothesis, around which there is no scientific proof. And you should first know that this issue is not among the sensory and observable matters, so there is no hope of finding for it evidence from observable sensory experience. That is because the research is not about present-day man, such that the subject could be subjected to the microscope of experience and observation, but rather it is about discovering a historical aspect of him that has passed and vanished. And all that can be used in research, from fossils and similarities between man and other animals and so on, are only means of research.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage is a combined argument and refutation. It first discusses two interpretations of a pronoun in a hadith about the creation of Adam: either referring to Adam or to Allah. In both cases, the hadith confirms the Quran's definitive indication of Adam's honor from the beginning. The author then draws a conclusion: if Adam was created with full honor and dignity, then humanity did not undergo any evolutionary change; man did not advance from one species to another or change form. This is presented as a definitive result based on three facts: (1) man is the best and most noble of creatures, (2) he was created from dust and multiplied from Adam, and (3) he was created in the best form initially. The second part of the passage addresses the conflict between this definitive truth and the theory of evolution. The author states that the Muslim must hold to the definitive truth, rejecting the theory because it is merely a hypothesis without scientific proof. He clarifies that this issue is not observable or testable by experiment, as it concerns a past historical aspect. Fossils and similarities between species are only means of research, not conclusive proof. Therefore, the correct stance is to abrogate the theory in favor of the definitive truth.

Key Terms
الضمير
الصورة
أحسن تقويم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The debate over the pronoun in the hadith allows for different meanings that could accommodate evolution.
Correction: Buti shows that both interpretations lead to the same conclusion: Adam was created with full honor, which is incompatible with evolution.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, how many definitive matters about man are mentioned as the basis for rejecting evolution?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The three definitive matters about man's creation—nobility, origin from dust and Adam, and best form—make it impossible for evolutionary change to have occurred.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that man was created in the best form from the beginning, how does that affect your view of your own worth and purpose? Are you living in a way that honors that original creation?
?
Buti argues that the three definitive matters make it impossible for man to have evolved. Reflect on your own life: are you 'evolving' morally away from that best form, or are you actively striving to return to it?
?
The hadith interpretations both confirm that Adam was honored from the start. Do you treat your own beginning—your birth, your fitrah—as something to be preserved and honored, or do you allow society to convince you that you must 'evolve' into something else?

Rejecting the Theory of Evolution
Buti explains the total contradiction and urges the Muslim to reject evolution as an unproven hypothesis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Muslim's stance when a definitive truth conflicts with a theory like evolution, and why evolution is considered an unproven hypothesis.

Core Idea
Definitive truth abrogates theory; evolution is a hypothesis lacking proof.

Having established the definitive truth about human creation, Buti now confronts the theory of evolution. He states that this truth and the theory are in total contradiction. The Muslim's position must be to uphold the definitive truth and reject the theory, as any rational person would when a proven fact conflicts with a mere hypothesis. He emphasizes that the issue is not observable by experiment, so fossils and similarities are only research tools, not proofs.

Guided Path
1
Understand the contradiction
Buti declares that the definitive truth about man totally contradicts the theory of evolution.
2
Identify the rational stance
A rational person abrogates the theory in favor of the definitive truth, not the other way around.
This is a general principle.
3
Recognize evolution as hypothesis
Evolution is not a scientific proof but a hypothesis; it lacks conclusive evidence.
Buti notes that the matter is historical, not observable, so fossils are only aids.

Source Text

?

?
The passage says that any rational person would uphold a scientific truth over a theory. Do you truly hold the Islamic belief about human creation as an unshakeable truth? Or is it merely a belief you hold culturally? Ask yourself: would you be willing to lose intellectual credibility to defend this truth?

Lamarck's Mechanism of Evolution
Defines Lamarckism and presents its causal mechanism with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Lamarck's proposed mechanism for how species change over time, including the role of environmental factors, habits, and the example of organ atrophy.

Core Idea
Lamarck believed environment drives habit changes that gradually reshape physical form.

Lamarck was among the first to propose a systematic mechanism for evolution. He argued that species are not fixed but transform gradually in response to their environments. The passage outlines his core idea: changes in circumstances lead to changes in habits, which over time alter bodily functions and eventually the organs themselves. Let's examine this causal chain and the examples he used.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of Lamarckism
Start by reading the Arabic passage that defines Lamarckism. Notice how it begins with 'اللاماركية :' and explains the instability of species due to varying circumstances.
Pay attention to the causal sequence: circumstances -> habits -> functions -> form.
2
Identify the causal chain
The passage describes a step-by-step process: change in circumstances leads to change in habits, which with continuity leads to change in functions, then with time to change in form and organs. Write down each step.
3
Study the examples
Lamarck provided examples: vertebrates that don't chew (whale, anteater) have atrophied teeth; moles living in darkness have tiny eyes. Ask yourself how these illustrate his mechanism.
These examples are meant to show use and disuse of organs.
4
Reflect on the logic
Consider whether this mechanism seems plausible. Note that Lamarck's theory is now rejected, but it was an early attempt at explaining evolution.
This lesson only covers the mechanism; the next lesson discusses its reception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نموه في حقل الأدلة التي اعتمد عليها ، ثم رجوعه القهقرى إلى حيث الضالة والضعف ، تحت وطأة النقض والنقد اللذين تسارعا إليه من كل جانب

اللاماركية :
ولعل من أسبق هذه النظريات وأهمها ما نادى به العالم التصنيفي لامارك من أن عدم ثبات الأنواع على حالها إنما يعود إلى الظروف المختلفة التي تتقلب على كل منها ، كالإقليم أو الغذاء أو طراز الحياة أو طبيعة المناخ الخ . فاختلاف شيء من هذه الظروف يؤثر في اختلاف العادات ، واختلاف العادات يؤثر - مع الاستمرار - في اختلاف الوظائف والأعمال ، واختلافهما يؤثر - مع الزمن - في اختلاف الشكل والأعضاء .
ولقد دعم لامارك نظريته هذه بعدد من الأمثلة الحية التي استرعت انتباهه ، فالفقاريات التي تتغذى بدون مضغ تضمر أسنانها وتصبح خفية في اللثتين . والحوت وآكل النمل مثالان على ذلك . والخلد الذي يعيش في الظلام يتمتع بعينين صغيرتين جداً لا تكادان تنهضان بوظيفة

وعلى الرغم من أن هذا التحليل الذي تقدم به لامارك ، كتفسير لما فرضه من آلية التطور ، لم ينل في البدء إلا قليلاً من النجاح ، فإنه راح يشع فيما بعد في أذهان الناس ، وراحوا يعتبرونه ، إلى حين من الزمن ، خير تفسير لظاهرة التطور . والتصقت النظرية باسم صاحبها ، فراحوا يطلقون عليها :
اللاماركية
ولكن ما إن وضعت النظرية تحت مجهر البحث والنقد ودلائل التجربة والاستقراء ، حتى انطفأ شعاعها وانكفأت على أعقابها وتقلص ما كان لها من سلطان على الأذهان
His growth in the field of evidence he relied upon, then his retreat back to where misguidance and weakness lie, under the pressure of refutation and criticism that rushed at him from every side.

Lamarckism:
Perhaps one of the earliest and most important of these theories is what the taxonomist Lamarck proclaimed: that the instability of species in their state is due to the different circumstances that change upon each of them, such as climate, food, lifestyle, nature of climate, etc. So a change in any of these circumstances affects a change in habits, and a change in habits affects—with continuity—a change in functions and actions, and their change affects—with time—a change in form and organs.
Lamarck supported his theory with a number of living examples that caught his attention: vertebrates that feed without chewing have teeth that atrophy and become hidden in the gums. The whale and the anteater are two examples of that. And the mole that lives in darkness has very small eyes that can hardly perform their function.

Although this analysis presented by Lamarck, as an explanation for the mechanism of evolution he assumed, initially achieved little success, it later radiated in people's minds, and they came to consider it, for a time, the best explanation for the phenomenon of evolution. The theory stuck to its author's name, and they began to call it: Lamarckism.
But once the theory was placed under the microscope of research and criticism and the evidence of experiment and induction, its radiance faded, it retreated on its heels, and its sway over minds shrank.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage introduces Lamarck's theory of evolution. It begins with a brief reference to a previous discussion about the growth and decline of a theory. Then it defines Lamarckism: species are not fixed but change due to environmental factors like climate, food, lifestyle, etc. The mechanism is explained stepwise: change in circumstances leads to change in habits, which over time leads to change in functions, and finally change in form and organs. Lamarck provided examples: vertebrates that eat without chewing have atrophied teeth; the whale and anteater; the mole with tiny eyes. The theory initially had little success but later gained popularity as the best explanation for evolution, becoming known as Lamarckism. However, when subjected to scrutiny, it was refuted and lost its influence.

Key Terms
اللاماركية
الظروف
العادات
الوظائف
الشكل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Lamarck believed evolution happens randomly.
Correction: Lamarck proposed a directed mechanism: environmental changes force animals to change habits, which then alter their bodies.

Checkpoint
According to Lamarck, what is the initial trigger for evolutionary change in a species?
A) Random mutations in DNA
B) Changes in environmental circumstances
C) Natural selection of fit individuals
D) The will of the organism

Key Takeaway
Lamarck proposed that species evolve through a causal chain: environmental change alters habits, which over time change functions and eventually physical form.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a habit you have maintained for years—perhaps a good one like gratitude, or a harmful one like procrastination. How has that habit shaped your abilities or even your physical body? If Lamarck is correct about the power of consistent habits to change form, what does that mean for the habits you are choosing today? Will you let your environment passively shape you, or will you intentionally cultivate habits that transform you from the inside out? What one habit will you commit to changing starting now?
?
Lamarck taught that necessity drives adaptation—the environment forces change. In your spiritual life, has adversity forced you to grow, or have you resisted? Consider a recent difficulty: did it change your habits and bring you closer to God, or did it harden you? If you have not changed for the better, what is holding you back? Right now, name one practical habit you can adopt this week that will strengthen your connection to your Creator, and resolve to do it daily.

The Rise and Fall of Lamarckism
Describes the historical acceptance and subsequent decline of Lamarckism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical trajectory of Lamarckism: its initial obscurity, later acceptance, and eventual refutation under scientific scrutiny.

Core Idea
Lamarckism was once the best explanation for evolution but was later abandoned due to lack of evidence.

The previous lesson introduced Lamarck's mechanism. Now we see how the theory fared historically. Initially ignored, it later gained popularity and even became synonymous with evolution for a time. However, when tested, it was found lacking and eventually rejected by the scientific community.

Guided Path
1
Read about the theory's initial reception
The passage says it 'initially achieved little success' but later 'radiated in people's minds'. Note the shift from obscurity to popularity.
2
Understand why it became popular
It was considered the best explanation for evolution for a while. The theory became attached to Lamarck's name.
This shows that a theory can be influential despite later being wrong.
3
See the fall
When subjected to research and experiment, the theory faded and lost its influence. This is a cautionary tale about scientific verification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نموه في حقل الأدلة التي اعتمد عليها ، ثم رجوعه القهقرى إلى حيث الضالة والضعف ، تحت وطأة النقض والنقد اللذين تسارعا إليه من كل جانب

اللاماركية :
ولعل من أسبق هذه النظريات وأهمها ما نادى به العالم التصنيفي لامارك من أن عدم ثبات الأنواع على حالها إنما يعود إلى الظروف المختلفة التي تتقلب على كل منها ، كالإقليم أو الغذاء أو طراز الحياة أو طبيعة المناخ الخ . فاختلاف شيء من هذه الظروف يؤثر في اختلاف العادات ، واختلاف العادات يؤثر - مع الاستمرار - في اختلاف الوظائف والأعمال ، واختلافهما يؤثر - مع الزمن - في اختلاف الشكل والأعضاء .
ولقد دعم لامارك نظريته هذه بعدد من الأمثلة الحية التي استرعت انتباهه ، فالفقاريات التي تتغذى بدون مضغ تضمر أسنانها وتصبح خفية في اللثتين . والحوت وآكل النمل مثالان على ذلك . والخلد الذي يعيش في الظلام يتمتع بعينين صغيرتين جداً لا تكادان تنهضان بوظيفة

وعلى الرغم من أن هذا التحليل الذي تقدم به لامارك ، كتفسير لما فرضه من آلية التطور ، لم ينل في البدء إلا قليلاً من النجاح ، فإنه راح يشع فيما بعد في أذهان الناس ، وراحوا يعتبرونه ، إلى حين من الزمن ، خير تفسير لظاهرة التطور . والتصقت النظرية باسم صاحبها ، فراحوا يطلقون عليها :
اللاماركية
ولكن ما إن وضعت النظرية تحت مجهر البحث والنقد ودلائل التجربة والاستقراء ، حتى انطفأ شعاعها وانكفأت على أعقابها وتقلص ما كان لها من سلطان على الأذهان
His growth in the field of evidence he relied upon, then his retreat back to where misguidance and weakness lie, under the pressure of refutation and criticism that rushed at him from every side.

Lamarckism:
Perhaps one of the earliest and most important of these theories is what the taxonomist Lamarck proclaimed: that the instability of species in their state is due to the different circumstances that change upon each of them, such as climate, food, lifestyle, nature of climate, etc. So a change in any of these circumstances affects a change in habits, and a change in habits affects—with continuity—a change in functions and actions, and their change affects—with time—a change in form and organs.
Lamarck supported his theory with a number of living examples that caught his attention: vertebrates that feed without chewing have teeth that atrophy and become hidden in the gums. The whale and the anteater are two examples of that. And the mole that lives in darkness has very small eyes that can hardly perform their function.

Although this analysis presented by Lamarck, as an explanation for the mechanism of evolution he assumed, initially achieved little success, it later radiated in people's minds, and they came to consider it, for a time, the best explanation for the phenomenon of evolution. The theory stuck to its author's name, and they began to call it: Lamarckism.
But once the theory was placed under the microscope of research and criticism and the evidence of experiment and induction, its radiance faded, it retreated on its heels, and its sway over minds shrank.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage introduces Lamarck's theory of evolution. It begins with a brief reference to a previous discussion about the growth and decline of a theory. Then it defines Lamarckism: species are not fixed but change due to environmental factors like climate, food, lifestyle, etc. The mechanism is explained stepwise: change in circumstances leads to change in habits, which over time leads to change in functions, and finally change in form and organs. Lamarck provided examples: vertebrates that eat without chewing have atrophied teeth; the whale and anteater; the mole with tiny eyes. The theory initially had little success but later gained popularity as the best explanation for evolution, becoming known as Lamarckism. However, when subjected to scrutiny, it was refuted and lost its influence.

التطور
النقض
النقد

Misconception: Lamarckism was always accepted after Darwin.
Correction: Lamarckism predated Darwin and later fell out of favor; it was never universally accepted.

Checkpoint

B) It was confirmed
C) It lost its radiance and influence

Key Takeaway
Lamarckism rose from obscurity to become the leading evolutionary theory of its time, only to be rejected when empirical evidence failed to support it.

Imagine you are a scientist who once promoted Lamarckism. When the evidence turned against your theory, would you have the humility to 'retreat on your heels' and abandon it? What attachments in your own life might prevent you from changing your mind when faced with truth?

First Critique of Lamarckism: Extinction as a Counterexample
First critique: extinction contradicts Lamarck's assumption of guaranteed survival.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the observed phenomenon of extinction undermines Lamarck's core assumption that evolution always leads to better adaptation and survival.

Core Idea
Extinction proves that evolution does not guarantee survival.

Lamarck's theory of evolution assumed that organisms always evolve in ways that benefit their survival and maintain harmony with their environment. But if that were always true, why do species go extinct? In this passage, al-Būṭī presents a straightforward critique: the observable fact of extinction contradicts Lamarck's optimistic view of evolution.

Guided Path
1
Understand Lamarck's assumption
Read the passage's opening sentences that describe what Lamarck's theory implies: evolution is always beneficial, ensuring survival and harmony with nature.
Notice the phrase 'مقتضى ما يراه لامارك' — the necessary implication of his view.
2
Identify the counterevidence
The passage then states 'غير أن الواقع المشاهد لم يثبت استمرار هذا السير' and gives the example of extinction. Identify that this is a direct contradiction.
3
Analyze why extinction is contradictory
According to Lamarck, if conditions change, organisms should evolve to adapt. But extinction shows they did not. Ask: why does this disprove the assumption?
The passage says 'وقد كان من مقتضى افتراضات لامارك أن تتطور...' — but they didn't.
4
Summarize the critique in your own words
Write a one-sentence summary of the first critique: Lamarck says evolution ensures survival; extinction shows it does not.

أولاً - مقتضى ما يراه لامارك ، أن سير التطور يتجه إلى فائدة الحيوان وضمان استمراره في عمله الوظيفي ، والحفاظ على أكبر قدر من التناسق بينه وبين أحوال الطبيعة مهما اختلفت وتطورت ؛ ولقد لاحظنا ذلك من الأمثلة التي استند إليها

غير أن الواقع المشاهد لم يثبت استمرار هذا السير . فإن أنواعاً كثيرة من الحيوانات قد انقرضت وبادت تحت وطأة ما يسمى بالعوامل الطبيعية ، وقد كان من مقتضى افتراضات لامارك أن تتطور تلك الحيوانات وفقاً لاختلاف الأحوال الطبيعية ، وما يتقلب عليها من طوارئ الظروف والأجواء والبيئات ، بحيث تضمن لنفسها استمرار البقاء النوعي على أقل تقدير
Critique of Lamarckism:
We will now enumerate some of the criticisms directed at it:

First: The implication of what Lamarck holds is that the course of evolution is directed toward the benefit of the animal, guaranteeing its continuation in its functional work, and preserving the greatest degree of harmony between it and the conditions of nature, however much they differ and evolve; and we have observed that from the examples he relied upon.
But observed reality has not proven the continuation of this course. For many species of animals have become extinct and perished under the pressure of so-called natural factors, whereas Lamarck's assumptions would require that those animals evolve according to the changing natural conditions and the vicissitudes of circumstances, atmospheres, and environments that befall them, so as to ensure for themselves the continuation of species survival, at the very least.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage presents the first critique of Lamarckism. It first sets up the heading 'Critique of Lamarckism' and states that some criticisms will be enumerated. The first objection is that Lamarck's theory implies evolution always benefits the animal, ensuring its survival and harmony with nature. However, observed reality does not support this: many species have gone extinct due to natural factors. If Lamarck's assumptions were correct, those species should have evolved to adapt to changing conditions and thus avoid extinction. The fact that they did not contradicts the theory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The argument here is not against evolution itself, but specifically against Lamarck's claim that evolution always ensures survival and adaptation.

Key Takeaway
Extinction shows that evolution does not always benefit organisms, contradicting Lamarck's core assumption.
