Second Critique of Lamarckism: Inherited Traits Present at Birth
Second objection: many traits are present at birth, not acquired through environmental pressure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why certain traits being present at birth disproves the Lamarckian mechanism of acquired characteristics.

Core Idea
Traits are inherited, not acquired through environmental pressure.

This passage presents the second major critique of Lamarck's theory of evolution. Lamarck observed many traits across species and assumed they developed through environmental pressure. However, the author argues that many of these traits are actually present from birth, meaning they are hereditary and cannot be explained by Lamarckian acquisition. We'll examine several examples that demonstrate this point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a general claim followed by three specific examples. Pay attention to the conclusion.
The passage ends with a concluding statement that we cannot explain these by previous adaptation.
2
Analyze the examples
Each example (child's soles, camel callosities, fetal thigh bones) shows the trait is present at birth. Consider why this contradicts Lamarck's idea that traits develop during life.
3
Understand the argument
The author is not denying that these traits are adaptations, but denying that they are acquired. They are inherited. This refutes the core of Lamarckism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانياً - إن أكثر ما لاحظه لامارك ، من مظاهر التطور التي اعتمدها أساساً لبحثه وميزاناً لفرضيته ، إنما يجري ضمن سلسلة الأفراد ، بعامل الوراثة ، أي من قبل أن يلتقي الحيوان مع الظروف أو البيئة أو الأحوال التي تلجئه إلى نوع من التطور أو التشكل للانسجام معها
فجلد الطفل يكون ، منذ ولادته ، أشد غلظاً على أخمص القدمين منه في أي جهة أخرى من أجزاء الجسم
وللجمال ثفنات تقع في سويات رسغ اليدين والمرفق بحيث تطابق السطوح التي تتحمل وطأة الوزن عندما يستنيخ البعير . وتكون هذه الثفنات موجودة في ولد الناقة منذ ولادته
وتتجه الامتدادات العظمية في عظام الفخذ في جنين الإنسان ، كما تتجه في البالغ المكتمل، أي وفقاً لاتجاه الضغوط التي تطرأ على العظام عند المشي
ولا يمكننا في مثل هذه الأحوال أن نعلل الأمر بتكييف سابق تأثير
Second: The majority of what Lamarck observed, of the manifestations of evolution that he relied upon as a basis for his research and a criterion for his hypothesis, actually occurs within the series of individuals, by the factor of heredity—that is, before the animal meets with the circumstances, environment, or conditions that would compel it to some kind of evolution or formation for adaptation to them.
For the skin of a child, from its birth, is thicker on the soles of the feet than on any other part of the body.
Camels have callosities on the wrists and elbows that correspond to the surfaces that bear the weight when the camel kneels. These callosities exist in the newborn camel since its birth.
The bony extensions in the thigh bones of a human fetus are oriented in the same way as in a fully grown adult—that is, according to the direction of pressures that occur on the bones when walking.
In such cases, we cannot explain the matter by a previous adaptive influence.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents the second critique of Lamarckism. It argues that many of the evolutionary features Lamarck observed are actually inherited and present from birth, not acquired through environmental pressure during the animal's lifetime. Examples include: the thicker skin on the soles of human feet (present from birth), camel callosities (present in newborns), and the orientation of thigh bones in human fetuses (matching that of adults). These traits are hereditary and exist before any interaction with the environment that would supposedly cause them. Therefore, they cannot be explained by Lamarckian acquired characteristics.

Key Terms
الوراثة
التكييف
الثفنات
الامتدادات العظمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think these examples support Lamarck because they show adaptations.
Correction: The author uses them to show the traits are pre-existing, not acquired, thus refuting Lamarck.

Checkpoint

B) They are present from birth, showing they are inherited, not acquired.
C) They are not actually adaptations.
D) They prove Lamarck was right.

Key Takeaway
Lamarck's evidence actually works against him because the traits he observed are hereditary and exist before environmental interaction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a skill or trait you believe you developed through effort. Could it be that some of what you think you acquired was actually a gift from birth? How does this change your sense of gratitude?
?
The passage shows that many traits are predetermined by heredity. If that is true for physical traits, what about your moral character? Could some of your virtues be inherited rather than earned? Does that make you humble or proud?
?
Lamarck's error was assuming that environment shapes everything. Where in your life have you assumed that your circumstances determine your identity, ignoring what you were born with? How can you correct that assumption?

Extinction Refutes Lamarck's Survival Claim
Criticizes Lamarck's claim using extinction as counterevidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the empirical fact of extinction undermines Lamarck's claim that evolution guarantees an animal's survival and functional continuity.

Core Idea
Observed extinction contradicts Lamarck's assumption that evolution always ensures survival.

Lamarck built his theory on examples suggesting evolution proceeds for the animal's benefit, maintaining harmony with nature. But if evolution truly guaranteed survival, why do we find countless extinct species? This lesson examines that contradiction, showing how a clear empirical observation—extinction—challenges the core of Lamarck's hypothesis.

Guided Path
1
Recall Lamarck's core claim
Start by recalling Lamarck's position as summarized: evolution aims at the animal's benefit and ensures its continuity. This sets up the expectation that should be met.
The author says Lamarck's claim is that evolution tends to the benefit of the animal and preserving harmony.
2
Identify the counterevidence
Read the passage to find the key fact the author presents as counterevidence: the extinction of many species under natural factors.
Look for words like 'انقرضت' (became extinct) and 'بادت' (perished).
3
Understand the logical contradiction
Reflect on why extinction contradicts Lamarck's assumptions. According to Lamarck, animals should evolve to adapt to changing conditions and thus survive. Extinction shows this adaptation did not occur.
The author emphasizes that Lamarck's own logic would require at least species-level survival.
4
Formulate the critique in your own words
Summarize the argument: Lamarck's theory predicts adaptation and survival, but the existence of extinction proves that adaptation is not guaranteed, thus the theory is flawed.
You can use the phrase 'البقاء النوعي' (specific survival) as a key term.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولاً - مقتضى ما يراه لامارك ، أن سير التطور يتجه إلى فائدة الحيوان وضمان استمراره في عمله الوظيفي ، والحفاظ على أكبر قدر من التناسق بينه وبين أحوال الطبيعة مهما اختلفت وتطورت ؛ ولقد لاحظنا ذلك من الأمثلة التي استند إليها . غير أن الواقع المشاهد لم يثبت استمرار هذا السير . فإن أنـواعـاً كثيرة من الحيوانات قد انقرضت وبادت تحت وطأة ما يسمى بالعوامل الطبيعية ، وقد كان من مقتضى افتراضات لامارك أن تتطور تلك الحيوانات وفقاً لاختلاف الأحوال الطبيعية ، وما يتقلب عليها من طوارئ الظروف والأجواء والبيئات ، بحيث تضمن لنفسها استمرار البقاء النوعي على أقل تقدير
Firstly - The implication of what Lamarck sees, that the course of evolution tends to the benefit of the animal and ensuring its continuity in its functional work, and preserving the greatest amount of harmony between it and the conditions of nature no matter how they differ and develop; and we have observed that from the examples he relied upon. However, observed reality has not proven the continuity of this course. For many types of animals have become extinct and perished under the weight of so-called natural factors, and it was required by Lamarck's assumptions that those animals should evolve according to the differences in natural conditions, and the changes of circumstances, climates, and environments that befall them, so that they would ensure for themselves the continuation of specific survival at the very least.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is the first critique of Lamarck's evolutionary theory. The author begins by summarizing Lamarck's position: that evolution proceeds for the benefit of the animal, ensuring its functional continuity and harmony with nature regardless of changes. The author acknowledges that Lamarck provided examples to support this. However, the author then presents a decisive counterargument: observed reality does not confirm this continuity. Many species have gone extinct under the pressure of natural factors. According to Lamarck's assumptions, these animals should have evolved to adapt to changing conditions and thus ensure their survival. The fact that they did not contradicts the theory. The phrase 'at the very least' emphasizes that Lamarck's theory would predict at least species-level survival, but extinction shows this prediction fails.

Key Terms

التطور
الانقراض
البقاء النوعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Lamarck claimed all species must necessarily survive, and that extinction disproves his entire theory. In fact, Lamarck argued that adaptation leads to survival, but extinction shows that adaptation does not always occur, not that survival is impossible.
Correction: The passage corrects this by showing that Lamarck's own logic would require at least species-level survival given adaptation, but extinction proves that adaptation did not happen for those species, thus the theory's mechanism is incomplete.

?
Lamarck's error was trusting his theory over observable reality. When have you trusted your own reasoning or comfort over clear evidence in your life? What 'extinction' are you avoiding by not changing?
?

Second Critique: Adaptations Are Hereditary, Not Acquired
Argues that Lamarck's observed adaptations are inherited, not acquired.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the traits Lamarck cited as evidence for acquired characteristics are actually hereditary and do not support his theory.

Core Idea
Lamarck's examples are hereditary, not acquired.

Lamarck observed that organisms seem to adapt to their environments, but he mistakenly thought these adaptations were acquired during life. In this passage, the author demonstrates that many such traits are present from birth, passed down through heredity, not developed in response to environment. We'll examine three examples and the genetic basis that disproves Lamarck's mechanism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the author's argumentative structure: claim, examples, genetic explanation, conclusion.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three examples
Find the three examples: infant's thick soles, camel callosities, and embryonic femur orientation. Note how each is said to be present from birth.
These counter Lamarck's idea of acquired traits.
3
Understand the genetic explanation
The author invokes genetics: the basic structure is internal, determined by chromosomes and gametes, not external factors.
Modern science confirms this.
4
Consider the metaphysical claim
The author rejects the notion that traits were once acquired in ancient times as a metaphysical assertion contradicting observed reality.
This is a strong refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانياً - إن أكثر ما لاحظه لامارك ، من مظاهر التطور التي اعتمدها أساساً لبحثه وميزاناً لفرضيته ، إنما يجري ضمن سلسلة الأفراد ، بعامل الوراثة ، أي من قبل أن يلتقي الحيوان مع الظروف أوالبيئة أو الأحوال التي تلجئه إلى نوع من التطور أو التشكل للإنسجام معها فجلد الطفل يكون ، منذ ولادته ، أشد غلظاً على أخمص القدمين منه في أي جهة أخرى من أجزاء الجسم وللجمال ثفنات تقع في سويات رسغ اليدين والمرفق بحيث تطابق السطوح التي تتحمل وطأة الوزن عندما يستنيخ البعير . وتكون هذه الثفنات موجودة في ولد الناقة منذ ولادته وتتجه الامتدادات العظمية في عظام الفخذ في جنين الإنسان ، كما تتجه في البالغ المكتمل، أي وفقاً لاتجاه الضغوط التي تطرأ على العظام عند المشي ولا يمكننا في مثل هذه الأحوال أن نعلل الأمر بتكييف سـابـق تـأثر بالظروف والأحوال ) سيما وقد تبين من علم الوراثة أن الهيكل الأساسي للكائن الحي ليس من العوامل الخارجية وإنما هو أصل ذاتي حسب اقتران الصبغيات والناسلات لكل نوع وحده . ودعوى أن الأمر لم يكن على هذا النحو الوراثي في غابر الأزمان السحيقة ، زعم غيبي بحت يتنافى مع الواقع المستمر المشاهد
Secondly - Most of what Lamarck observed, of the manifestations of evolution that he adopted as the basis of his research and the criterion for his hypothesis, actually occurs within the chain of individuals, through the factor of heredity, i.e., before the animal encounters the conditions, environment, or circumstances that would compel it to a type of evolution or formation to harmonize with them. For the skin of a child, from its birth, is thicker on the soles of the feet than in any other part of the body. And camels have callosities located on the carpal joints and elbows, corresponding to the surfaces that bear the weight when the camel kneels. And these callosities are present in the young camel from its birth. And the bony extensions in the femur of the human embryo are directed as they are in the fully mature adult, i.e., according to the direction of pressures that occur on the bones during walking. And in such cases we cannot explain the matter by prior adaptation influenced by conditions and circumstances, especially since it has become clear from genetics that the basic structure of the living organism is not from external factors but is an inherent origin according to the pairing of chromosomes and gametes for each species alone. And the claim that this was not the case on this hereditary pattern in the remote past ages is a purely metaphysical assertion that contradicts the continuous observed reality.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is the second critique of Lamarck's theory. The author argues that most of the phenomena Lamarck considered as evidence for acquired characteristics are actually hereditary traits present from birth, not acquired through interaction with the environment. Three examples are given: (1) Human babies have thicker skin on the soles of their feet from birth, not as a result of walking. (2) Camels have callosities on their knees and elbows that are present at birth, not developed from kneeling. (3) In human embryos, the orientation of bone extensions in the femur matches that of adults, corresponding to pressures from walking, yet the embryo has never walked. The author then states that genetics has shown that the basic structure of an organism is determined internally by chromosomes and gametes, not by external factors. Therefore, claiming that such traits were once acquired in ancient times is a speculative metaphysical claim that contradicts observable continuity.

Correction: These traits are present from birth and are hereditary, determined by chromosomes and gametes.

Lamarck's Theory Only Explains Minor Changes, Not Full Transmutation
Points out that Lamarck's theory only explains minor adaptations, not complete species transformation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Lamarck's theory fails to account for complete species transformation and only addresses minor environmental adaptations.

Core Idea
Lamarck explains small adaptations, not the full specific evolution of entire animal constitution.

The author sets aside previous criticisms and points to a fundamental mismatch: Lamarck's theory deals with a much narrower question than the comprehensive transmutation hypothesis under investigation. While Lamarck accounts for changes in form and color due to environment, the real question is about a complete overhaul of instinct, intellect, and body structure under conditions unrelated to such transformation. This lesson draws the distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice how the author distinguishes between two levels of change.
Pay attention to the phrase 'تطور نوعي كامل' (complete specific evolution).
2
Identify the two scopes
The author contrasts Lamarck's theory (partial changes in organs due to environment) with the hypothesis under study (complete transformation of all aspects). List the differences.
3
Understand why Lamarck falls short
Reflect on why the author says Lamarck's analysis covers only a very small part of the basic research subject. Consider what questions remain unanswered.
This shows the limitation of Lamarck's explanatory power.

This passage is the third critique of Lamarck's theory. The author's research concerns a hypothesis that claims animals can undergo complete specific evolution (تطور نوعي كامل) affecting the entire constitution—instinct, intellect, shape, hair, claws, nails—under conditions that bear no apparent relation to such a radical change. Lamarck's theory, in contrast, only explains partial changes in forms and organs that are influenced over time by environmental factors. The author concludes that the core issue still requires thorough analysis and explanation to answer many pressing questions.

Darwin's Mechanical Explanation of Evolution via Natural Selection
Introduces Darwin's book and his mechanical explanation via natural selection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Darwin's attempt to explain evolution through a purely mechanical process, relying on the principle of survival of the fittest, and how he derived this idea from Malthusian economics.

Core Idea
Darwin sought to explain evolution without appealing to purpose, yet his mechanism still echoed teleology.

In this passage, the author introduces Darwinism by describing Darwin's famous book and his goal of providing a purely mechanical explanation for evolution. He notes Darwin's reliance on the principle of survival of the fittest and traces the origin of this idea to the economist Malthus. This sets the stage for a critique of the theory from a theological perspective.

Guided Path
1
Understand Darwin's objective
Read the passage to grasp Darwin's aim: to reduce evolution to a purely mechanical explanation, as independent as possible from final causes (teleology).
2
Identify the mechanism
Notice that Darwin used the principle of 'survival of the fittest' as the cause of evolution. This is natural selection.
The phrase 'survival of the fittest' was coined by Herbert Spencer, but Darwin adopted it.
3
Trace the intellectual source
The passage reveals that Darwin derived his theory from Malthus's book 'Population', which discussed competition for resources.
4
Recognize the tension
Reflect on the contradiction: Darwin aimed for a mechanical explanation free from purpose, but 'survival of the fittest' can imply a directed outcome.
This tension is often raised by critics of Darwinism.

الداروينية : في عام ١٨٧١ أخرج داروين كتابه المشهور المسمى بـ « أصل الأنواع والانتخاب بالنسبة للجنس » حاول فيه أن يردّ التطور إلى تفسير آلي بحت . بحيث يكون مستقلاً قدر الإمكان عن الأسباب الغائية ولكنه مع ذلك اتخذ من مبدأ اختيار الأصلح سبباً للتطور . وقد استمد داروین نظريته من كتاب « السكان » للاقتصادي المعروف

Nevertheless, he took the principle of survival of the fittest as the cause of evolution. And Darwin derived his theory from the book 'Population' by the well-known economist.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage introduces Darwin's theory. The author notes that in 1871, Darwin published his famous work 'The Origin of Species and Selection in Relation to Sex' (likely referring to 'The Descent of Man and Selection in Relation to Sex'). Darwin's goal was to provide a purely mechanical explanation for evolution, avoiding teleological (final cause) explanations as much as possible. However, he did adopt the principle of 'survival of the fittest' (originally coined by Herbert Spencer) as the driving mechanism. The author also points out that Darwin's idea was influenced by the book 'Population' by the economist Thomas Malthus, which discussed population growth and resource competition.

Darwin's Theory of Natural Selection and Its Malthusian Basis
Describes Darwin's theory of natural selection and its Malthusian basis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Malthus's population principle forms the foundation of Darwin's theory of natural selection, and how the elephant example illustrates the necessity of natural selection.

Core Idea
Natural selection is driven by competition for limited resources.

This passage explains the intellectual roots of Darwin's theory. It begins by citing Malthus's observation about population growth versus food supply, which introduces competition. Darwin then infers that individuals with advantageous traits are naturally selected, leading to the survival of the fittest. The author uses the example of elephant reproduction to illustrate the vast potential for population growth that is checked by natural selection, and then shows how this process results in the diversity of species, with humans as one outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify Malthus's premise
Read the first part of the passage and note Malthus's claim about population growth versus food supply. Understand why this leads to competition.
The premise sets the stage for Darwin's theory.
2
Understand natural selection
Read how Darwin uses variation in traits to explain survival. Notice that the qualities may not be obviously important but still affect survival.
3
Analyze the elephant example
Examine the calculation: a female elephant produces only six young, but if all survived, the population would explode. This shows that most offspring die, supporting natural selection.
The example demonstrates the power of natural checks.
4
Connect competition to species diversity
Read how competition over time leads to a ladder of species, with humans as a product of this process.
This part explains the broader outcome of natural selection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مالتوس، الذي كان يزعم بأن السكان يزدادون بنسبة هندسية بينما لا تزداد نسبة الغذاء إلا بنسبة حسابية، مما يؤدي إلى تنافس وتنازع بين الأفراد على الغذاء ليتلاشى غير الأكفاء (1) فهو يرى أن ثمة صفات، قد لا تكون ذات أهمية في الظاهر، يتفاوت الأفراد في مدى اتصافهم بها، يكون لها أثر فعال في المحافظة على صاحبها وترشيحه لمستوى أفضل. وعندما يدخل هؤلاء الأفراد في صراع مع الطبيعة من أجل الحياة يجري اصطفاء طبيعي يؤدي إلى بقاء أشد الأفراد كفاءة وصلاحية للبقاء، بما تمتاز به من تلك الصفات، أو بما تمتاز به من الحصول على أعلى الرتب منها. ويستشهد داروين على أحقية هذا الاصطفاء بتلك العوامل الهائلة. التي تبيد نتاج كثير من الكائنات الحية مع الزمن. فهو يلفت نظرنا مثلاً إلى أن أنثى الفيل تضع خلال حياتها ستة صغار، ولو اتبعنا هذا الأساس فإنه يجب أن نتاج كل ذكر واحد وأنثى واحدة في نهاية سبعمائة وخمسين عاماً نحو تسعة عشر مليوناً. وواضح جداً أن الواقع الطبيعي بعيد كل البعد عن هذا الحساب). وهكذا فإن التفوق الذي يتمتع به الحيوان، من حيث هو نوع بالنسبة للأنواع الأخرى، أو من حيث هو فرد بالنسبة للأفراد الأخرى يمكنه من اكتساح غيره لا في أصل الوجود فحسب بل في خصائص الوجود أيضا وما قد ينطوي عليه من تعقيدات مفيدة. وفي غمرة هذا التسابق الذي تم منذ أقدم العصور في عالم الأحياء، ونتيجة لتفاوت الصفات الكامنة في كل منها - وهي الطاقة الوحيدة لذلك التسابق - ظهر سلم الدرجات التي صنفت هذه الأحياء إلى أنواع مختلفة ومتفاوتة شتى. وليس الإنسان، في سلم هذه الدرجات، إلا واحداً من فريق تلك الحيوانات البسيطة التي بدأت السباق فيما بينها، ضمن دائرة نوعية واحدة، فكان من حسن حظه أن كان له من الصفات الكامنة ما تقدم به صعداً في حلبة ذلك السباق ورشحه لتبوء أسمى درجات الحياة، من حيث تخلف زملاؤه عنه في درجات متفاوتة شتى.
Malthus, who claimed that population increases geometrically while the food supply increases only arithmetically, leading to competition and conflict among individuals over food so that the unfit disappear (1). So he (Darwin) sees that there are qualities, which may not be apparently important, in which individuals vary in the degree they possess them, and they have an effective role in preserving their owner and recommending him to a better level. When these individuals enter into a struggle with nature for existence, a natural selection occurs that leads to the survival of the fittest and most capable individuals for survival, due to those qualities they possess, or due to their attainment of the highest ranks of them. Darwin cites as evidence for the validity of this selection those enormous factors that destroy the offspring of many living organisms over time. For example, he draws our attention to the fact that the female elephant gives birth during her life to six young, and if we follow this basis, then the product of one male and one female at the end of 750 years should be about 19 million. It is very clear that natural reality is far from this calculation. Thus the superiority that the animal enjoys, whether as a species relative to other species, or as an individual relative to other individuals, enables it to overwhelm others not only in the origin of existence but also in the characteristics of existence and what it may entail of useful complexities. In the midst of this competition that has taken place since ancient times in the world of living things, and as a result of the variation in the latent qualities in each of them - which is the sole energy for that competition - the ladder of degrees appeared that classified these living things into various different and varied types. And man, in this ladder of degrees, is but one of those simple animals that began the race among themselves, within a single species circle, and it was his good fortune that he had from the latent qualities what advanced him upward in the arena of that race and qualified him to occupy the highest degrees of life, while his fellows lagged behind him in various different degrees.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage presents Darwin's theory of natural selection as derived from Malthus's population principle. It begins by citing Malthus's claim that population grows geometrically while food grows arithmetically, leading to competition. Then it explains Darwin's inference: individuals possess varying qualities that affect survival; those with advantageous traits are selected naturally, leading to the survival of the fittest. Darwin supports this by noting that most offspring do not survive, as illustrated by the elephant example: if all offspring survived, populations would explode. Then the passage explains how this competition produces a ladder of species, with humans being one product of this process.

Darwin's Four Lines of Evidence for Human Evolution
Listing Darwin's categories of evidence for human evolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four categories of evidence Darwin used to argue for human evolution from a common ancestor.

Core Idea
Darwin argued human evolution using anatomy, embryology, vestigial structures, and psychology.

Darwin's theory of evolution by natural selection required evidence that humans shared a common ancestor with other animals. In this passage, the author lists the four main types of evidence Darwin presented: comparative anatomy, embryology, vestigial structures, and psychology. Specific examples like skeletal similarities and the embryonic tail illustrate how Darwin built his case.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify Darwin's question
Start by reading the opening question: on what evidence did Darwin rely? This sets up the passage's purpose.
2
List the four evidence categories
Identify the four types of evidence: comparative anatomy, embryology, vestigial structures, and psychology.
Notice that vestigial structures are mentioned but not exemplified in detail.
3
Examine the comparative anatomy examples
Darwin compared skeletal, muscular, nervous system, and brain structures between humans and animals. Understand the method of analogy.
This is a key argument for common ancestry.
4
Analyze the embryological evidence
The recapitulation idea and the tail example: human and dog embryos both have a tail-like structure, which disappears in humans. This suggests shared development.
5
Consider the psychological evidence
Darwin pointed to emotions and consciousness as shared between humans and some animals. Reflect on what this implies about mental continuity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن على أي دليل اعتمد داروين في الذهاب إلى أن الإنسان كبقية الحيوانات الأخرى تطور من نوع واحد؟ لقد استمد داروين دليله على ما يقول من علوم التشريح المقارن والأجنة ومن التراكيب الأثرية التي توجد في الإنسان. فقد وجد مثلاً أن أجزاء الهيكل العظمي للإنسان، يمكن مقارنتها بمثيلاتها في بعض الحيوانات الأخرى، وكذلك الأمر بالنسبة للجهاز العضلي أو العصبي، حتى تركيب المخ وأجزائه يمكن مقارنتها بين الإنسان والحيوان واستخراج كثير من أوجه الشبه بينهما. كما رأى بالنسبة للأدلة المستمدة من علم الأجنة أن عملية تكوين الجنين في الإنسان ما هي إلا استعادة لأطوار الحياة في حيوانات أقل مرتبة، كما أن المراحل الأولى لتطوير الجنين تتشابه تشابهاً كبيراً في الإنسان والحيوان. فقد لاحظ مثلاً أن عجز الجنين ينتهي بما يشبه الذيل في جنين كل من الإنسان والكلب وبتطور الجنين يختفي الذيل في جنين الإنسان ويبقى في الكلب. كما استدل داروين بمظاهر من الترابط النفسي بين الإنسان وبعض أنواع الحيوانات، مثل ظاهرة الوجدان والشعور والانفعالات النفسية (1)
But on what evidence did Darwin rely in going to say that man, like other animals, evolved from a single type? Darwin derived his evidence for what he says from the sciences of comparative anatomy and embryology and from vestigial structures found in man. He found, for example, that the parts of the human skeleton can be compared with their counterparts in some other animals, and likewise for the muscular or nervous system, even the structure of the brain and its parts can be compared between man and animal, extracting many points of similarity between them. As he saw regarding the evidence derived from embryology, the process of fetal development in man is nothing but a recapitulation of life stages in lower animals, and the early stages of fetal development are greatly similar in man and animal. He observed, for example, that the tailbone of the fetus ends with something resembling a tail in the fetus of both man and dog, and with fetal development the tail disappears in the human fetus and remains in the dog. Also Darwin inferred from manifestations of psychological connection between man and some animal species, such as the phenomenon of feeling, consciousness, and psychological emotions (1).
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage presents Darwin's evidence for human evolution. It first asks the question of evidence, then states that Darwin used comparative anatomy, embryology, and vestigial structures. The passage details specific examples: skeletal, muscular, nervous system, and brain similarities; embryological recapitulation; and the tail example (human fetal tail versus dog). Finally, it mentions psychological evidence such as emotions and consciousness. This form of argumentation uses analogy and shared characteristics to argue for common ancestry.

Correction: The passage shows that Darwin also used embryology, vestigial structures, and psychology, making a broader case.

Checkpoint

A) It proves both species are identical
B) It shows a common developmental stage, suggesting common ancestry
C) It is a random similarity without meaning

Key Takeaway
Darwin supported human evolution with evidence from comparative anatomy, embryology, vestigial structures, and psychology, suggesting a common ancestry.

Two Critiques of Darwinism: Natural Selection and Chance
Buti presents two objections to Darwinism: the persistence of weak species and the role of chance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two fundamental critiques of Darwinism: the persistence of weak species contradicts natural selection, and the role of chance undermines the mechanism of competition.

Core Idea
Darwinism fails to explain why weak species survive and why survival is often a matter of chance.

This lesson presents two objections to Darwinism drawn from the work of Dr. Abdul Halim Suwaidan. These critiques question the core tenets of natural selection and survival of the fittest, pointing to observable phenomena that seem to contradict Darwin's theory. We will examine each objection and consider their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to grasp the two critiques.
Notice that the passage begins by noting Darwin himself admitted problems.
2
Understand the first critique
The first critique argues that the law of survival of the fittest is contradicted by the continued existence of weak and unfit species.
Consider why the 'starting point' of evolution should have been left behind.
3
Understand the second critique
The second critique distinguishes between extinction due to natural calamities and extinction due to competition, pointing out that chance often determines survival.
Reflect on the difference between observable fact and theoretical claim.
4
Synthesise and reflect
Think about how these two critiques together challenge the core mechanism of Darwinism.
Consider whether these objections are answered by modern evolutionary theory.

نقد الداروينية :
يقول الدكتور عبد الحليم سويدان : لقد أثارت النظرية الداروينية كثيراً
من النقد . ثم عرض لطائفة منها قال عنها بعد ذلك إنها جزء يسير من انتقادات كثيرة أخرى وجهت إلى الداروينية )
فلنعدد ، على وجه السرعة ، هذه الانتقادات وغيرها ، آخذين بعين الاعتبار ما وجه داروين نفسه إلى نظريته من مشكلات اعترف بالنسبة لكثير منها بأنها مشكلات عويصة واكتفى بذلك عن محاولة حلها أو الإجابة عليها !...
١ - إن الواقع الذي نشاهده يتنافى بشكل حاد مع ما أسماه داروين بقانون الاصطفاء والبقاء للأصلح . فإن الكون لا يزال - بعد كل ما قطعه من عمره المديد - يعج بالأصلح والصالح وغير الصالح من شتى أصناف الحيوانات بدءاً بالهلاميات إلى القردة فالإنسان !...
ولو كان قانونه صحيحاً ؛ لكان من أبسط مقتضياته الواضحة ، أن يتجاوز موكب السباق الحيواني نقطة البدء على أقل تقدير مهما فرضنا حركة التطور والاصطفاء بطيئة. ولكن ها هي ذي نقطة البدء لا تزال تفور بحيواناتها الضعيفة المتخلفة ولا تزال تتمتع بحياتها وخصائصها المعاشية كما يتمتع بها السابقون

٢ - لا خلاف في أن كل نوع من الحيوانات تطرأ عليه خسائر ضخمة مع الزمن بسبب عوادٍ وعوامل طبيعية مختلفة تتغلب عليها . هذه حقيقة مشاهدة لا تنكر . أما أن تكون الكارثة نتيجة تسابق وتنافس ينتهيان باصطفاء الأنسب والأقدر فهذه ـ كما يقول الدكتور عبد الحليم سويدان - مسألة أخرى ... إن كلاً من الموت والنجاة من الموت كثيراً ما يكون عائداً إلى المصادفة المجردة لا إلى (۱)
علم الحياة الحيوانية : ص ١٣٣ .
Criticism of Darwinism: Dr. Abdul Halim Suwaidan says: Darwinian theory has aroused much criticism. Then he presented a group of them, saying about them afterwards that they are a small part of many other criticisms directed at Darwinism. So let us quickly enumerate these and other criticisms, taking into account what Darwin himself directed at his theory of problems, many of which he admitted were intractable, and he contented himself with that rather than trying to solve or answer them!...
1 - The reality we observe sharply contradicts what Darwin called the law of selection and survival of the fittest. For the universe - after all its long age - still teems with the fittest, the fit, and the unfit from all kinds of animals, from jellyfish to apes to humans!... And if his law were correct, one of its simplest and clearest implications would be that the race procession of animals would have at least passed the starting point, no matter how slow we suppose the movement of evolution and selection. But here is the starting point still teeming with its weak, backward animals, and they still enjoy their lives and livelihood characteristics just as the forerunners do, alike for alike.
2 - There is no dispute that each species of animal suffers huge losses over time due to various natural calamities and factors that overcome them. This is an observable fact that cannot be denied. But that the catastrophe is the result of competition and rivalry ending in the selection of the most suitable and capable - this, as Dr. Abdul Halim Suwaidan says, is another matter... For both death and survival from death are often due to pure chance, not to (1)
Animal Biology: p. 133.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage presents a critique of Darwinism, beginning with a quotation from Dr. Abdul Halim Suwaidan noting that Darwin himself admitted many problems with his theory. The author then enumerates two specific criticisms. The first criticism argues that the law of survival of the fittest contradicts observable reality: the universe still contains a wide range of organisms, including weak and unfit species, long after evolution should have eliminated them. If the law were correct, the starting point of evolution should have been left behind, yet primitive forms still thrive. The second criticism distinguishes between observable extinction caused by natural calamities (which is undeniable) and the claim that extinction results from competition driving selection. It argues that death and survival are often due to pure chance, not competition. The footnote cites 'Animal Biology' as the source for this second criticism. The passage does not provide a rebuttal but presents the objections as valid concerns.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Darwinism is a proven fact with no major objections.
Correction: The passage highlights serious criticisms even from within science, showing that the theory has significant problems acknowledged by Darwin himself.

Checkpoint
According to the first critique, what contradicts Darwin's law of survival of the fittest?
A) The extinction of many species
B) The continued existence of weak and unfit species alongside the fittest
C) The fossil record showing gradual change
D) The psychological similarities between humans and animals

Key Takeaway
The persistence of weak species and the role of chance pose serious challenges to Darwin's theory of natural selection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that weak species survive despite the 'survival of the fittest'. Consider a weakness in your own faith that persists. Instead of eliminating it, God allows it. What might He be teaching you about your dependence on Him? Will you humble yourself and ask for His help, or continue pretending you are strong enough alone?
?
Chance, according to this passage, determines many deaths and survivals. If your life today is the result of chance, does that not terrify you? How will you live differently knowing that your next breath is not guaranteed by your plans?
?
Darwin himself admitted problems with his theory. Are you willing to admit the weaknesses in your own worldview, even if it is uncomfortable? What specific belief about yourself or the world do you hold that might be contradicted by clear evidence, and will you examine it honestly today?

The Contradiction of Death with Natural Selection
Third argument: death contradicts Darwin's survival of the fittest.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how death itself undermines Darwin's principle of survival of the fittest, especially given statistical evidence.

Core Idea
Death spares the average and attacks the superior—a direct contradiction of natural selection.

This argument strikes at the heart of Darwinian selection: if nature favors the fittest, why does death often take them first? The author cites statistical studies to show that death targets those above average, leaving the average and below to survive. This challenges the core prediction of Darwin's theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Pay attention to the rhetorical question and the statistical evidence cited.
Note the footnote reference—this shows the argument is based on empirical data.
2
Analyze the logical structure
Identify the two parts: (1) the conceptual contradiction between death and survival of the fittest, and (2) the empirical evidence that death strikes above-average individuals first.
Ask yourself: If survival of the fittest means the best survive, why do the best die first?
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this argument weakens Darwin's theory. The evidence suggests natural selection does not work as Darwin predicted.
This is not a rejection of all evolution, but a specific critique of natural selection as the driving mechanism.

3 - Death also contradicts what Darwin sees that nature directs the community of living beings according to the law of selection and survival of the fittest. So what survival of the fittest occurs if death lies in wait for it? Moreover, statistical studies established by scientists of this matter show that death attacks at first those individuals who may rise above the average type, after which the average type and what is below it remain. And this is a result that contradicts Darwin's theory and his predictions. (1) The Science of Life by Dr. Suwaidan: 133

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument against Darwin's theory of natural selection. The author states that death itself contradicts Darwin's view that nature guides living beings according to the law of selection and survival of the fittest. He asks a rhetorical question: what survival of the fittest can occur if death constantly threatens them? Then he cites statistical studies showing that death first attacks individuals who rise above the average, leaving the average and below-average types to survive. This empirical result, he concludes, directly contradicts Darwin's predictions and theory. The footnote references Dr. Suwaidan's book 'The Science of Life' as the source for these statistics.

Misconception: One might think Darwin's theory predicts only the weak die, but this argument shows death often takes the strong first.
Correction: Darwinian natural selection expects the fittest to survive and reproduce, but statistical evidence indicates that death frequently targets superior individuals, contradicting the expected pattern.

A) Death targets the weak and sick first.
B) Death attacks individuals who rise above the average first.
C) Death spares all individuals equally.
D) Death only occurs in old age.

Key Takeaway
Death's tendency to strike the most fit individuals directly contradicts Darwin's principle of survival of the fittest.

?

?
If death spares the average and below, what does that suggest about the worldly value of being 'average'? Are you content to remain spiritually average, knowing that death may not single you out? What would it take for you to seek excellence in your faith despite this?

The Problem of Creating and Then Eliminating the Weak
Argument against natural selection's inconsistency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical inconsistency in the idea that nature creates weak individuals only to eliminate them later.

Core Idea
Creating life only to destroy it is irrational.

This lesson examines a powerful argument against the notion that nature operates through trial and error. The author presents a scenario where a weak individual is allowed to enter life and participate fully, only to be singled out for destruction. This raises a fundamental question: why create what you will later destroy? The passage invites us to see the contradiction in such a process.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with a hypothetical scenario (law kāna al-amru bi-yadihā).
2
Identify the two alternatives
The passage presents two options: either nature controls creation or it does not. Identify where each option is introduced.
The first alternative is implicit in the initial scenario; the second is introduced by 'wa ammā idhā qulnā...'.
3
Analyze the logical problem
For each alternative, consider the contradiction. If nature creates the weak, why later destroy them? If nature does not create them, how can it destroy them?
This is a classic dilemma: both horns lead to inconsistency.
4
Connect to the broader argument
Understand how this argument refutes the idea of unguided natural selection as a coherent process.
This is the fifth argument in a series against natural selection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ه - إن وقاية الحياة من أن يتسلل إليها ضعيف لا تتوفر فيه مجموعة الصفات الصالحة ، أيسر على الطبيعة - لو كان الأمر بيدها - من أن تذهل عنه . حتى إذا تسلل إلى الحياة وأخذ قسطه منها وراح يشارك أمثاله في القيام بكافة الوظائف الحياتية ، انتبهت إليه فجأة ثم راحت تلتقطه وأمثاله من بين سائر الحيوانات لتقضي عليه وتصحح في محوه خطيئتها التي ما كان لها أن ترتكبها . إن كان هذا الضعيف محكوماً عليه بالتخلف ، فالزوال ، لأنه ليس من صنف الصالح أو الأصلح ، فلماذا أوجدت الطبيعة هذا الذي تريد اليوم أن تقضي عليه أو تؤخره عن الركب ؟.. أما إذا قلنا أن أمر إيجاده لم يكن إليها ، فأحرى أن لا يكون إليها أيضاً أمر تهذيب الكون بإعدامه والقضاء على خطيئة وجوده
5 - Preventing life from being infiltrated by a weak individual lacking a set of good qualities is easier for nature—if the matter were in its hands—than to be heedless of it. Then when it infiltrated life, took its share of it, and began to participate with its likes in performing all vital functions, it suddenly paid attention to it and then began to pick it and its likes from among the rest of the animals to eliminate it and correct by its erasure the sin that it should not have committed. If this weak individual is destined to be backward and then perish, because it is not of the good or fittest type, then why did nature create this which it today wants to destroy or delay from the race? But if we say that the matter of its creation was not in its hands, then it follows that the matter of refining the universe by exterminating it and eliminating the sin of its existence is also not in its hands.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth argument, which points out an inconsistency in the idea of natural selection as a process of eliminating the weak. The author begins by stating that if nature had control, it would be easier for it to prevent a weak individual—lacking good qualities—from entering life in the first place, rather than being heedless. However, after such a weak individual enters life, takes its share, and participates in vital functions, nature suddenly 'notices' it and picks it out for elimination, as if correcting a 'sin' it should not have committed. The author then poses a question: if this weak individual is doomed to be backward and perish because it is not of the good or fittest, why did nature create it in the first place, only to now want to destroy it or delay it from the race? Alternatively, if we claim that nature did not create it (i.e., its creation is outside nature's control), then it follows that the matter of refining the universe by exterminating it and correcting the 'sin' of its existence is also not in nature's hands. Thus, the argument shows a logical contradiction: either nature is responsible for both creation and elimination, in which case it acts irrationally by creating what it later destroys, or it is not responsible for creation, in which case it cannot be responsible for elimination.

Key Terms
الضعيف
الخطيئة
الاصطفاء الطبيعي
التخلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Natural selection simply eliminates the weak without any problem.
Correction: This argument shows that creating the weak only to destroy them is logically inconsistent, implying that natural selection, if blind, cannot be responsible for both creation and elimination.

Checkpoint
What logical problem does the fifth argument identify in natural selection?
A) The weak are never eliminated.
B) The strong are always eliminated instead.
C) Creating the weak then destroying them is inconsistent.
D) Nature never creates weak individuals.

Key Takeaway
The fifth argument shows that if nature creates the weak only to destroy them, it acts irrationally; if it does not create them, it cannot be responsible for their destruction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have likely excused your own weaknesses by saying 'it's just how I was made.' But if you believe in a Creator who does not create to destroy, how does this passage confront your acceptance of your own faults? What will you do today to change one weakness instead of resigning to it?
?
The author calls the creation of the weak a 'sin' if done by nature. How would you feel if you created something only to later destroy it? How does this challenge your view of God's actions? Are you willing to trust that your struggles have a purpose beyond elimination?
?
If you were the weak individual described who was created only to be eliminated, how would you feel? Now consider that according to this argument, God does not act that way. How does this change how you view your own worth in His sight?

The Missing Intelligence: A Challenge to Natural Selection
Sixth argument: natural selection should have given higher animals more intelligence, but it didn't.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the absence of higher intelligence in animals like apes poses a problem for the theory of natural selection, and how Darwin himself acknowledged this gap.

Core Idea
Darwin could not explain why natural selection didn't give apes human-like intelligence.

This passage presents a powerful objection to Darwinian evolution: if natural selection always favors the fittest, why haven't higher animals developed rational powers comparable to humans? The author shows that even Darwin himself admitted he could not answer this question, exposing a fundamental gap in his theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the Arabic passage once, then follow the English translation. Notice the logical structure: premise, question, and Darwin's response.
2
Understand Darwin's response
The passage shows Darwin gave two replies, both admitting inability to answer. Identify the key phrases where he acknowledges this.
Look for 'he did not answer' and 'admitted his inability'.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why this objection is serious for evolution. Consider what it means if a core prediction (more intelligence in beneficial cases) fails.
This connects to the learning objective: how the argument challenges natural selection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٦ - إذا كان مبدأ الاصطفاء الطبيعي هو مبعث التطور المستمر في الكائنات الحية ، وكان هذا التطور يتجه دوماً شطر ما هو الأصلح - فلماذا لا نجد القوى العاقلة في كثير من الحيوانات أكثر تطوراً وارتقاء من غيرها ما دام هذا الارتقاء ذا فائدة لمجموعها ؟.. ولماذا لم تكتسب القردة العليا من القوى العاقلة بمقدار ما اكتسبه الإنسان مثلاً ؟ لقد عرض داروين لهذه المشكلة التي وجهها إليه ، كما يقول هو في كتابه أكثر من كاتب ، ولكنه لم يجب عليها وإنما علّق عليها بقوله : إننا لا ينبغي لنا أن نعثر على جواب محدود معين على هذا السؤال ، إذا ما عرفنا أننا لا جرم نعجز عن الإجابة على سؤال أقل من هذا تعقيداً (( ثم إنه عرض مرة أخرى لهذه المشكلة التي وقفت مع مشكلات كثيرة أخرى في طريق نظريته ، بأسلوب آخر ، ومرة أخرى أقر بعجزه عن الإجابة عليها فقال : طالما تساءل بعض الباحثين : كيف أن أثر الانتخاب الطبيعي ، ما دام بالغاً إلى الحدود البعيدة القصية ، لم يستحدث في أنواع معينة ، تراكيب ، إن استحدثت فيها كانت ذات فائدة كبيرة لها ؟.. غير أنه مما يضاد بديهة العقل أن (1) أصل الأنواع : ص ٤١٢
6 - If the principle of natural selection is the source of continuous evolution in living organisms, and this evolution always tends towards what is fittest—then why do we not find the rational powers in many animals more developed and advanced than others, as long as this advancement is of benefit to their whole? And why did the higher apes not acquire rational powers to the extent that man acquired, for example? Darwin presented this problem that was directed to him, as he says in his book more than one writer, but he did not answer it; rather he commented by saying: 'We should not find a specific limited answer to this question, if we know that we are certainly unable to answer a less complex question than this.' Then he presented this problem again, which stood with many other problems in the way of his theory, in another style, and again he admitted his inability to answer it, saying: 'Some researchers have long wondered: how is it that the effect of natural selection, since it reaches the farthest limits, did not produce in certain species structures that, if produced in them, would be of great benefit to them? But it is contrary to common sense that...' (1) The Origin of Species: p. 412
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth argument against Darwin's theory. The author begins by stating the premise: if natural selection is the source of continuous evolution always moving towards what is fittest, then why don't many animals have more developed rational powers, especially since such advancement would benefit them? Specifically, why haven't higher apes acquired rational powers to the same extent as humans? The author then notes that Darwin himself was confronted with this problem by more than one writer, but he did not answer it. Instead, Darwin commented that we should not expect a specific answer, because we are unable to answer an even less complex question. The author adds that Darwin presented this problem again in another style, and again admitted his inability to answer, quoting Darwin's own words: researchers have wondered why natural selection, despite its far-reaching effects, did not produce beneficial structures in certain species. The quote is cut off, but the footnote identifies the source as Darwin's 'The Origin of Species' page 412. The argument highlights a major explanatory gap in Darwin's theory: it cannot account for why some species lack obviously beneficial traits like higher intelligence.

التطور
القوى العاقلة
القردة العليا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Darwin had a satisfactory explanation for why higher apes lack human intelligence.
Correction: The passage shows Darwin himself admitted he could not answer this question, both in his initial comment and in a later restatement.

Checkpoint
According to the sixth argument, how did Darwin respond to the question of why higher apes did not acquire rational powers like humans?
A) He provided a detailed evolutionary explanation.
B) He admitted he could not answer it.
C) He denied that apes lack rational powers.
D) He said the question is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
Darwin's own admission of inability to explain why higher apes lack human-level intelligence reveals a fundamental gap in the theory of natural selection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever placed your trust in a scientific theory without examining its weaknesses? This passage shows a founder of evolutionary biology admitting a fundamental gap. Are you willing to question the theories you've been taught, even if it means confronting uncomfortable truths about origins?
?
If Darwin could not explain why apes lack human intelligence, what does that tell you about the limits of naturalistic explanations? Does this challenge lead you to consider alternative explanations, such as divine creation? How will you respond the next time someone presents evolution as an indisputable fact?

Empirical Evidence Against Evolution: Egypt and the Ice Age
Author cites Egyptian artifacts and ice age fossils as evidence of species constancy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how empirical evidence from Egyptian artifacts and ice age fossils challenges the evolutionary hypothesis by demonstrating species stability.

Core Idea
Species stability contradicts evolution.

The author presents concrete empirical observations from ancient Egypt and the ice age to argue against the theory of evolution. Examining this evidence helps us evaluate the foundations of evolutionary theory and see that not all biological evidence supports it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the rhetorical question at the end.
2
Identify the two pieces of evidence
The passage gives two separate empirical observations. Find them and note how each is described.
One is from ancient Egypt, the other from the ice age.
3
Reflect on the rhetorical question
The author ends with 'So where is this undeniable reality in relation to the hypothesis of evolution?' Consider what this question implies about the validity of evolution.

لقد ثبت لدى الدراسة أن كثيراً من نباتات مصر وحيواناتها ، لم تتغير عن وضعها خلال قرون كثيرة متطاولة ، يتضح ذلك من الأنسال الداجنة المنحوتة في بعض الآثار المصرية القديمة ، أو التي حفظت بالتحنيط وكيف أنها تشابه كل المشابهة الصور الباقية اليوم ، بل ربما لا تكاد تفترق عنها بفارق ما بل إن هنالك تلك الحيوانات العديدة التي لم يطرأ على تركيبها أي تحول منذ بداية العصر الجليدي، على الرغم من أنها قد وضعت تحت تأثيرات كثيرة في تغيير المناخ بل إنها كثيراً ما هاجرت مسافات شاسعة على سطح الكرة الأرضية وذلك باعتراف داروين نفسه فأين هذا الواقع الذي لا ريب فيه من فرضية النشوء والارتقاء ؟؟
It has been established by study that many of the plants and animals of Egypt did not change from their state over many long centuries. This is evident from the domesticated lineages carved in some ancient Egyptian monuments, or preserved by embalming, and how they completely resemble the forms remaining today; indeed, they hardly differ from them by any difference. Rather, there are those numerous animals whose structure has not undergone any transformation since the beginning of the ice age, despite the fact that they have been placed under many influences in climate change; indeed, they have often migrated vast distances across the surface of the globe, and that by Darwin's own admission. So where is this undeniable reality in relation to the hypothesis of evolution?
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents two pieces of empirical evidence that contradict the theory of evolution. First, the author states that studies have shown that many plants and animals in Egypt have remained unchanged for many long centuries. This is evident from domesticated species carved in ancient Egyptian monuments or preserved through mummification; they closely resemble the forms existing today, with hardly any difference. Second, the author notes that there are numerous animals whose structure has not undergone any transformation since the beginning of the ice age, despite having been subjected to many influences changing the climate and having migrated vast distances across the globe—a fact acknowledged by Darwin himself. The passage concludes with a rhetorical question: where does this undeniable reality stand in relation to the hypothesis of evolution?

Misconception: That evolution is supported by all biological evidence.
Correction: The author shows specific counterexamples where species have remained unchanged for long periods, contradicting the idea of gradual change.

?

Critique of Darwin's Descriptive Evidence and the Possibility of Divine Creation
Author critiques Darwin's descriptive evidence and suggests creation as an alternative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author argues that Darwin's observations are merely descriptive and do not prove common descent, and how the possibility of divine creation remains a valid alternative.

Core Idea
Similarity between species does not prove descent; creation explains the same pattern.

In this passage, the author examines the nature of Darwin's evidence. He argues that the observed ascending similarity among organisms is a descriptive fact, not a proof of common ancestry. He then poses crucial rhetorical questions: could differences be due to essence rather than stage, and why not accept creation as the origin of the gradation? This lesson unpacks that critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the author's tone and the rhetorical questions he poses.
The passage is a critique, not a detailed scientific rebuttal.
2
Identify the two key concepts
Find where the author distinguishes between 'descriptive observations' and 'proof', and where he contrasts 'essence' (mahiyyah) with 'stage' (tawr).
These distinctions are central to the argument.
3
Reflect on the author's conclusion
Consider why the author says no experimental proof has been provided. How does this support the possibility of divine creation?
The author leaves the question open but favors the creation alternative.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخيراً نقول : إن كل ما اعتمده داروين لا يعدو أن يكون من نوع المشاهدات الوصفية الثابتة، أي إنه لاحظ ظاهرة التشابه التصاعدي في الكائنات الحية بدءاً من الخلية الأولى إلى أرقى أنواعها وهو الإنسان . ولكن ما علاقة هذا التشابه الثابت بين سلسلة الحيوانات بدعوى أنها جميعاً منحدرة من أصل حيواني واحد ؟ .. ألا يمكن أن يكون الفرق بين الإنسان وغيره من الحيوانات مثلاً فرقاً ناشئاً من اختلاف الماهية لا من الاختلاف في الطور وإن تراءى بينهما بعض الشبه ؟ .. أي لماذا لا تكون هذه السلسلة المتدرجة في الكائنات الحية ، قائمة على هذا التدرج والتشابه نفسه منذ أن خلقها الله عز وجل ؟.. لو كان ثمة ميزان من دليل التجربة والمشاهدة ، لكان في ميسوره أن يقضي على هذا التساؤل من أساسه . وأن يحمل إلينا القول الفصل في المسألة . ولكن لا داروين ، ولا من سبقه أو لحقه من علماء هذا الشأن استطاع أن يمدنا بدليل ما من هذا القبيل
Finally we say: Everything that Darwin relied upon is nothing more than fixed descriptive observations, meaning he observed the phenomenon of ascending similarity in living organisms from the first cell to its highest type, which is man. But what connection does this fixed similarity between the chain of animals have with the claim that they are all descended from a single animal origin? Could it not be that the difference between man and other animals, for example, is a difference arising from a difference in essence (al-mahiyyah) and not from a difference in stage (al-tawr), even if some resemblance appears between them? That is, why should not this gradual chain of living organisms be based upon this gradation and similarity itself since God, the Mighty and Majestic, created them? If there were a scale of experimental and observational proof, it would be able to eliminate this questioning entirely and bring us the decisive word on the matter. But neither Darwin, nor those before him or after him from the scholars of this field, were able to provide us with any proof of this kind.

Commentary
This passage is a critical analysis of the evidence Darwin presented. The author first characterizes Darwin's observations as being only descriptive—noting a pattern of ascending similarity, but not proving that this similarity is due to common descent. The author then poses a series of rhetorical questions: Can similarity between species be equated with descent from a common ancestor? Could not the differences between humans and animals be due to a difference in their essential nature (mahiyyah) rather than a difference in developmental stage (tawr)? Finally, the author suggests that the graded similarity could be exactly as it was created by God. The passage ends with a statement that no experimental proof has been provided to settle the question—neither Darwin nor any other scientist has provided such evidence.

The Rise of Neo-Darwinism: Random Mutation as the Basis of Evolution
Author outlines the rise of neo-Darwinism and its core claim of random mutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how neo-Darwinism emerged as a corrected version of Darwin's theory, and the central role of random mutations instead of natural selection.

Core Idea
Neo-Darwinism replaced Darwin's natural selection with random mutation as the driving force of evolution.

After Darwin's theory faced heavy criticism and fell into decline, a new school of thought arose to revive it in a modified form. This passage introduces neo-Darwinism, highlighting its key proponents and its fundamental departure from classical Darwinism—the replacement of natural selection with random, sudden mutations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the historical context and main claims.
Notice the contrast between classical Darwinism and neo-Darwinism.
2
Identify the key change
Compare neo-Darwinism to classical Darwinism. Identify the shift from natural selection to random mutation as the primary mechanism.
The passage explicitly states that evolution is based on mutation, not selection.
3
Understand mutation and inheritance
Reflect on the author's description: mutations occur suddenly, by chance, with no apparent purpose, and then become recorded in the genetic heritage and inherited.
Consider how this differs from Darwin's gradual selection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الداروينية الجديدة :
كان للانتقادات الكثيرة التي توجهت إلى نظرية داروين أثر كبير في أن تتهاوى ويمر عليها عهد من السقوط والتردّي ، ولكن طائفة من الباحثين عادوا فأشادوا من أنقاضها نظرية أخرى جديدة أطلق عليها فيما بعد اسم : الداروينية الجديدة ، اعتبرت بمثابة النسخة المصححة لنظرية داروين
وقد تزعم هؤلاء الباحثين العالم الهولندي Hugo de Veries
ثم شايعه ودعمه في ذلك طائفة من علماء الحيــاة أكثرهم إنكليزيــون وأمريكيون
وأهم ما ينهض عليه هذا المذهب الجديد ويعتبر فارقاً أسـاسـيـاً يتميز به عن نظرية داروين ما قد ترجح عند هؤلاء الآخرين من أن التطور إنما يقوم على أساس الطفرة التي تحدث فجأة وبالمصادفة ، لا على أساس انتخاب الأصلح كما يقول داروين . ويقولون إن التغيرات بعد أن تتم فجأة وعلى سبيل الطفرة التي لا يستبين فيها سبب غائي تتسجل فوراً في الذخيرة الوراثية ، حيث تنتقل بعـد ذلك إلى السلالة بعامل من الوراثة
•
وإذاً فإن هذا المذهب لا يقبل فكرة الاصطفاء الذي أطال داروين في افتراضها وتصورها ، بل يجعل للمصادفة الدور الرئيسي في تكون الأنواع وتكاثرها ، مع الاعتراف بما للوسط الذي ينشأ فيه الحيوان من أثر ثابت على كمية التغيير ونوعيته
Neo-Darwinism: The many criticisms directed at Darwin's theory had a great impact on its decline and a period of its fall and deterioration. But a group of researchers returned and built from its ruins another new theory, later called 'Neo-Darwinism,' considered a corrected version of Darwin's theory. The leader of these researchers was the Dutch scientist Hugo de Vries, then a group of biologists, mostly English and American, supported and backed him. The most important foundation of this new school, considered a fundamental distinction from Darwin's theory, is what became established among these others: that evolution is based on mutation that occurs suddenly and by chance, not on the basis of the survival of the fittest as Darwin said. They say that after changes occur suddenly and as mutations in which no teleological cause is discernible, they are immediately recorded in the genetic heritage, and then transmitted to the lineage through a factor of heredity. So this school does not accept the idea of selection which Darwin elaborated in his assumption and concept; rather, it makes chance the primary role in the formation and multiplication of species, while acknowledging the fixed effect of the environment in which the animal develops on the quantity and quality of change.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage introduces neo-Darwinism as a response to the criticisms of classical Darwinism. The author explains that after Darwin's theory fell into decline, some researchers revived it in a corrected form called neo-Darwinism, led by Hugo de Vries. The key distinction is that neo-Darwinism rejects natural selection (al-istifa') as the primary mechanism and instead posits that evolution occurs through sudden, random mutations (tufra). These mutations are then inherited and become fixed in the gene pool. The school grants chance the primary role, while acknowledging that the environment has an effect on the quantity and quality of change.

الداروينية الجديدة
الطفرة
المصادفة
الاصطفاء
الذخيرة الوراثية
الوسط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Neo-Darwinism is essentially the same as Darwin's theory.
Correction: The author clarifies that neo-Darwinism differs fundamentally by replacing natural selection with random mutation as the primary mechanism.

Checkpoint
What is the main difference between Darwin's theory and neo-Darwinism according to the author?
A) Neo-Darwinism emphasizes natural selection
B) Neo-Darwinism rejects common descent
C) Neo-Darwinism replaces natural selection with random mutation
D) Neo-Darwinism accepts Lamarckian inheritance

Key Takeaway
Neo-Darwinism emerged as a response to criticisms of Darwin's theory, positing that evolution is driven by random mutations rather than natural selection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The passage states that mutations occur 'by chance with no discernible purpose.' Have you ever considered that if this is true, then your own intelligence, morality, and sense of right and wrong are also random accidents? How does that sit with your heart, and what does it drive you to seek?

Neo-Darwinism: Its Origin and Core Ideas
Buti describes the emergence of Neo-Darwinism and its central doctrine of mutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical context of Neo-Darwinism and its key claim that evolution occurs through sudden, chance mutations rather than natural selection.

Core Idea
Neo-Darwinism replaces natural selection with random mutation as the driver of evolution.

Buti begins by explaining how Darwin's original theory faced heavy criticism and fell into decline. However, a group of researchers, led by Hugo de Vries, revived it in a new form called Neo-Darwinism, which they considered a corrected version. This lesson introduces the core idea of Neo-Darwinism: that evolution is driven by sudden, random mutations rather than gradual natural selection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully.
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse. Then read the translation. Let the author's historical narrative come through.
Notice the historical context: the collapse of Darwin's theory.
2
Identify the key difference from Darwinism.
Buti states the fundamental difference: evolution via sudden, chance mutation (الطفرة) versus natural selection (انتخاب الأصلح). Find that sentence.
3
Understand the role of chance and heredity.
Buti explains that mutations are not goal-directed and are immediately inherited. Notice how chance is given the principal role.
4
Note the environmental influence.
Buti acknowledges that the environment has a stable effect on the quantity and quality of change. This is a nuance.

Source Text

كان للانتقادات الكثيرة التي توجهت إلى نظرية داروين أثر كبير في أن تتهاوى ويمر عليها عهد من السقوط والتردّي ، ولكن طائفة من الباحثين عادوا فأشادوا من أنقاضها نظرية أخرى جديدة أطلق عليها فيما بعد اسم : الداروينية الجديدة ، اعتبرت بمثابة النسخة المصححة لنظرية داروين
وقد تزعم هؤلاء الباحثين العالم الهولندي Hugo de Veries
ثم شايعه ودعمه في ذلك طائفة من علماء الحيــاة أكثرهم إنكليزيــون وأمريكيون
وأهم ما ينهض عليه هذا المذهب الجديد ويعتبر فارقاً أسـاسـيـاً يتميز به عن نظرية داروين ما قد ترجح عند هؤلاء الآخرين من أن التطور إنما يقوم على أساس الطفرة التي تحدث فجأة وبالمصادفة ، لا على أساس انتخاب الأصلح كما يقول داروين . ويقولون إن التغيرات بعد أن تتم فجأة وعلى سبيل الطفرة التي لا يستبين فيها سبب غائي تتسجل فوراً في الذخيرة الوراثية ، حيث تنتقل بعـد ذلك إلى السلالة بعامل من الوراثة

وإذاً فإن هذا المذهب لا يقبل فكرة الاصطفاء الذي أطال داروين في افتراضها وتصورها ، بل يجعل للمصادفة الدور الرئيسي في تكون الأنواع وتكاثرها ، مع الاعتراف بما للوسط الذي ينشأ فيه الحيوان من أثر ثابت على كمية التغيير ونوعيته

نقد الداروينية الجديدة :
غير أن هذه « النسخة المصححة « لمذهب داروين استهدفت هي الأخرى انتقادات كثيرة ووقعت تحت نقائض لم تجد أي مفر منها . وإليك بعض هذه الانتقادات :
1 - إن التطور المفروض الذي هو أصل البحث ، تطور تقدمي ولا ريب ، التفسير المقترح لتدرج أصناف الحيوانات على ضوئه . فهل من شأن الطفرة أن تنطوي على هذا التطور التقدمي المطرد ؟
إذ هو
،
المعروف أن الطفرة إنما تنطوي دائماً على صفات الانتقاص والاضطراب وهل الموت وما يكون بين يديه من أسباب ومقدمات إلا من أبرز مظاهر الطفرة ؟ .. فكيف يفسر التطور التصاعدي المطرد على أساس من هذا العامل الانتقاصي المضطرب ؟
وبتعبير آخر ، لماذا لا تتجه الطفرة يوماً ما في سيرها بالركب الحيواني ، نحو الانتكاس إلى الخلف بدلاً من الصعود الشاق الدائب إلى الأمام
ولا ريب أن اعتماد أي إجابة موضوعية على هذه الأسئلة ، كفيل بأن يؤدي إلى انهيار هذه النظرية الجديدة من أساسها .
٢ - إذا كانت الطفرة هي التي تتحكم فيما يطرأ على الكائن الحي من تغير وتطور ، فأي موجب يبقى لافتراض نشأة الكائنات الحية من أصل واحد ؟ .. إذ من المعلوم أن هذا الافتراض إنما لاقى القبول عند أصحابه بناء على ما لاحظوه من الشبه التصاعدي بين هذه الكائنات الملاحظة التي جعلتهم يقولون بمبدأ وهي الاصطفاء وانتخاب الأصلح .
فإذا نسف هذا المبدأ بافتراض الطفرة ، فلا بد من تجاهل ظاهرة التشابه
Neo-Darwinism:
The numerous criticisms directed at Darwin's theory had a great effect in causing it to collapse and pass through a period of decline and deterioration, but a group of researchers returned and built from its ruins another new theory, later called Neo-Darwinism, considered as a corrected version of Darwin's theory.
The Dutch scientist Hugo de Vries led these researchers,
then a group of biologists, most of them English and American, supported and backed him in that.
And the most important thing upon which this new doctrine is based and which is considered a fundamental difference distinguishing it from Darwin's theory is what these others have come to believe: that evolution occurs on the basis of mutation (al-ṭafra) that happens suddenly and by chance, not on the basis of natural selection (intikhāb al-aṣlaḥ) as Darwin says. And they say that after changes occur suddenly and by way of mutation (ṭafra) in which no final cause (sabab ghāʼī) is apparent, they are immediately recorded in the genetic heritage, then transmitted thereafter to the offspring by a factor of heredity.
•
Therefore, this doctrine does not accept the idea of natural selection (al-iṣṭifāʼ) which Darwin extensively assumed and conceived, but instead assigns to chance the principal role in the formation and multiplication of species, while acknowledging the stable effect of the environment in which the animal arises on the quantity and quality of change.

Critique of Neo-Darwinism:
However, this 'corrected version' of Darwin's doctrine also became the target of many criticisms and fell into contradictions it could not escape. Here are some of these criticisms:
1 - The supposed evolution that is the subject of research is progressive evolution without doubt, and the proposed explanation for the gradation of animal species is based on it. So is mutation capable of containing this steady progressive evolution?
For it is known that mutation only ever contains characteristics of deficiency and disorder. Is death and what precedes it by way of causes and preludes anything other than the most prominent manifestations of mutation? So how can continuous upward evolution be explained on the basis of this deficient and disordered factor?
In other words, why does mutation not sometimes direct the animal procession towards regression backward instead of the arduous and persistent upward climb?
There is no doubt that adopting any objective answer to these questions would lead to the collapse of this new theory from its foundations.
2 - If mutation is what controls the change and evolution that occur in the living being, then what reason remains for assuming the origin of living beings from a single ancestor? For it is known that this assumption found acceptance among its proponents based on what they observed of the upward similarity among these observed beings, which led them to affirm the principle of natural selection and survival of the fittest (al-iṣṭifāʼ wa-intikhāb al-aṣlaḥ).
If this principle is demolished by assuming mutation, then the phenomenon of similarity must be ignored
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a combination of exposition and critique. It first defines Neo-Darwinism, then presents two criticisms against it. The author, Ramadan Buti, begins by noting that Darwin's original theory fell out of favor due to criticisms, but a new version arose: Neo-Darwinism, led by Hugo de Vries. The key difference from Darwinism is that Neo-Darwinism grounds evolution in sudden, chance mutations rather than gradual natural selection. Mutations are not goal-directed and are immediately inherited. This doctrine rejects natural selection as the main driver, giving chance the primary role, while acknowledging environmental influence on the quantity and quality of change.

The critique then follows, stating that Neo-Darwinism also faces serious objections. The first criticism is that if evolution is progressive (moving from simple to complex), mutations cannot account for this because they are typically degenerative (causing loss or disorder). Death itself is a manifestation of mutation. So how can upward evolution come from a source that tends downward? Mutation should sometimes cause regression, but it does not. Therefore, the theory collapses unless an objective answer is given.

The second criticism (incomplete on the page) challenges the idea of common ancestry: if mutation is the mechanism, then the evidence from structural similarities between species—which originally supported common descent via natural selection—becomes meaningless. If natural selection is rejected, the similarity argument loses its basis. The passage ends mid-sentence, implying the criticism continues.

Key Terms
الداروينية الجديدة
الطفرة
الاصطفاء
انتخاب الأصلح

D) Neo-Darwinism ignores environmental influence.

Key Takeaway

When you observe the astonishing complexity of life around you, do you find it easier to believe it arose from random mutations or to marvel at the hand of a purposeful Creator? What does your answer reveal about the state of your faith?
?
If mutations have no final cause (sabab ghāʼī) as Neo-Darwinism claims, then life's order is mere illusion. Do you live as if your own existence has purpose, or have you allowed the idea of randomness to creep into your heart? What will you do to affirm your belief in Allah's purpose for you today?
