Critique of Neo-Darwinism: The Problem of Mutation
Buti presents two criticisms of Neo-Darwinism focusing on the inadequacy of mutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two powerful criticisms against Neo-Darwinism: that mutations cannot produce progressive evolution, and that the mutation mechanism undermines the evidence for common ancestry.

Core Idea
Mutations are degenerative, not progressive, so they cannot explain upward evolution.

Buti now turns to critique the 'corrected version' of Darwinism. He argues that Neo-Darwinism faces its own serious problems. The first criticism is that mutations are inherently defective and disorderly, so they cannot account for the progressive complexity observed in evolution. The second criticism (though incomplete in the text) challenges the basis for inferring common ancestry from similarities if natural selection is rejected. This lesson presents these criticisms as found in the source.

Guided Path
1
Read the criticism passage.
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that Buti introduces two numbered criticisms.
2
Understand the first criticism.
Buti argues that mutations are characterized by deficiency and disorder, using death as an example. Therefore they cannot produce upward evolution.
He asks: why don't mutations sometimes cause regression?
3
Consider the second criticism.
If mutation is the mechanism, the argument from similarity for common ancestry collapses because that argument relied on natural selection.
The passage ends mid-argument, but the point is clear.
4
Reflect on the overall conclusion.
Buti states that any objective answer to these questions would lead to the collapse of Neo-Darwinism.

كان للانتقادات الكثيرة التي توجهت إلى نظرية داروين أثر كبير في أن تتهاوى ويمر عليها عهد من السقوط والتردّي ، ولكن طائفة من الباحثين عادوا فأشادوا من أنقاضها نظرية أخرى جديدة أطلق عليها فيما بعد اسم : الداروينية الجديدة ، اعتبرت بمثابة النسخة المصححة لنظرية داروين

ثم شايعه ودعمه في ذلك طائفة من علماء الحيــاة أكثرهم إنكليزيــون وأمريكيون

نقد الداروينية الجديدة :
غير أن هذه « النسخة المصححة « لمذهب داروين استهدفت هي الأخرى انتقادات كثيرة ووقعت تحت نقائض لم تجد أي مفر منها . وإليك بعض هذه الانتقادات :

،

Neo-Darwinism:
The numerous criticisms directed at Darwin's theory had a great effect in causing it to collapse and pass through a period of decline and deterioration, but a group of researchers returned and built from its ruins another new theory, later called Neo-Darwinism, considered as a corrected version of Darwin's theory.
The Dutch scientist Hugo de Vries led these researchers,
then a group of biologists, most of them English and American, supported and backed him in that.
And the most important thing upon which this new doctrine is based and which is considered a fundamental difference distinguishing it from Darwin's theory is what these others have come to believe: that evolution occurs on the basis of mutation (al-ṭafra) that happens suddenly and by chance, not on the basis of natural selection (intikhāb al-aṣlaḥ) as Darwin says. And they say that after changes occur suddenly and by way of mutation (ṭafra) in which no final cause (sabab ghāʼī) is apparent, they are immediately recorded in the genetic heritage, then transmitted thereafter to the offspring by a factor of heredity.
•
Therefore, this doctrine does not accept the idea of natural selection (al-iṣṭifāʼ) which Darwin extensively assumed and conceived, but instead assigns to chance the principal role in the formation and multiplication of species, while acknowledging the stable effect of the environment in which the animal arises on the quantity and quality of change.

Critique of Neo-Darwinism:
However, this 'corrected version' of Darwin's doctrine also became the target of many criticisms and fell into contradictions it could not escape. Here are some of these criticisms:
1 - The supposed evolution that is the subject of research is progressive evolution without doubt, and the proposed explanation for the gradation of animal species is based on it. So is mutation capable of containing this steady progressive evolution?
For it is known that mutation only ever contains characteristics of deficiency and disorder. Is death and what precedes it by way of causes and preludes anything other than the most prominent manifestations of mutation? So how can continuous upward evolution be explained on the basis of this deficient and disordered factor?
In other words, why does mutation not sometimes direct the animal procession towards regression backward instead of the arduous and persistent upward climb?
There is no doubt that adopting any objective answer to these questions would lead to the collapse of this new theory from its foundations.
2 - If mutation is what controls the change and evolution that occur in the living being, then what reason remains for assuming the origin of living beings from a single ancestor? For it is known that this assumption found acceptance among its proponents based on what they observed of the upward similarity among these observed beings, which led them to affirm the principle of natural selection and survival of the fittest (al-iṣṭifāʼ wa-intikhāb al-aṣlaḥ).
If this principle is demolished by assuming mutation, then the phenomenon of similarity must be ignored
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a combination of exposition and critique. It first defines Neo-Darwinism, then presents two criticisms against it. The author, Ramadan Buti, begins by noting that Darwin's original theory fell out of favor due to criticisms, but a new version arose: Neo-Darwinism, led by Hugo de Vries. The key difference from Darwinism is that Neo-Darwinism grounds evolution in sudden, chance mutations rather than gradual natural selection. Mutations are not goal-directed and are immediately inherited. This doctrine rejects natural selection as the main driver, giving chance the primary role, while acknowledging environmental influence on the quantity and quality of change.

The critique then follows, stating that Neo-Darwinism also faces serious objections. The first criticism is that if evolution is progressive (moving from simple to complex), mutations cannot account for this because they are typically degenerative (causing loss or disorder). Death itself is a manifestation of mutation. So how can upward evolution come from a source that tends downward? Mutation should sometimes cause regression, but it does not. Therefore, the theory collapses unless an objective answer is given.

The second criticism (incomplete on the page) challenges the idea of common ancestry: if mutation is the mechanism, then the evidence from structural similarities between species—which originally supported common descent via natural selection—becomes meaningless. If natural selection is rejected, the similarity argument loses its basis. The passage ends mid-sentence, implying the criticism continues.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mutations always lead to progressive evolution.
Correction: Buti points out that mutations are characterized by deficiency and disorder, not progress.

Checkpoint
What is the first criticism Buti makes against Neo-Darwinism?
A) Mutations are too rare to cause significant change.
B) Mutations are generally harmful and cannot produce upward evolution.
C) Mutations are not inherited by offspring.
D) Mutations are directed by the environment.

Key Takeaway
Buti's first criticism shows that mutations, being generally degenerative, are an unsuitable mechanism for progressive evolution, while the second criticism questions the basis for common ancestry without natural selection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What would it take for you to examine the assumptions behind any belief you hold, even if it feels unsettling? Will you commit to critically evaluating the origins of life as taught in modern science, or will you remain comfortable with what you've been told?
?
Buti says mutation only yields deficiency and disorder—think of death as its ultimate manifestation. In your own life, are the 'mutations' or changes you experience leading you toward growth or decay? What specific steps can you take today to ensure that your direction is upward, guided by revelation rather than random chance?
?
If the principle of common ancestry collapses without natural selection, as Buti argues, what does that mean for your understanding of human origins? Are you willing to accept that humans may not share a common ancestor with other species, even if that goes against mainstream science? How does this affect your view of human purpose and accountability?

First Objection: Mutation Cannot Explain Progressive Evolution
The author states the first objection to mutation theory: mutation is inherently deficient and cannot explain progressive evolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author argues that mutation, being degenerative, cannot account for steady progressive evolution.

Core Idea
Mutation leads to deficiency, not advancement, so it cannot explain upward evolution.

The author begins by noting that the revised version of Darwinism still faces severe criticisms. The first objection directly challenges the core mechanism of mutation: how can a process that produces defects and death possibly drive the continuous improvement seen in the fossil record? This lesson unpacks that objection.

Guided Path

Notice how the author describes mutation as always involving deficiency and disorder, using death as an example.

The author asks why mutation does not sometimes lead to regression instead of always progressing. Reflect on the implications.
4

أولاً ـ فكرة التطور وما يتبعها من انتخاب الأصلح ونحوه ، لم تتجاوز بعــد مرحلة الفرضية التي تتجاذبها الشواهد والاستدلالات المتناقضة . وكل ما قيل أو كتب فيها لا يعدو أن يكون محاولات مبتورة وبحوثاً مجزأة تثير مزيداً من مشكلاتها أكثر مما تحل شيئاً من معضلاتها

Critique of Neo-Darwinism:
But this 'corrected version' of Darwin's doctrine also faced many criticisms and fell into contradictions from which it could find no escape. Here are some of these criticisms:
1 - The supposed evolution which is the basis of the inquiry is undoubtedly progressive evolution, the proposed explanation for the gradation of species of animals in its light. So is mutation capable of containing this steady progressive evolution? For it is known that mutation always involves qualities of deficiency and disorder. Are not death and what precedes it of causes and introductions among the most prominent manifestations of mutation? So how can steady upward evolution be explained on the basis of this disruptive deficient factor? In other words, why does mutation not one day direct its course with the animal kingdom towards regression backward instead of the arduous constant ascent forward? Undoubtedly, adopting any objective answer to these questions is sufficient to lead to the collapse of this new theory from its foundation.
2 - If mutation is what controls the change and evolution that occur in the living organism, what reason remains for assuming the origin of living beings from a single ancestor? For it is known that this assumption was accepted by its proponents based on what they observed of the ascending similarity among these observed beings which made them adopt the principle of natural selection and survival of the fittest. So if this principle is demolished by the assumption of mutation, then the phenomenon of tangible ascending similarity among the classes of living beings must be ignored. At that time, no acceptable basis remains for the assumption of the unity of animal origin. Thus, the doctrine of mutation carries within itself the factors of destruction for the idea of evolution from its foundation.
3 - The claim that the law of inheritance embraces the mutational push that supposedly drove the animal at some time in its specific or 'lineage' lifespan to an evolutionary leap, without any indication of what might be considered a semblance of evidence for this leap, is nothing more than concealing the weakness of this view behind the system of inheritance. For it is natural for the researcher to ask about any landmark that can indicate to us, even remotely, any historical era in which a mutation appeared for some animal, that is, before it disappeared into the hidden recesses of genetic oblivion!
Later:
Afterwards, all of this was a summary of the modern opinions and doctrines that arose in conflict and succession regarding the hypothesis of evolution concerning the living being in general and man in particular. So what does the scale of scientific vision record regarding the subject after all that? It immediately records the following points:
First - The idea of evolution and what follows from it of natural selection and the like has not yet surpassed the stage of hypothesis, which is pulled by contradictory evidences and arguments. Everything that has been said or written about it is nothing but incomplete attempts and fragmented researches that raise more of its problems than they solve any of its difficulties.
Second - The nature of this conflict that we have reviewed is a nature of bewilderment.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage presents a critique of neo-Darwinism (the mutation theory of evolution). The author first states that the 'corrected version' of Darwinism has faced many criticisms and contradictions. He then enumerates three specific objections.

The first objection (1) challenges the claim that mutation can produce steady progressive evolution. The author argues that mutation is known to involve qualities of deficiency and disorder, as seen in death and its causes. Therefore, it cannot explain continuous upward evolution; rather, mutation should sometimes lead to regression. Any objective answer to this dilemma would collapse the theory.

The second objection (2) targets the assumption of a common ancestor. If mutation is the mechanism of change, then the observable ascending similarity among species—which originally led scientists to posit common descent and natural selection—must be ignored. Without that similarity, there is no basis for the hypothesis of a single origin. Thus, mutation itself destroys the idea of evolution from its foundation.

The third objection (3) criticizes the appeal to the law of inheritance to explain mutational leaps. The author says this is merely a cover for the weakness of the theory because there is no evidence or historical marker for any such mutation. Researchers cannot point to any time or place where a mutation occurred before it vanished into genetic history.

After these objections, the author summarizes by stating that all modern opinions on evolution are in conflict. He concludes with two points: First, evolution remains a hypothesis with contradictory evidence and unsolved problems. Second, the nature of the debate is one of bewilderment (the passage ends here, possibly incomplete).

تطور تصاعدي

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mutation always leads to progressive evolution.
Correction: The author shows that mutation is degenerative and disruptive, making it unsuitable as a driver of progressive evolution.

Checkpoint

A) Mutation causes steady progressive evolution.
B) Mutation always involves deficiency and disorder, so it cannot explain progressive evolution.
C) Mutation is proven by inheritance.
D) Mutation supports common ancestry.

Key Takeaway
Mutation, being inherently deficient, cannot serve as the mechanism for progressive evolution.

Second Objection: Mutation Contradicts Common Ancestry
The author presents the second objection: mutation disproves the unity of origin by negating the evidence of ascending similarity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author argues that the mutation hypothesis undermines the assumption of a common ancestor.

Core Idea
Mutation destroys the evidence for a single origin by removing the basis for observed similarities.

The second objection targets the assumption of a common ancestor, which was originally inferred from the gradual similarity among species. If mutation is the mechanism, then this similarity becomes irrelevant, and the hypothesis of a single origin loses its foundation. This lesson explores that argument.

4

ولا ريب أن اعتماد أي إجابة موضوعية على هذه الأسئلة ، كفيل بأن يؤدي إلى انهيار هذه النظرية الجديدة من أساسها .
٢ - إذا كانت الطفرة هي التي تتحكم فيما يطرأ على الكائن الحي من تغير وتطور ، فأي موجب يبقى لافتراض نشأة الكائنات الحية من أصل واحد ؟ .. إذ من المعلوم أن هذا الافتراض إنما لاقى القبول عند أصحابه بناء على ما لاحظوه من الشبه التصاعدي بين هذه الكائنات الملاحظة التي جعلتهم يقولون بمبدأ وهي الاصطفاء وانتخاب الأصلح .
فإذا نسف هذا المبدأ بافتراض الطفرة ، فلا بد من تجاهل ظاهرة التشابه التصاعدي الملموس بين أصناف الأحياء . وعندئذ لا يبقى لافتراض وحدة الأصل الحيواني آي وجه مقبول
وهكذا فإن القول بالطفرة يحمل في طواياه عوامل التدمير لفكرة التطور من أساسها .
٣ - إن القول باحتضان قانون الوراثة للدفع الطفري الذي يفترض أنه ساق الحيوان في وقت ما من عمره النوعي أو « السلالي » إلى قفزة تطورية ، دون الإشارة إلى ما قد يعتبر شبه دليل على هذه القفزة ، ليس أكثر من ستر لضعف هذا الرأي وراء نظام الوراثة
إذ من الطبيعي أن يتساءل الباحث عن أي معلمة من المعالم التي بإمكانها أن تشير لنا ، ولو عن بعد ، إلى أي حقبة تاريخية ظهرت فيها طفرة ما لحيوان ما ، أي قبل أن تختفي في مكنون الغيب الوراثي !
وبعد :
وبعد ، فقد كان هذا كله خلاصة للآراء والمذاهب الحديثة التي قامت متصارعة متناسخة ، حول فرضية التطور بالنسبة للكائن الحي عموماً والإنسان خصوصاً ، فما الذي يسجله ميزان الرؤية العلمية للموضوع بعد ذلك كله ؟ إنه يسجل على الفور النقاط التالية :
أولاً ـ فكرة التطور وما يتبعها من انتخاب الأصلح ونحوه ، لم تتجاوز بعــد مرحلة الفرضية التي تتجاذبها الشواهد والاستدلالات المتناقضة . وكل ما قيل أو كتب فيها لا يعدو أن يكون محاولات مبتورة وبحوثاً مجزأة تثير مزيداً من مشكلاتها أكثر مما تحل شيئاً من معضلاتها
ثانياً - إن طبيعة هذا الصراع الذي استعرضناه هي طبيعة حيرة
Critique of Neo-Darwinism:
But this 'corrected version' of Darwin's doctrine also faced many criticisms and fell into contradictions from which it could find no escape. Here are some of these criticisms:
1 - The supposed evolution which is the basis of the inquiry is undoubtedly progressive evolution, the proposed explanation for the gradation of species of animals in its light. So is mutation capable of containing this steady progressive evolution? For it is known that mutation always involves qualities of deficiency and disorder. Are not death and what precedes it of causes and introductions among the most prominent manifestations of mutation? So how can steady upward evolution be explained on the basis of this disruptive deficient factor? In other words, why does mutation not one day direct its course with the animal kingdom towards regression backward instead of the arduous constant ascent forward? Undoubtedly, adopting any objective answer to these questions is sufficient to lead to the collapse of this new theory from its foundation.
2 - If mutation is what controls the change and evolution that occur in the living organism, what reason remains for assuming the origin of living beings from a single ancestor? For it is known that this assumption was accepted by its proponents based on what they observed of the ascending similarity among these observed beings which made them adopt the principle of natural selection and survival of the fittest. So if this principle is demolished by the assumption of mutation, then the phenomenon of tangible ascending similarity among the classes of living beings must be ignored. At that time, no acceptable basis remains for the assumption of the unity of animal origin. Thus, the doctrine of mutation carries within itself the factors of destruction for the idea of evolution from its foundation.
3 - The claim that the law of inheritance embraces the mutational push that supposedly drove the animal at some time in its specific or 'lineage' lifespan to an evolutionary leap, without any indication of what might be considered a semblance of evidence for this leap, is nothing more than concealing the weakness of this view behind the system of inheritance. For it is natural for the researcher to ask about any landmark that can indicate to us, even remotely, any historical era in which a mutation appeared for some animal, that is, before it disappeared into the hidden recesses of genetic oblivion!
Later:
Afterwards, all of this was a summary of the modern opinions and doctrines that arose in conflict and succession regarding the hypothesis of evolution concerning the living being in general and man in particular. So what does the scale of scientific vision record regarding the subject after all that? It immediately records the following points:
First - The idea of evolution and what follows from it of natural selection and the like has not yet surpassed the stage of hypothesis, which is pulled by contradictory evidences and arguments. Everything that has been said or written about it is nothing but incomplete attempts and fragmented researches that raise more of its problems than they solve any of its difficulties.
Second - The nature of this conflict that we have reviewed is a nature of bewilderment.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage presents a critique of neo-Darwinism (the mutation theory of evolution). The author first states that the 'corrected version' of Darwinism has faced many criticisms and contradictions. He then enumerates three specific objections.

The first objection (1) challenges the claim that mutation can produce steady progressive evolution. The author argues that mutation is known to involve qualities of deficiency and disorder, as seen in death and its causes. Therefore, it cannot explain continuous upward evolution; rather, mutation should sometimes lead to regression. Any objective answer to this dilemma would collapse the theory.

The second objection (2) targets the assumption of a common ancestor. If mutation is the mechanism of change, then the observable ascending similarity among species—which originally led scientists to posit common descent and natural selection—must be ignored. Without that similarity, there is no basis for the hypothesis of a single origin. Thus, mutation itself destroys the idea of evolution from its foundation.

The third objection (3) criticizes the appeal to the law of inheritance to explain mutational leaps. The author says this is merely a cover for the weakness of the theory because there is no evidence or historical marker for any such mutation. Researchers cannot point to any time or place where a mutation occurred before it vanished into genetic history.

After these objections, the author summarizes by stating that all modern opinions on evolution are in conflict. He concludes with two points: First, evolution remains a hypothesis with contradictory evidence and unsolved problems. Second, the nature of the debate is one of bewilderment (the passage ends here, possibly incomplete).

Key Terms
طفرة
افتراض وحدة الأصل
انتخاب الأصلح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Mutation and natural selection both support common ancestry.
Correction: The author argues that mutation, by being random and disruptive, actually undermines the selective process that was used to infer common ancestry.

Checkpoint
According to the second objection, what is the basis for assuming a common ancestor?
A) Mutation theory
B) Observed ascending similarity and natural selection
C) Genetic inheritance
D) The fossil record

Key Takeaway
Mutation destroys the evidential basis for common ancestry, leaving the assumption unsupported.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a widely accepted scientific claim, do you ever pause to examine whether its internal assumptions are consistent, or do you accept it because it is popular? How can this lesson's exposure of a contradiction reshape your approach to evaluating ideas?
?
Think of a belief you once held strongly but eventually abandoned because its supporting arguments crumbled under scrutiny. What did that experience teach you about the importance of foundational consistency? How does this lesson reinforce that lesson?
?
This argument shows that one part of a theory (mutation) can undermine another part (natural selection) on which the whole theory relies. Are there areas in your own life where mutually exclusive beliefs or actions coexist, weakening your overall position? What will you do today to identify and resolve one such inconsistency?

Third Objection: Mutation Lacks Evidence in Inheritance
The author presents the third objection: the mutation hypothesis lacks empirical evidence and hides behind the concept of inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author criticizes the appeal to inheritance as a cover for the lack of evidence for mutational leaps.

Core Idea
Claiming mutation is hidden in inheritance is just a way to conceal the theory's weakness.

The third objection addresses the claim that the law of inheritance can accommodate mutational leaps without leaving traces. The author argues that this is a mere verbal cover for the absence of any historical evidence for mutations. This lesson examines that critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the third objection.
2
Identify the claim being criticized
The claim is that inheritance embraces the mutational push that causes evolutionary leaps.
3
See the author's rebuttal
The author says there is no evidence or historical landmark for any mutation; the claim is just hiding weakness.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The objection concludes that the theory lacks empirical support and relies on an abstract concept.

Conclusion: Evolution Remains a Hypothetical Bewilderment
The author concludes that evolution remains a hypothesis and the debate is characterized by bewilderment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's final assessment that evolution remains an unresolved hypothesis mired in contradictory evidence.

Core Idea
Evolution is still just a hypothesis, not a proven fact, and its debate ends in bewilderment.

After presenting three objections to neo-Darwinism, the author steps back to summarize the state of the debate. He declares that evolution remains a hypothesis, with fragmented research and conflicting evidence, and that the conflict itself leads to bafflement. This lesson captures that conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the concluding passage
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the author's final assessment.
2
Identify the first point
The author states that evolution has not surpassed the stage of hypothesis, with contradictory evidence and fragmented research.
3
Identify the second point
The author describes the nature of the conflict as bewilderment.
4
Reflect on the overall critique
Consider how the three objections lead to this conclusion: evolution is not a proven fact but a problematic hypothesis.

At that time, no acceptable basis remains for the assumption of the unity of animal origin. Thus, the doctrine of mutation carries within itself the factors of destruction for the idea of evolution from its foundation.
3 - The claim that the law of inheritance embraces the mutational push that supposedly drove the animal at some time in its specific or 'lineage' lifespan to an evolutionary leap, without any indication of what might be considered a semblance of evidence for this leap, is nothing more than concealing the weakness of this view behind the system of inheritance. For it is natural for the researcher to ask about any landmark that can indicate to us, even remotely, any historical era in which a mutation appeared for some animal, that is, before it disappeared into the hidden recesses of genetic oblivion!
Later:
Afterwards, all of this was a summary of the modern opinions and doctrines that arose in conflict and succession regarding the hypothesis of evolution concerning the living being in general and man in particular. So what does the scale of scientific vision record regarding the subject after all that? It immediately records the following points:
First - The idea of evolution and what follows from it of natural selection and the like has not yet surpassed the stage of hypothesis, which is pulled by contradictory evidences and arguments. Everything that has been said or written about it is nothing but incomplete attempts and fragmented researches that raise more of its problems than they solve any of its difficulties.
Second - The nature of this conflict that we have reviewed is a nature of bewilderment.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage presents a critique of neo-Darwinism (the mutation theory of evolution). The author first states that the 'corrected version' of Darwinism has faced many criticisms and contradictions. He then enumerates three specific objections.

The first objection (1) challenges the claim that mutation can produce steady progressive evolution. The author argues that mutation is known to involve qualities of deficiency and disorder, as seen in death and its causes. Therefore, it cannot explain continuous upward evolution; rather, mutation should sometimes lead to regression. Any objective answer to this dilemma would collapse the theory.

The second objection (2) targets the assumption of a common ancestor. If mutation is the mechanism of change, then the observable ascending similarity among species—which originally led scientists to posit common descent and natural selection—must be ignored. Without that similarity, there is no basis for the hypothesis of a single origin. Thus, mutation itself destroys the idea of evolution from its foundation.

The third objection (3) criticizes the appeal to the law of inheritance to explain mutational leaps. The author says this is merely a cover for the weakness of the theory because there is no evidence or historical marker for any such mutation. Researchers cannot point to any time or place where a mutation occurred before it vanished into genetic history.

After these objections, the author summarizes by stating that all modern opinions on evolution are in conflict. He concludes with two points: First, evolution remains a hypothesis with contradictory evidence and unsolved problems. Second, the nature of the debate is one of bewilderment (the passage ends here, possibly incomplete).

Key Terms
فرضية التطور
حيرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Evolution is a proven scientific fact.
Correction: The author classifies evolution as still being at the hypothesis stage, not a proven fact.

Checkpoint
According to the conclusion, what stage has the idea of evolution not surpassed?
A) Fact
B) Hypothesis
C) Law
D) Theory

Key Takeaway
Evolution remains an unresolved hypothesis, with the debate defined by bewilderment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Mutation and the Illusion of Hereditary Evidence
Buti argues that invoking heredity for mutations is a cover for lack of evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why invoking heredity as a mechanism for mutation-driven evolution does not solve the lack of empirical evidence.

Core Idea
Heredity cannot disguise the absence of evidence for mutational leaps.

Author Buti delivers a sharp critique of evolutionary theory's reliance on mutation and heredity. He argues that claiming heredity 'absorbs' mutations without proof is just a rhetorical cover. This lesson exposes the logical weakness in that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the rhetorical question at the end.
2
Identify the author's rhetorical question
Find the question the author poses about landmarks of mutation history. This is the core challenge to the evolutionary claim.
The question exposes the gap in evidence.
3
Analyze the logical structure
Break down the passage into three parts: the claim about mutation, the cover of heredity, and the unanswered question. Reflect on how each part builds the argument.
This structure is typical of critical arguments in kalam.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهكذا فإن القول بالطفرة يحمل في طواياه عوامل التدمير لفكرة التطور من أساسها . ٣ - إن القول باحتضان قانون الوراثة للدفع الطفري الذي يفترض أنه ساق الحيوان في وقت ما من عمره النوعي أو « السلالي » إلى قفزة تطورية ، دون الإشارة إلى ما قد يعتبر شبه دليل على هذه القفزة ، ليس أكثر من ستر لضعف هذا الرأي وراء نظام الوراثة إذ من الطبيعي أن يتساءل الباحث عن أي معلمة من المعالم التي بإمكانها أن تشير لنا ، ولو عن بعد ، إلى أي حقبة تاريخية ظهرت فيها طفرة ما لحيوان ما ، أي قبل أن تختفي في مكنون الغيب الوراثي !

The statement that the law of heredity embraces the mutational push which supposedly drove an animal at some time of its specific or 'racial' lifespan to an evolutionary leap, without reference to what might be considered a quasi-proof of this leap, is nothing more than covering the weakness of this opinion behind the system of heredity. Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage presents the third argument against evolutionary theory, focusing on the inadequacy of mutation and heredity as evidence. The author begins by stating that the very claim about mutation contains factors that undermine evolution from its foundation. He then explains that relying on heredity to accommodate a supposed mutational push that caused an evolutionary leap, without providing even a semblance of evidence for such a leap, is merely a way to disguise the weakness of this view behind the concept of heredity. The author then poses a natural question: a researcher would ask for any sign or landmark that could indicate, even remotely, when in history a specific mutation occurred in a specific animal before it disappeared into the hereditary unseen. This rhetorical question highlights the total lack of empirical evidence for mutation-driven evolution.

Correction: Heredity is a mechanism, not evidence; claiming heredity 'absorbs' mutations does not prove that specific mutations occurred or caused evolutionary leaps.

Evolution as Hypothesis: Three Scientific Conclusions
Author enumerates three scientific conclusions about evolution's status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three reasons why evolution remains a hypothesis rather than a scientific fact.

Core Idea
Evolution is still a hypothesis, not a proven fact.

After reviewing modern schools of thought on evolution, the author steps back to assess the scientific status of the theory. He presents three clear conclusions that challenge the idea that evolution is a settled scientific truth. This passage summarizes why, from a scientific perspective, evolution remains an open problem.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the three numbered points the author makes.
The author uses enumeration (first, second, third) to structure his argument.
2
Identify the three points
After reading, list the three points in your own words. The first point is about the hypothesis stage, the second about the nature of the debate, and the third about the inability to form scientific judgments.
3
Reflect on the implications

The author's view is that evolution lacks the hallmarks of a mature scientific theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعد : فقد كان هذا كله خلاصة للآراء والمذاهب الحديثة التي قامت متصارعة متناسخة ، حول فرضية التطور بالنسبة للكائن الحي عموماً والإنسان خصوصاً ، فما الذي يسجله ميزان الرؤية العلمية للموضوع بعد ذلك كله ؟ إنه يسجل على الفور النقاط التالية : أولاً ـ فكرة التطور وما يتبعها من انتخاب الأصلح ونحوه ، لم تتجاوز بعــد مرحلة الفرضية التي تتجاذبها الشواهد والاستدلالات المتناقضة . وكل ما قيل أو كتب فيها لا يعدو أن يكون محاولات مبتورة وبحوثاً مجزأة تثير مزيداً من مشكلاتها أكثر مما تحل شيئاً من معضلاتها ثانياً - إن طبيعة هذا الصراع الذي استعرضناه هي طبيعة حيرة واضطراب ، في موضوع مغلق وليست طبيعة سير منهجي لفهم أمر معلوم الحقيقة محدود النطاق والحجم ثالثاً ـ وبناء على ذلك فإنه لا يجوز إقامة أي حكم علمي على شيء من البحوث والآراء ، ولا يجوز أن نعتبرها بحد ذاتها حقيقة علمية تجاوزها العقل بالقناعة والقبول . وإن في استمرار سلسلة النقض والنقد التي تلاحقها لأبلغ شاهد على ذلك
After that, this is all a summary of the modern opinions and schools that arose conflicting and successive, concerning the hypothesis of evolution regarding living beings in general and humans in particular. So what does the scale of scientific vision record on the subject after all this? It immediately records the following points: First — the idea of evolution and what follows from it of natural selection and the like has not yet exceeded the stage of hypothesis, pulled by contradictory evidence and deductions. Everything said or written about it is nothing but incomplete attempts and fragmented research that raises more problems than it solves any of its difficulties. Second — the nature of this conflict we have reviewed is a nature of confusion and disorder regarding a closed subject, not the nature of a systematic process to understand something known in truth and limited in scope and volume. Third — accordingly, it is not permissible to establish any scientific judgment on any of the research and opinions, nor is it permissible to consider them in themselves a scientific truth that the mind has surpassed with conviction and acceptance. The continued series of refutation and criticism that pursues them is the clearest evidence of that.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage provides the author's concluding summary on the scientific status of evolutionary theory. It begins by stating that the preceding discussion was a summary of modern schools of thought about evolution. Then the author asks what the scientific balance records, and he gives three points. First, evolution and its corollaries like natural selection remain at the hypothesis stage, pulled by contradictory evidence; all writings about it are incomplete attempts that raise more problems than they solve. Second, the nature of the ongoing conflict is one of confusion and disorder about a closed subject, not a systematic understanding of a known truth. Third, consequently, no scientific judgment can be made based on these researches nor can they be considered scientific truths accepted by reason; the continuing criticism itself is the best proof of their inadequacy.

Reflecting on the Afterlife: Buti's Exhortation
Buti warns against heedlessness and urges reflection on the hereafter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's argument that heedlessness about the afterlife is a form of self-deception and that reflection with a pure mind is essential.

Core Idea
The afterlife is as real as the world you have seen.

In this passage, Buti directly addresses the reader, warning against the common tendency to dismiss warnings about the afterlife as mere fantasies. He uses vivid imagery and a compelling analogy to shake the reader out of heedlessness and call them to sincere reflection. The source passage is a powerful exhortation that sets the tone for deeper theological discussions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice Buti's direct address and evocative language.
2
Identify the initial contrasts
Buti begins by stating that the distant is near, the doubtful certain, the opportunity lost, and regret useless. Observe the rhetorical effect of these paired opposites.
3
Examine Buti's analogy about the wonders of the world
Buti compares the denial of the afterlife to the denial of worldly wonders before seeing them. Understand how this analogy reinforces his point.
Think about how you might have reacted if someone described something you've never seen.
4
Understand the metaphor of the mount
The 'mount of night and day' carries you inevitably from this world to the afterlife. Reflect on the inevitability of this journey and the futility of ignoring it.
Buti emphasizes that we cannot stop this movement.
5
Reflect on Buti's conclusion
Buti advises caution and pure reflection, free from self-interest and passions. Consider how this applies to your own life and thoughts about the afterlife.
He says no rational person can offer more than this advice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الموقف بعينك وإذا البعيد قريب ، وإذا المشكوك متحقق وإذا الفرصة فائتة والندم لا يفيد . ولا يجديك أن تسمع هذا الكلام وأنت منصرف عنه غير حافل به تحسبه وهماً من الأوهام ، فلو أن أحداً حدثك عن أعاجيب هذه الدنيا قبل أن تراها ، لكنت لها أشد إنكاراً ولكنت تحسبها أيضاً وهماً من الأوهام . ثم إن مطية الليل والنهار سائرة بك من معبر هذه الدنيا التي دخلتها البارحة وستفارقها غداً ، إلى هذا الهول الذي لا تحفل به ، ولن تستطيع أن توقف حركة هذه المطية عن المسير ، فخير لك أن تحذر وتتأمل بفكر نقي خالص عن شوائب الأغراض والأهواء ولا يملك عقل عاقل أن يبصر صاحبه بأكثر من هذا الذي أقول .
You see with your own eye that the distant is near, the doubtful is certain, the opportunity is lost, and regret is useless. And it will not avail you to hear this speech while you are turning away from it, not caring about it, thinking it to be a mere fancy. If someone had told you of the wonders of this world before you saw them, you would have denied them most vehemently and would have also thought them mere fancies. Then the mount of night and day is carrying you from the crossing of this world—which you entered yesterday and will leave tomorrow—to this terror which you do not care about. And you cannot stop the movement of this mount from journeying. So it is better for you to be cautious and reflect with a pure mind, free from the impurities of self-interests and passions. And no rational person can show his companion more than what I am saying.

Commentary
This passage is an exhortation and warning. Buti begins by addressing the reader directly, urging them to see reality: the distant afterlife is actually near, the doubtful is certain, the opportunity is fleeting, and regret afterwards is useless. He then criticizes those who hear such warnings but are indifferent, dismissing them as illusions. He draws an analogy: if someone had described the wonders of the world before you saw them, you would have denied them; similarly, the afterlife seems unreal only because you have not seen it yet. He then uses the metaphor of a mount (the night and day) that carries a person inexorably from this temporary world to the afterlife. One cannot stop this journey, so the only wise course is to be cautious and reflect with a clear mind, free from bias. Buti concludes that no rational person can offer more than this advice.

Human Function: Execution of Divine Law
Buti defines human function as mere execution and deviation as tyranny.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Buti's definition of human function as mere execution of divine law and the gravity of deviating from it.

Core Idea
Our role is to implement God's law, not to invent our own.

Buti poses a fundamental question: What is humanity's purpose concerning the established truth of divine sovereignty? His answer is direct and uncompromising. This passage clarifies that our function is strictly executive, and any attempt to legislate beyond revelation is an act of rebellion that borders on self-deification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the full argument without analysis.
Notice the rhetorical opening: 'So what is the function of man?'
2
Identify the core claim
Locate the statement that human function is 'mere execution' (التنفيذ فقط). Consider what this excludes.
The word 'only' (فقط) is crucial.
3
Note the exceptions and boundaries
Buti allows ijtihad and consultation only where commanded or where no explicit text or consensus exists. Mark these conditions.
These are not loopholes but limited permissions within the executive framework.
4
Understand the consequence of deviation
Read how Buti describes departure from this function as 'self-deification and tyranny' and explains why it amounts to shirk in legislation.
This is the climax of the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظيفة الإنسان :
وإذا فما هي وظيفة الإنسان في الدنيا تجاه هذه الحقيقة الثابتة ؟ إن وظيفته التنفيذ فقط !.. إنه مسؤول عن تنفيذ كل حرف من القانون الذي أنزله إليه وألزمه به ، لا يجتهد في ذلك إلا حيث أمره بالاجتهاد ، ولا يلجأ إلى شورى في الرأي أو الحكم إلا حيث لا نص صريحاً في كتاب ولا سنة وحيث لا إجماع . وهذه الوظيفة هي المعني بمارسة العبودية لله عز وجل . والخروج عنها أو التمرد عليها هو التأله والطغيان بعينه. إذ الإنسان عنـدمـا يُعرض عن وظيفته التنفيذية هذه ليعكف على وضع تشريع آخر لنفسه إنما يخرج بذلك عن سلطان ربه ويحاول التحرر عن عبوديته له ، ثم يُشرك نفسه معه في التشريع والحكم !..
The function of man: So what is the function of man in this world regarding this established truth? His function is mere execution! He is responsible for executing every letter of the law which He sent down to him and obligated him with. He does not exercise ijtihad in that except where He commanded him to exercise ijtihad, and he does not resort to consultation in opinion or judgment except where there is no explicit text in the Book or the Sunna and where there is no consensus. And this function is meant by practicing servitude to God, Mighty and Majestic. And departing from it or rebelling against it is self-deification and tyranny itself. For when man turns away from this executive function to devote himself to laying down another legislation for himself, he thereby exits from the authority of his Lord and attempts to free himself from servitude to Him, then associates himself with Him in legislation and judgment!
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the human function in life according to Buti. He begins with a rhetorical question: 'What is the function of man in this world regarding this established truth?' The answer is that it is mere execution (التنفيذ فقط). Man is responsible for implementing every letter of the divine law; he may only exercise ijtihad where God has permitted it, and he may resort to consultation only where there is no explicit text from Quran, Sunna, or consensus. Buti then states that this function is precisely what is meant by 'practicing servitude to God' (ممارسة العبودية لله). Any departure or rebellion against this function is described as 'self-deification and tyranny' (التأله والطغيان). He explains why: when man abandons his executive role and sets out to make his own legislation, he exits the authority of his Lord, attempts to free himself from servitude, and ultimately associates himself with God in legislation and judgment—thus committing shirk in the domain of rule-making.

Key Terms
التنفيذ
العبودية
التشريع
التأله
الطغيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the human function includes inventing new laws beyond divine revelation.
Correction: Buti clarifies that it is only execution, not legislation. Even ijtihad and consultation are limited to where no explicit text or consensus exists.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the primary function of humans regarding divine law?
A) To interpret and adapt the law as needed
B) To execute every letter of the law without innovation
C) To focus only on the ends of justice and peace
D) To consult scholars before making decisions

Key Takeaway
Human function is limited to executing divine law; deviating to legislate is an act of self-deification and tyranny.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent decision you made that was not clearly addressed by the Quran or Sunnah. Did you genuinely seek guidance through the permitted means (scholars, principles, shura within limits) or did you simply follow your own reasoning? How does Buti's warning that this is 'exiting the authority of your Lord' sit with your conscience? Will you repent and realign?
?
You claim to be a servant of Allah, but do you secretly harbor the belief that your own mind or culture knows better than revelation in some areas of life? Where exactly? Buti says that making your own legislation is 'self-deification and tyranny.' Can you name one specific rule you have set for yourself that contradicts or adds to divine law? What will you do about it today?
?
Imagine you are part of a community decision-making process. Someone proposes a policy that has no explicit textual basis but seems beneficial. How will you, in light of this lesson, ensure that the process remains within the bounds Buti outlines—namely, that shura is only a last resort when no text or consensus exists? Are you ready to challenge even a popular opinion if it oversteps divine boundaries?

Refutation of the Ends-Means Fallacy
Buti refutes the hypocritical claim that God commands only ends, not means.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the hypocritical claim that God commands only ends (not means) is false, and how Buti refutes it by affirming the inseparability of ends and means in divine law.

Core Idea
In Islam, ends and prescribed means are inseparable; God commands both.

The hypocrites propose a seemingly reasonable excuse: God only cares about justice and peace, leaving humans free to pick methods. Buti exposes this as a fallacy. In this lesson, you will examine their argument and its refutation, learning that divine legislation binds both ends and means.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing; then read the English translation. Let the flow of Buti's argument come through before you interpret.
Notice the rhetorical tone: 'strange and amusing' sets the stage.
2
Identify the hypocrite claim and its universal implication
Find the sentence where the hypocrite states their position: God obligated only the goal. Then notice Buti's counter: all nations claim to pursue justice and peace, differing only in means – so by the hypocrite's logic, all are obedient.
This reveals the absurdity of the claim.
3
Understand Buti's refutation and the correct view
Buti states that God obligated ends exactly by obligating their means. Justice is not an invented concept but the result of following God's specific path. Identify this key corrective statement in the Arabic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللمنافقين في هذا الصدد مخرج عجيب وطريف !.
إن أحدهم ليقول : إنما كلف الله عباده بإقامة شريعة الحب والعدل والابتعاد عن مطارح الظلم والجور .
فعلينا أن نخط السبيل إلى هاتين الغايتين كما نرى وكما يقتضيه الظرف والمصلحة . أي إنه يقول : إن الله كلفنا بالغاية فقط ، أما الوسيلة إليها فنحن الذين نختارها ونضعها
ولعمري إن جميع أمم الأرض من شرق وغرب منفذون لأمر الله قائمون بحكمه على هذا الأساس من الفهم : فما من أمة مؤمنة كانت أم كافرة وملحدة إلا وهي تزعم أنها تتوخى في مذهبها وتشريعها تحقيق العدالة كأحسن ما تكون العدالة ، وإقامة دعائم السلم كأفضل ما يكون السلم ، وما تفرقوا عن بعضهم إلا في اختيار الوسائل والمناهج ، وإنما ذلك شيء تركه الله لاختيــار عبـاده على حد زعم المنافقين !!..
ولكن المسلم الصادق لا يقول هذا ، بل لا يتصور كيف يفهم هذا إن الله عز وجل لم يلزم عباده بالغايات إلا من حيث ألزمهم بوسائلها ولم يكلفهم بالأهداف إلا من حيث كلفهم بالسير في مناهجها ، والعدالة ليست ما يخترعه الإنسان بما يتخذ إليه من وسائل ، ولكنها الغاية التي يصل إليها من وراء السير في شريعة الله تعالى وحكمه .
And the hypocrites have in this regard a strange and amusing way out! One of them says: 'God only obligated His servants to establish the law of love and justice and to avoid the arenas of oppression and tyranny. So we must chart the path to these two goals as we see fit and as circumstance and interest require.' That is, he says: 'God obligated us only with the goal, but the means to it—we choose and set them.' And by my life, all the nations of the earth, east and west, are executors of God's command, upholders of His judgment on this basis of understanding: there is no nation, believer or disbeliever or atheist, except that it claims to intend in its doctrine and legislation the achievement of justice in the best possible form, and the establishment of the pillars of peace in the best possible form, and they differ from one another only in the choice of means and methods. And that is something God left to the choice of His servants, according to the claim of the hypocrites!! But the truthful Muslim does not say this; rather, he cannot conceive how this is understood. Indeed, God Almighty did not obligate His servants with ends except insofar as He obligated them with their means, and He did not charge them with goals except insofar as He charged them with walking in their paths. Justice is not what man invents by way of the means he adopts; rather, it is the goal reached by following the law of God Almighty and His judgment.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes a hypocritical argument. Buti begins by characterizing the hypocrites' excuse as 'strange and amusing' (مخرج عجيب وطريف). The claim they make is that God only commanded the ends (love, justice, avoidance of injustice) and left humans free to choose the means according to circumstance. Buti then points out that all nations, regardless of belief, claim to pursue justice and peace; they differ only in means—exactly what the hypocrites assert God left to human choice. This, he implies, would make their innovation not special but universal, and yet it is false. The truthful Muslim rejects this reasoning. Buti explains that God obligated ends only by also obligating their means; justice is not whatever humans invent but the specific outcome of following God's law. The passage thus upholds the inseparability of ends and means in divine legislation.

Key Terms
الغاية
الوسيلة
المنافقون
المسلم الصادق
العدالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is mistakenly thought that Islam cares only about the outcome (justice) and leaves methods completely open to human choice.
Correction: Buti insists that God has prescribed the means as well; justice is the specific result of following God's law, not an independent goal.

Checkpoint
What is the hypocrites' excuse regarding divine law, according to Buti?
A) That God's law is too difficult to implement
B) That God commanded only ends, allowing humans to choose means
C) That the law was abrogated
D) That only scholars can interpret the law

Key Takeaway
The claim that God commands only ends while humans choose means is a hypocritical fallacy; in reality, divine law prescribes both ends and their specific means.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever justified a prohibited means (like lying or cheating) by telling yourself the end goal was good? How does this passage expose that reasoning as hypocritical?
?
When you are tempted to think that your own judgment of what is 'just' overrides a clear divine command, whose authority are you really following?
?
If all nations claim to pursue justice, what distinguishes your submission to God's will from their pursuit? Will you commit to seeking justice only through the means Allah has prescribed, even when your own reasoning suggests otherwise?

Worship Without Correct Belief Is Worthless
Buti warns that worship is useless with wrong belief about legislation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that abundant worship does not benefit a person if he holds the wrong belief that humans can legislate for themselves or that some divine commands are unsuitable for today.

Core Idea
Worship without submission to divine law is hollow.

Buti issues a stark warning: performing many prayers, supererogatory acts, and remembrances does not save a person from responsibility. If someone believes that humans can legislate for themselves or that some of God's commands are unfit for today, their worship becomes worthless. This lesson explains the severity of such belief as apostasy according to Muslim consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Pay attention to Buti's strong language ('dust, of no value').
2
Identify the two wrong beliefs
Buti mentions two specific beliefs that nullify worship: (1) believing humans can legislate as they wish, and (2) believing some of God's commands are unsuitable today.
3
Understand the consequence: apostasy
Buti cites consensus based on decisive evidence that such belief removes a person from the circle of Islam.
This shows the gravity of the issue.
4
Reflect on the purpose of worship
Ask yourself: What is the point of worship if one rejects God's authority in life? Buti's warning ties worship to acceptance of divine legislation.
Internal connection helps internalize the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أنه لا ينجي الإنسان عن مسؤوليته تجاه تحقيق هذه الوظيفة أن يكون متعبداً كثير الصلوات والنوافل والأذكار . فإن ذلك كله هباء لا قيمة له إذا كان يعتقد أن للإنسان أن يشرع لحياته ما يشاء ، أو إذا كان يعتقد أن في أحكام الله وأوامره ما لا يصلح عليه حال الناس اليوم. لقد اجتمعت كلمة المسلمين كلهم ، بناء على قواطع الأدلة ، أن مثل هذا المعتقد مرتد خارج عن دائرة الإسلام . معذرة كاذبة :
ويعتذر آخرون عن إعراضهم عن تشريع الله ، بأنه تشريع غير صالح للتطبيق ، وبأن التاريخ برهن على أنه غير صالح، ويشرحون برهانهم التاريخي هذا بقولهم: إن المجتمع الإسلامي لم يتحقق كما يريده الإسلام خلال التاريخ الإسلامي كله إلا حقبة يسيرة من الأزمنة المتفرقة ، هي بضع سنوات من آخر حياة النبي الله إلى نهاية خلافة عمر بن الخطاب ، ثم سنوات يسيرة من عهد عمر بن عبد العزيز . أما ما بين ذلك ومـا بعـده فقد كان الإسلام عاجزاً عن عرض نفسه وبسط سلطانه !..
وهذه معذرة كاذبة ليس لها أي ظل من الحقيقة والواقع .
And know that it does not save a person from his responsibility toward fulfilling this function that he be a worshiper, performing many prayers, supererogatory acts, and remembrances. For all that is dust, of no value, if he believes that man may legislate for his life whatever he wishes, or if he believes that in God's judgments and commands there is something that does not suit the condition of people today. The consensus of all Muslims, based on decisive evidence, is that such a belief is apostasy, exiting the circle of Islam. A false excuse: And others excuse their turning away from God's legislation by saying that it is legislation unfit for application, and that history has proven it is unfit. And they explain this historical proof by saying: 'The Islamic society never realized itself as Islam wants it throughout all Islamic history except for a brief period of scattered times—a few years from the end of the Prophet of God's life to the end of the caliphate of Umar ibn al-Khattab, then a few years from the era of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz. As for what was between that and after it, Islam was incapable of presenting itself and extending its authority!' And this is a false excuse that has no shadow of truth and reality.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct but related points. First, Buti issues a stern warning: abundant worship (prayers, supererogatory acts, dhikr) does not absolve a person from his duty to implement divine law. Such worship is worthless if the person believes that humans can legislate for themselves or that some of God's commands are unsuitable for today. He states the consensus of Muslims that such belief is apostasy. Second, Buti addresses another excuse: the claim that divine law is historically inapplicable, evidenced by the brief periods of ideal Islamic society (the Prophet's last years up to Umar ibn al-Khattab, and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz). He dismisses this as a 'false excuse' with no basis in truth. The passage thus reinforces that belief in the completeness and applicability of divine law is non-negotiable, and historical failures do not indicate a flaw in the law itself.

Key Terms
العبادة
الردة
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that performing many prayers and dhikr is enough to be a good Muslim, even if one rejects divine law in societal matters.
Correction: Buti teaches that such worship is worthless if one believes humans can legislate or that some divine commands are outdated. Correct belief in the comprehensiveness and applicability of divine law is essential.

Checkpoint
According to Buti, what is the ruling on a person who performs many prayers but believes that humans can legislate for themselves?
A) He is excused because of his worship
B) His worship is worthless and he is an apostate
C) He is a sinner but still Muslim
D) He only needs to change his belief

Key Takeaway
Worship is only accepted when accompanied by correct belief in the completeness and applicability of divine law; otherwise, it is worthless and constitutes apostasy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You who fill your days with prayer and dhikr, yet harbor the thought that some of Allah's commands are not suited for today: what does Buti say your worship truly is? Will you repent from that belief today?
?
Is there any area of your life where you believe you have the right to decide right and wrong for yourself, apart from Allah's law? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and what will you do about it?
?
The consensus of all Muslims is that such a belief removes one from Islam. Have you ever dismissed this warning as extreme? What step will you take now to ensure your beliefs align with divine legislation in all matters?

The False Excuse of Historical Inapplicability
Buti refutes the excuse that history proves Islamic law inapplicable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the false excuse that Islamic law is historically inapplicable and Buti's refutation of it.

Core Idea
History's failures do not prove the law flawed.

Some people excuse their abandonment of divine law by claiming it has never worked in history except briefly. Buti presents their argument and then dismisses it as a false excuse with no basis in reality. This lesson examines that claim and the response.

Guided Path
1
Read the excuse presented by Buti
Identify the historical argument: that ideal Islamic society only existed briefly (end of Prophet's life to Umar's caliphate, plus brief Umayyad period).
2
Understand the implied conclusion
These people conclude that Islamic law is unfit for application because it has failed historically.
This is a form of historical determinism.
3
Buti's dismissal
Buti calls it a 'false excuse' with 'no shadow of truth and reality.' Reflect on why he rejects it so strongly.
Buti does not elaborate here, but the context implies that the failure is due to human implementation, not the law itself.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider: does the misuse of a system or its partial implementation prove the system invalid? Buti says no.
This connects to the earlier lesson on correct belief.

Why Sins Occurred Under Islamic Rule
Buti defends Islamic rule against the charge that sins prove its absence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the occurrence of sins in Islamic history does not prove that Islamic rule was absent; rather, it reflects universal human fallibility.

Core Idea
Sins in Islamic history prove human fallibility, not failed Sharia implementation.

This passage addresses a common objection: if Islamic rule was truly established, why did sins and crimes still happen? Buti responds by pointing to the Companions themselves who sinned and were punished. He then clarifies that the cause of sin is not the absence of Islamic rule but the inherent imperfection of human beings. This lesson unpacks his argument and its implications for understanding Islamic governance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice that Buti first gives examples of sins and punishments, then states the reason.
Pay attention to the flow from examples to conclusion.
2
Identify the key claim
What is the reason Buti gives for the occurrence of sins? It is not that Islamic rule was absent, but that people are not infallible. Find the exact phrase in Arabic.
Look for the phrase 'غير معصومين'.
3
Reflect on the argument
Why does Buti mention the Companions? What does that example do for his argument? Think about how this defends the idea that Islamic rule was implemented.
Consider the rhetorical power of citing the most righteous generation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستره الله ، وينحرف أخرى فيفتضح أمره ويقام عليه الحد أو ينفذ فيه القصاص . وقد زل أناس من الصحابة أنفسهم فأقيمت عليهم الحدود ، وكان في الناس على امتداد عصر التابعين والأمويين والعباسيين من انحرفوا إلى ارتكاب بعض المعاصي ، ووجد فيهم من مال إلى بعض الشهوات والأهواء ، وكان تحت جنح الظلام وفي ضمير الخفاء بعض الذنوب والآثام ولكن سبب ذلك كله ، أن الناس جميعاً ، ملوكاً كانوا أم رعايا ، غير معصومين ولا منزهين ؛ وليس سببه أن الحكم الإسلامي لم يكن قائماً وأن شريعة الإسلام لم تكن منفذة
And Allah conceals him, and another deviates so his affair is exposed and the prescribed punishment is carried out on him or retribution is executed. And some of the Companions themselves slipped and prescribed punishments were carried out on them, and there were among the people throughout the era of the Followers, the Umayyads, and the Abbasids those who deviated to commit some sins, and among them were those who inclined to some desires and whims, and there were under the cover of darkness and in the secret of concealment some sins and offenses. But the reason for all of that is that all people, kings or subjects, are not infallible nor immaculate; and it is not because Islamic rule was not established and the Sharia of Islam was not implemented.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage is a defense against the claim that historical sins and mistakes prove Islamic rule was never properly implemented. The author acknowledges that sins occurred even among the Companions and later generations, and that capital punishments were applied. He then states that the cause of these sins is human fallibility—people are not infallible—not that Islamic rule was absent. The structure first presents examples of sin and punishment, then establishes the universal principle of human imperfection, and concludes that the occurrence of sin does not negate the existence of Islamic governance.

Key Terms
غير معصومين
الحدود
الحكم الإسلامي
شريعة الإسلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the presence of sin in Islamic history means the Sharia was not implemented.
Correction: The author argues that sins occurred because humans are fallible, not because Islamic rule was absent. Even the Companions sinned while the Sharia was fully applied.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why did sins occur under Islamic rule?
A) Because Islamic rule was not established.
B) Because people are not infallible.
C) Because the Sharia was not implemented.
D) Because the rulers were oppressive.

Key Takeaway
Sins under Islamic rule are due to human imperfection, not the failure of the Islamic system.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own sins, do you tend to excuse them by blaming your environment or upbringing, rather than admitting your own fallibility? How does this lesson's reminder that even the Companions sinned challenge you to take full responsibility?
?
If you were caught committing a sin publicly, would you accept the prescribed punishment with humility like the Companions did, or would you try to hide or justify it? What does your answer reveal about your trust in Allah's justice and the Sharia?
?
The passage mentions sins committed 'under the cover of darkness and in the secret of concealment.' What sin are you currently hiding from others? Knowing that human fallibility is universal, will you today repent sincerely and seek Allah's forgiveness?

The Fitna Between Ali and Muawiyah: Authentic vs Orientalist Accounts
Author exhorts reader to compare fitna accounts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how authentic Islamic historical sources differ from orientalist accounts in narrating the conflict between Ali and Muawiyah and the murder of Uthman.

Core Idea
Authentic sources honor the Sahaba; orientalist accounts slander them.

The author challenges us to compare accounts of early Islamic conflicts. He urges readers to examine original Arabic histories and then contrast them with orientalist versions. This lesson focuses on the fitna between Ali and Muawiyah and the murder of Uthman, highlighting the stark differences between authentic narratives and biased distortions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the fitna
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the two sources
The passage mentions two types of sources: authentic Arabic history books and accounts written by orientalists and Europeans. Note the contrast the author sets up.
The author uses the phrase 'astonishing contradiction and amazing slander' to describe the difference.
3
Reflect on the rhetorical question
Ask yourself: Why does the author use the metaphor of the owner versus the thief? What does this imply about the reliability of each source?
This connects to the core idea of the lesson.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اقرأ أخبار الفتنة بين علي ومعاوية رضي الله عنهما وما يتعلق بمقتل عثمان رضي الله عنه في كتب التاريخ العربية الأصيلة ، ثم عد فاقرأ هذه الأخبار كما صاغها وكتبها المستشرقون والأوربيون لترى التناقض المذهل ، والافتراء العجيب . واقرأ ترجمة هارون الرشيد في الطبري والمسعودي وابن الأثير ، تجد نفسك أمام عابد متنسك ألَّى على نفسه أن يهب حياته كلها للجهاد في سبيل الله وإقامة دولة الله في الأرض ، يغزو عاماً ويحج عاماً يصلي في اليوم والليلة مائة ركعة مالم يعتل بعلة أو يكن مشغولاً بغزو لا يقطع بأمر في مسألة إلا بعد أن يلقى بها العلماء ويطمئن إلى حكم الله فيها ، وتجده مع كل هذا غير معصوم قد يجتهد فيخطئ ويغضب فيأثم ويعصي ثم يتوب . ثم اقرأ ترجمته في كتب هؤلاء الموظفين تجده رجلاً آخر : لا يستفيق من المجون واللهو ، يعيش بين دنان الخمر ، يظل متقلباً في حياة الترف والنعيم !... (۱) فأيهما نصدق ، صاحب الدار ومالكها ، أم السارق المتسلل إليها ؟ (1) لن تجد شيئاً من هذا كله في أي مصدر من المصادر التاريخية العربية الأصيلة . وإنما نجد عكس ذلك تماماً ومعذور كل العذر هؤلاء الأوربيون الذين يصورون حياة هارون الرشيد بهذه الصورة ، فهم ليسوا إلا أحفاداً لأولئك الرومان الذين جند الرشيد حياته كلها في سبيل سحق كيدهم وإخضاعهم لحكم الدولة الإسلامية ، وهم ليسوا إلا أحفاد مليكهم ( نقفور ) الذي أراد أن يتمرد على نفوذ الدولة الإسلامية وحكمها في عهده وأرسل إلى الرشيد يهدده ويتوعده ، فكتب إليه الرشيد : من هارون الرشيد أمير المؤمنين إلى نقفور كلب الروم، قرأت كتابك يا ابن الكافرة والجواب ما ترى لا ما تسمع ، ثم انطلق إليه في جيش جرار على طريق مفروشة بالثلوج مملوءة بالصقيع والأعاصير حتى أناخ بباب هرقلة ففتح وغنم وقاتل حتى خضع له نقفور وطلب منه الموادعة على خراج يؤديه كل عام. فلما رجع الرشيد ووصل إلى الرقة نقض نقفور العهد وخان الميثاق يائساً من رجعة الرشيد إليه ! إذ كان البرد شديداً والثلوج تهمى على طول الطريق ، ووصل الخبر إلى الجند فكتموه عن الرشيد إشفاقاً عليه وعلى أنفسهم ولكنه ما لبث أن علم الحبر _
Read the reports of the conflict between Ali and Muawiyah, may Allah be pleased with them, and what relates to the murder of Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, in the authentic Arabic history books, then go back and read these reports as the orientalists and Europeans formulated and wrote them, to see the astonishing contradiction and the amazing slander. And read the biography of Harun al-Rashid in al-Tabari, al-Mas'udi, and Ibn al-Athir, you will find yourself before a devout worshiper who bound himself to devote his entire life to jihad in the way of Allah and the establishment of the state of Allah on earth, campaigning one year and performing Hajj another year, praying one hundred rak'ahs day and night unless he had an excuse or was busy with a campaign, not deciding a matter in any issue except after presenting it to the scholars and being reassured of Allah's judgment in it, and you find him with all of this not infallible—he may exert effort and err, become angry and sin, disobey, and then repent. Then read his biography in the books of these employed [orientalists] you will find another man: not coming to his senses from debauchery and frivolity, living among wine casks, constantly turning in a life of luxury and bliss!... So which of the two do we believe, the owner of the house and its possessor, or the thief sneaking into it? (1) You will not find any of this at all in any authentic Arabic historical source. Rather, we find the complete opposite, and these Europeans who depict the life of Harun al-Rashid in this way are completely excused, for they are nothing but descendants of those Romans whom al-Rashid devoted his entire life to crushing their cunning and subduing them to the rule of the Islamic state, and they are nothing but descendants of their king (Nikephoros) who wanted to rebel against the influence and rule of the Islamic state in his era and sent to al-Rashid threatening and warning him, so al-Rashid wrote to him: 'From Harun al-Rashid, Commander of the Faithful, to Nikephoros, dog of the Romans. I have read your letter, O son of the unbelieving woman, and the answer is what you see, not what you hear.' Then he set out against him with a massive army on a road paved with snow, filled with frost and storms, until he encamped at the gate of Heraclea, conquered, took spoils, and fought until Nikephoros submitted to him and asked for a truce on a tribute he would pay every year. When al-Rashid returned and reached al-Raqqah, Nikephoros broke the covenant and betrayed the pact, despairing of al-Rashid's return to him! For the cold was severe and snow was falling all along the road, and the news reached the soldiers, so they concealed it from al-Rashid out of compassion for him and themselves, but he soon learned the news...
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage provides two concrete examples to illustrate the contrast between authentic Islamic historical sources and orientalist fabrications. First, the author cites the conflict between Ali and Muawiyah and the murder of Uthman, urging the reader to compare accounts from authentic Arabic sources with those written by orientalists to see the stunning contradiction and slander. Second, he presents the biography of Harun al-Rashid: in the authentic sources (al-Tabari, al-Mas'udi, Ibn al-Athir), Harun is portrayed as a devout worshiper, dedicated to jihad and pilgrimage, praying extensively, consulting scholars, yet still human and capable of error and repentance. In contrast, orientalist accounts depict him as a debauched drunkard living in luxury. The author then poses a rhetorical question: whom should we believe—the owner of the house or the thief? A lengthy footnote elaborates that such fabrications are not found in authentic Arabic sources, and that the Europeans are descendants of the Romans whom Harun fought against, specifically King Nikephoros, who broke a treaty after Harun's campaign. The footnote recounts Harun's campaign against Nikephoros, including the famous letter and the betrayal after Harun's return, showing the hostility that motivated the distortions.

Key Terms
الفتنة
علي
معاوية
عثمان
المستشرقون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Orientalist accounts of the fitna are objective and based on the same sources as Islamic histories.
Correction: The author claims that orientalist accounts contain deliberate slander and contradiction when compared to authentic Arabic sources, indicating bias.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what will you find when you compare authentic Arabic sources and orientalist accounts of the fitna?
A) They are identical.
B) A few differences.
C) An astonishing contradiction and slander.
D) The same overall narrative.

Key Takeaway
Authentic Islamic sources provide a reliable account of the fitna, whereas orientalist narratives are corrupted by bias.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a historical narrative about the Sahaba without verifying its source? Consider your knowledge of the fitna. Do you know which sources you have relied on? Will you now commit to seeking authentic accounts from trusted Islamic references?
?
The author contrasts 'the owner of the house' with 'the thief'. In your own study of Islamic history, are you allowing outsiders to define the narrative? How can you ensure that your understanding comes from within the tradition? What one step will you take this week to read from an authentic Arabic source?
?
If someone slanders a Companion you love, how does your heart react? Does it reflect the honor you owe them? This lesson warns against distorted accounts. Will you actively defend their honor by seeking truth and correcting falsehoods when you hear them?
